أنواع الأداء الثلاثة

فقدمت إليه تمراً وكان القِدْرُ يغلي من اللحم، فقال عليه ألا تجعلين لنا نصيبا من اللحم، فقالت: يا رسول الله إنه لحم تصدق علي، فقال علي: "لكِ صدقة ولنا هدية" يعني إذا من المالك كان صدقة عليك، وإذا أعطيته إيانا تصير هدية لنا، فعلم أن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدلاً في العين وعلى هذا يخرج كثير من المسائل.

حتى تجبر على القبول تفريع على كونه أداء أي تجبر المرأة على قبول ذلك العبد الممهور بعد التسليم، وهو من علامة كونه أداءً، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا باع عبدا واستحق العبد، ثم اشتراه البائع من المستحق حيث لا يجبر على تسليمه إلى المشتري؛ لأنه بالاستحقاق ظهر أن البيع كان موقوفا على إجازة المالك، فإذا لم يجزه بطل وانفسخ، بخلاف النكاح، فإنه لا ينفسخ باستحقاق المهر ولا بانعدامه.

كثير من المسائل منها: أن الفقير إذا أخذ زكاة ثم وهبها لغني أو هاشمي أو باع منهما حل ذلك المال لهما؛ لتبدل العين بتبدل الملك. ومنها: أن رجلاً إذا تصدق على قريبه فمات المتصدق عليه وعادت الصدقة إليه بالوراثة ملكها وما ضاع ثوابه.

وهذا بخلاف إلخ: هذا دفع دخل مقدر تقريره موقوف على مقدمة ممهدة، وهي: أن يعلم أولاً أن المرأة كما تجبر في الصورة المذكورة على القبول كذلك الزوج يجبر على تسليمه إذا طلبته المرأة؛ لكونه عين حقها مع قيام موجب التسليم وهو النكاح، وإذا علمت هذا فاعلم أنه يرد عليه أن العبد الممهور المذكور نظيره العبد المبيع إذا باعه واستحق، ثم اشتراه البائع من المستحق، فينبغي أن يكون حكمه أيضًا مثل حكم العبد الممهور أي ليجبر البائع على تسليمه إلى المشتري إذا طلبه وليس الحكم كذلك، فأجاب: بأن قياسه على العبد الممهور لا يليق؛ فإنه ههنا المانع عن الإخبار موجود، وهو انفساخ البيع بظهور الاستحقاق وليس موجود في النكاح، فإنه لا ينفسخ باستحقاق المهر.

واستحق إلخ: أي تقرر للعبد مالك آخر. بطل وانفسخ أي البيع، فبعد بطلان البيع لا وجه للجبر على البائع بتسليمه إلى المشتري.

أخرجه البخاري في "صحيحه" رقم: ٤۸۰۹، باب الحرمة تحت العبد، ومسلم، رقم: ١٥٠٤، باب إنما الولاء لمن أعتق، وابن حبان في "صحيحه" رقم ۵۱۱٦ ٥۱۸/۱۱، وابن ماجه في "سننه" رقم ۲۰٧٦، باب خيار الأمة إذا أعتقته، والنسائي رقم: ٣٤٤٧، باب خيار الأمة، وأحمد في "مسنده" رقم: ۲٤۸۸۳، عن عائشة بألفاظ متقاربة المعنى.

بيان أنواع القضاء وينفذ إعتاقه فيه دون إعتاقها، تفريع على كونه شبيها بالقضاء يُعنى ينفذ إعتاق الزوج إياه قبل تسليمه إلى المرأة؛ لأن المرأة لا تملكه إلا إذا سلم إليها، فقبل التسليم هو ملك الزوج كما أن قبل الشراء كان ملكًا للغير.

ولما كانت ذات العبد موجودة في كلا الحالين ووصف المملوكية متغير فيهما جعل أداء شبيها بالقضاء، ولم يجعل قضاء شبيها بالأداء رعاية لجانب الذات والأصل.

بيان أنواع القضاء: ولما فرغ عن بيان أنواع الأداء شرع في تقسيم القضاء، فقال: والقضاء أنواع أيضًا بمثل معقول، وبمثل غير معقول، وما هو في معنى الأداء، وفي هذا التقسيم أيضًا مسامحة، وكأنه قيل: والقضاء أنواع: قضاء محض وهو إما بمثل معقول أو بمثل غير معقول، وقضاء في معنى الأداء، ويُعنى بالقضاء المحض ما لا يكون فيه معنى الأداء أصلاً لا حقيقةً ولا حكمًا، وينفذ إعتاقه وكذا كل تصرف من الكتابة والبيع والهبة وغير ذلك ولو قال: وينفذ تصرفاته قبل تسليمه دونها لكان أولى؛ إذ لا فرق بين العتق والكتابة والبيع والهبة وغيرها.

لأن المرأة: إيماء إلى أن نفوذ إعتاق الزوج دون إعتاق المرأة ليس متفرعًا على جهة القضاء بالذات كما يوهمه ظاهر عبارة المصنف بل بواسطة عدم ثبوت الملك لها كذا قيل. هو ملك الزوج فهي تصرفات صادفت ملك نفسه.

ولما كانت إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر وهو: أنه لم سمي أداء شبيهًا بالقضاء و لم يسم قضاء شبيها بالأداء.

ولما كانت إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر تقريره مذكور في "قمر الأقمار" فانظر هناك، واعلم أن الشارح ترك ثمرة كون العبد مثل المسمى لا عينه، وهي أن القاضي لو قضى في الصورة المذكورة على الزوج بقيمة العبد للزوجة، ثم ملك الزوج العبد ثانيًا لا يعود حق المرأة في العين فلا يجبر الزوج على التسليم، ولا الزوجة على القبول؛ لأن حقها قد انتقل من العبد إلى القيمة بالقضاء، ولو كان له حكم المسمى بعينه لعاد حقها فيه إذا كان القضاء بقول الزوج مع اليمين.

في كلا الحالين أي حال العقد وحال التسليم. لجانب الذات أي ذات العبد فإنها تقتضي كونه أداء المحشي: أيضًا أي كما في تقسيم الأداء.
Section on al-Khass. The three types of performance. She brought dates to him while the pot was boiling with meat, and he [the Prophet] said: 'Do you not give us a share of the meat?' She said: 'O Messenger of Allah, it is meat given as charity to me.' Ali said: 'It is charity for you and a gift for us.' Meaning that if it was from the owner it was charity for you, and if you give it to us it becomes a gift for us. Thus it is known that change of ownership necessitates a change in the object, and many issues derive from this. The compulsion to accept is a branch of it being performance, i.e., the woman is compelled to accept that slave given as mahr after delivery, and this is a sign of it being performance. This differs from the case of selling a slave and the slave being claimed, then the seller buys it back from the claimant, where he is not compelled to deliver it to the buyer; because upon the claim it appears that the sale was suspended on the owner's permission, and if he does not permit it, the sale becomes void and annulled. This is contrary to marriage, which is not annulled by the claim of the mahr nor by its loss. Many issues include: a poor person who takes zakat then gifts it to a rich person or a Hashimite, or sells it to them, that wealth becomes permissible for them due to the change of object with change of ownership. And a man who gives charity to his relative, then the recipient dies and the charity returns to him through inheritance, he owns it and his reward is not lost. 'And this differs...' is a repulsion of an expected objection whose establishment depends on a preliminary: first know that just as the woman is compelled to accept in the mentioned scenario, similarly the husband is compelled to deliver it if the woman requests it, because it is the very object of her right with the existence of the cause of delivery which is marriage. Knowing this, it is objected that the slave given as mahr is analogous to the sold slave if he sold it and it was claimed, then the seller bought it from the claimant, so its ruling should also be like the slave given as mahr, i.e., the seller should be compelled to deliver it to the buyer if he requests it, but the ruling is not so. He answered that the analogy to the slave given as mahr is not suitable; because here the preventing factor from compulsion exists, which is the annulment of the sale upon the appearance of the claim, and it does not exist in marriage, for marriage is not annulled by the claim of the mahr. 'And it was claimed...' meaning another owner was established for the slave. 'Became void and annulled' meaning the sale, so after the voidance of the sale there is no face for compulsion on the seller to deliver it to the buyer. Reported by Bukhari... Explanation of the types of judicial award: And his manumission is executed in it without her manumission, as a branch of it being similar to qada', meaning the manumission of the husband of him is executed before delivery to the woman, because the woman does not own him except when delivered to her, so before delivery he is the property of the husband. And since the essence of the slave exists in both states and the attribute of being owned changes in them, it was made performance resembling qada', and not made qada' resembling performance, out of consideration for the essence and the origin. Explanation of the types of qada': When he finished explaining the types of performance, he began dividing qada', saying: Judicial awards are also of types: by a tangible equivalent, by an intangible equivalent, and what is in the sense of performance. In this division there is also ease, as if it was said: Judicial awards are types: pure qada' which is either by a tangible equivalent or by an intangible equivalent, and qada' in the sense of performance. By pure qada' is meant that in which there is no meaning of performance at all, neither in reality nor in ruling. And his manumission is executed, and likewise every disposition like kitaba, sale, gift, etc. It would be better if he said: And his dispositions are executed before delivery without hers, as there is no difference between manumission and kitaba, sale, gift, etc. 'Because the woman' is a hint that the validity of the husband's manumission without the woman's manumission is not a branch of the essence of qada', as the apparent wording of the author might suggest, but rather due to the non-establishment of ownership for her. He is the property of the husband, so these dispositions strike his own property. 'And since...' is the answer to an estimated question: Why was performance called resembling qada' and not qada' called resembling performance? And know that the commentator left out the fruit of the slave being like the named [object] not its very self, which is that if the judge in the mentioned scenario gave judgment against the husband for the value of the slave for the wife, then the husband owned the slave a second time, the woman's right does not return in the object, so the husband is not compelled to deliver nor the woman compelled to accept, because her right has transferred from the slave to the value by the judgment. Whereas if it had the ruling of the named object itself, her right would return in it. 'In both states' i.e., the state of contract and the state of delivery. 'For the consideration of the essence' i.e., the essence of the slave, for it necessitates it being performance. The commentator: 'also' i.e., as in the division of performance.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar's commentary begins by examining a hadith about Ali and Fatima (may Allah be pleased with them) involving meat given as charity. The key legal principle extracted is that a change in ownership transforms the legal identity of an object (تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين). The commentator then applies this principle to several fiqh issues. First, in the case of a slave given as mahr, the wife is compelled to accept it after delivery because it is considered performance (ada') of the mahr. This contrasts with a sale where a sold slave is later reclaimed; the seller who reacquires the slave is not compelled to deliver it because the sale contract is voided by the claim. The principle is further illustrated with zakat and charity: a poor person who receives zakat and then gifts or sells it to a rich person or Hashimite renders it permissible for them due to ownership change. Similarly, if charity returns to the donor through inheritance, he owns it legitimately. The commentary then addresses a potential objection comparing the mahr slave to a sold slave, clarifying that in marriage the contract remains valid despite mahr issues, while a sale becomes void upon claim. Finally, the discussion moves to the classification of judicial awards (qada'), dividing them into pure qada' (by tangible or intangible equivalent) and qada' in the sense of performance. The classification of the mahr slave as 'performance resembling qada'' is justified by the persistence of the slave's essence despite changes in ownership status. A practical consequence is that only the husband's manumission of the slave before delivery is valid, not the wife's, since she does not yet own it.

Key Terms
تبدل الملك (tabaddul al-milk): Change of ownership from one person to another, which, according to the text, necessitates a change in the legal identity of the object (تبدل العين).
أداء (ada'): Performance of an obligation by delivering the exact specified object (عين) as agreed in the contract.
قضاء (qada'): Judicial award or fulfillment of an obligation by delivering a substitute (مثل) when the original is unavailable, either due to loss or legal impediment.
قضاء محض (qada' mahd): Pure qada' where there is no element of performance; the obligation is fulfilled by a substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the mahr slave considered 'ada' resembling qada'?
A) Because the slave is destroyed and cannot be delivered.
B) Because the slave's essence exists but ownership changes.
C) Because the wife refuses to accept the slave.
D) Because the husband manumits the slave before delivery.

Key Takeaway
Judicial awards (qada') are classified into pure qada' (substitute) and qada' in the sense of performance (essence retained), with the mahr slave as a key illustration.

The Hanafi Interpretation of the Hadith of Error and Forgetfulness
Debating the meaning of the hadith on error and forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school restricts the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' to the removal of sin only, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding intention in wudu.

Core Idea
The hadith lifts sin but not worldly legal effects; error (khata') involves negligence, so acts like fasting are invalidated.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the scope of the famous hadith. Both schools agree the hadith is authentic, but they differ on whether it removes only afterlife sin or also worldly legal consequences. The Hanafi position uses the principle that a literal interpretation leading to a false implication (kadhib) must be interpreted figuratively. Follow the steps to understand how this method resolves the seeming contradiction with other proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hadith and its Literal Meaning
Identify the hadith text: 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان'. Its apparent meaning (zahir) is that error and forgetfulness are lifted from the ummah.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut.
2
Identify the Impossible Implication
The literal reading implies that error and forgetfulness are attributes of the ummah themselves, which is false (kadhib). Since the Prophet cannot utter falsehood, the literal meaning cannot be intended.
Hanafi usul: if the zahir leads to a false implication, it must be interpreted figuratively (majaz).
3
Apply Hanafi Principle of Majaz
Interpret 'رفع' metaphorically as lifting the sin (ithm) in the Hereafter, not the worldly legal effects. This avoids the false implication.
This is an example of ta'wil based on qarina (indication of impossibility).
4
Contrast with Shafi'i Interpretation
Al-Shafi'i uses the hadith to argue that intention is not required in wudu, implying the hadith removes all worldly requirements. The Hanafi response: the hadith cannot override explicit texts that establish the need for intention in other acts.
Al-Shafi'i's position is based on a broader application of the hadith.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis hold wudu is valid without intention (but recommended), while Shafi'is require intention. Also, eating mistakenly in fasting invalidates the fast (Hanafi) due to negligence, but forgetfulness does not.
This is the outcome of the usul difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يدل على أن جواز العمل موقوف على النية، فلا تكون النية فرضًا في الوضوء على ما قال الشافعي له، وأما في سائر العبادات المحضة، فالمقصود فيها الثواب، فإذا خلت عن الثواب بدون النية فات الجواز أيضًا بهذه الوتيرة لا بأن النص دال على فوت الجواز. وقوله عليه: ورفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان، فإن ظاهره يدل على أن الخطاء والنسيان أمته، وهو كذب باطل، فيحمل على أن حكمه في الآخرة أعني المآثم مرفوع، وأما في الدنيا فغرمه باقٍ في حقوق العباد ألبتة، وكذا في فساد الصوم بالأكل خطاء، في الوضوء وكذا في الغسل، وتطهير الثياب وغيرهما. وأما في سائر العبادات المحضة كالصلاة والصوم إذا خلت عن النية بطلت فصحتها منوطة على النية، فصار معنى الحديث أن صحة الأعمال بالنيات. ولا يصح قياس الأكل خطاء في الصوم على الأكل ناسيا في نهار رمضان؛ فإن العذر حالة النسيان قوي لا جناية فيه أصلاً، وأما الخطاء فلا يخلو عن جناية عدم الاحتياط والتثبت. وأما في صورة النسيان كما إذا أكل ناسيا، فلا ينتقض به الصوم ولا إثم أيضًا؛ لما روى الشيخان عن أبي هريرة عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم "من نسي وهو صائم فأكل وشرب فيتم صومه، فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه الله".
Thus it does not indicate that the validity of action is dependent on intention, so intention is not obligatory in wudu as al-Shafi'i said. As for other purely devotional acts, their purpose is reward; if they lack reward without intention, validity is also lost in this manner, not because the text indicates loss of validity. And His statement (peace be upon him): 'And lifted from my nation error and forgetfulness' — its apparent meaning indicates that error and forgetfulness are from my nation, which is a false lie. So it is interpreted to mean that its ruling in the Hereafter, that is, sin, is lifted. But in this world, compensation remains in the rights of other people absolutely, and likewise in the invalidation of fasting by eating mistakenly, in wudu, likewise in ghusl, and purification of garments and others. As for purely devotional acts like prayer and fasting, if they lack intention, they become invalid; their validity depends on intention, so the meaning of the hadith becomes 'the validity of deeds is by intentions.' And it is not correct to analogize eating mistakenly in fasting to eating forgetfully during Ramadan daytime; for the excuse of forgetfulness is strong, with no offense at all, while error is not free from the offense of lack of caution. As for the case of forgetfulness, if one eats forgetfully, fasting is not nullified and there is no sin either, because the two shaykhs narrated from Abu Huraira from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Whoever forgets while fasting and eats or drinks should complete his fast, for Allah has fed him and given him drink.'
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a debate with al-Shafi'i over the interpretation of the hadith 'Rufi'a 'an ummati al-khata' wa al-nisyan.' The Hanafi position is that the hadith only removes sin in the afterlife; worldly rulings such as compensation (ghurm) in financial rights and invalidation of acts like fasting by eating mistakenly remain. al-Shafi'i uses the hadith to argue that intention is not obligatory in wudu, but the Hanafi response shows that hadith cannot be used that way because it does not negate worldly legal effects. The text also distinguishes between error (khata') and forgetfulness (nisyan): forgetfulness fully excuses, whereas error still involves some negligence, so acts like fasting and prayer are invalidated by error (e.g., eating mistakenly or speaking mistakenly in prayer).

Key Terms
الخطأ (al-khata'): Act done unintentionally with some negligence or lack of caution, as opposed to forgetfulness (nisyan). Legal consequences remain for worldly rulings.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness, a complete excuse where there is no offense; acts done out of forgetfulness do not nullify fasting according to the hadith.
الوتيرة (al-watira): The manner or path of leaving the literal meaning (haqiqah) and adopting metaphor (majaz).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation, what does the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' remove?
A) All worldly and afterlife consequences of error and forgetfulness
B) Only sin in the Hereafter
C) Only compensation in financial rights
D) Only invalidation of acts of worship

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of the hadith restricts removal to sin only; worldly rulings like compensation and invalidation remain for error (khata') but not for forgetfulness (nisyan).

The Conjunction Waw: Absolute Association without Order
Textual analysis and inter-madhhab dispute on the conjunction waw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the conjunction waw and explain how the hadith 'We begin with what Allah began with' is interpreted by the Hanafi school in the context of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The waw (و) is purely conjunctive; order comes from the Sunnah, not from the particle.

In legal interpretation, even a single particle can become the site of major madhhab dispute. This lesson examines the conjunction waw—does it imply order, simultaneity, or mere conjunction? The Hanafi school, following the majority of linguists, holds that waw indicates absolute association (mujarrad al-jam') without any added meaning. We will trace the Shafi'i counter-argument based on a hadith, and the Hanafi response that distinguishes between linguistic function and Prophetic command.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on waw
Identify what the Hanafi school claims about the conjunction waw: it is for absolute conjunction (mutlaq al-'atf) without indicating order (tartib) or simultaneity (muqarana). It merely shows partnership (shirka) in time or existence.
The text explicitly says: 'فالواو المطلق العطف من غير تعرض لمقارنة ولا ترتيب'.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Some Shafi'i scholars claim that waw implies order. Their proof is the hadith: 'نحن نبدأ بما بدأ الله به' (We begin with what Allah began with), narrated by al-Tirmidhi. They interpret the waw in the verse about Safa and Marwah as imposing order.
This hadith is cited by al-Shafi'i's supporters to argue that the waw itself requires starting with Safa.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith
The Hanafi response is that the hadith is a separate Prophetic command, not a linguistic interpretation of the waw. The waw remains purely conjunctive; the order is established by the Sunnah, not by the particle. The text says: 'والصحيح من مذهبه خلافه' – the correct view of the school is contrary.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between linguistic meaning (waw) and external proof (Sunnah).
4
Apply to the Sa'i ritual (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence: In Sa'i between Safa and Marwah, Hanafis permit starting with either hill, though the Sunnah is to start with Safa based on the Prophet's command. Shafi'is require starting with Safa based on the alleged order implied by waw.
This illustrates how a subtle linguistic point can affect actual practice.
5
Confirm the method of textual analysis
Recognize that this dispute demonstrates a core Hanafi usul principle: particles are interpreted according to their linguistically established meanings, not imported from external evidence. The Hanafi approach relies on the consensus of linguists and grammarians.
The text says: 'لمطلق العطف هذا عند عامة أهل اللغة والنحاة' – this is according to the generality of linguists and grammarians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحث الواو] وقال: فالواو المطلق العطف من غير تعرض لمقارنة ولا ترتيب يعني أن الواو لمطلق معية في الزمان الشركة، فإن كان في عطف المفرد على المفرد فالشركة ثابتة في المحكوم عليه أو به وإن كان في عطف الجمل، فالشركة في مجرد الثبوت والوجود، وبالجملة هو لا يتعرض للمقارنة كما زعمه بعض أصحابنا، ولا للترتيب كما زعمه بعض أصحاب الشافعي ، فإذا قيل "جاءني زيد وعمرو" يحتمل أنهما جاءاك معا، أو تقدم أحدهما على الاخر . والصحيح من مذهبه خلافه وحجّة الشافعي قوله عليه: "نحن نبدأ بما بدأ الله ..... . لمطلق العطف هذا عند عامة أهل اللغة والنحاة وإنما قدم الواو على الحروف الأخر العاطفة؛ لأنها كالبسيطة بالنسبة إليها، فإن معناها أصل كالجزء من معاني سائر الحروف العاطفة؛ لأن الواو تدل على المشاركة وسائر الحروف العاطفة عليه مع زيادة كالترتيب وغيره.(القمر) ولا ترتيب: أي تأخر ما بعد الواو عما قبلها في الزمان. (القمر) للمقارنة إلخ : أي الاجتماع في الزمان كما نقل عن مالك له، ونسب إلى محمد وأبي يوسف رحمها، وقوله ولا للترتيب أي تأخر ما بعدها لما قبلها في الزمان كما نقل عن الشافعي ونسب إلى أبي حنيفة . (القمر) كما قوله عليه : حين سأل الصحابة من السعي بين الصفا والمروة (المحشي) نحن نبدأ إلخ روى الترمذي عن جابر بن عبد الله قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: نبدأ بما بدأ الله به، وقرأ أيضًا ﴿إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ﴾ (البقرة : ١٥٨)
Discussion of waw: He said: The waw is for absolute conjunction without indicating simultaneity or order, meaning that waw is for absolute association in time of partnership. If it is in the conjunction of a single word upon a single word, then the partnership is established in the subject or object; and if it is in the conjunction of sentences, then the partnership is in mere affirmation and existence. In summary, it does not indicate simultaneity as claimed by some of our companions, nor order as claimed by some of al-Shafi'i's companions. When one says 'Zaid and Amr came to me,' it is possible that they both came together or that one preceded the other. And the correct view of his school is otherwise. Al-Shafi'i's proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'We begin with what Allah began with...' (the hadith is incomplete). For absolute conjunction – this is according to the generality of linguists and grammarians. He only gave precedence to waw over the other conjunctive letters because it is like the simple one in relation to them, for its meaning is a root like a part of the meanings of the other conjunctive letters, because waw indicates participation and the other conjunctive letters [indicate] that plus an increase like order and so forth. (al-Qamar) And no order: i.e., the delay of what is after waw compared to what is before it in time. (al-Qamar) So the partnership: i.e., between the conjoined and what it is conjoined to. (al-Qamar) In the subject: like 'Zaid stood and sat.' (al-Qamar) Or object: like 'Zaid and Amr stood.' (al-Qamar) In conjunction of sentences: like 'Zaid stood and Amr sat.' (al-Qamar) So the partnership: i.e., between the conjoined and what it is conjoined to. (al-Qamar) For simultaneity etc.: i.e., togetherness in time as related from Malik, and attributed to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), and his saying 'and not order' i.e., the delay of what comes after it compared to what comes before it in time as related from al-Shafi'i and attributed to Abu Hanifa. (al-Sanbali) Some of al-Shafi'i's companions claimed that, and that is also reported from al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar) As his saying (peace be upon him): when the Companions asked about the Sa'i between Safa and Marwa (al-Muhashi) 'We begin with what Allah began with' – al-Tirmidhi narrated from Jabir ibn Abdullah who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'We begin with what Allah began with,' and he recited also: 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah' (al-Baqarah: 158).
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the conjunction waw (و) in Arabic grammar as used in legal texts, specifically addressing whether it implies order (tartib) or simultaneity (muqarana). The author states that waw is for absolute conjunction (mujarrad al-jam') without any indication of order or simultaneity. This is the position of the majority of linguists and grammarians. Some Hanafi scholars claimed that waw indicates simultaneity, and some Shafi'i scholars claimed it indicates order. The author rejects both, asserting that waw simply joins without any extra meaning. The Shafi'i proof is a hadith: 'We begin with what Allah began with,' referring to the verse about Safa and Marwah. The Hanafi response, implicit in the commentary, is that this hadith is a separate command to start with what Allah started, not a linguistic proof that waw itself implies order. The waw in the verse is purely conjunctive. The correct Hanafi view is that waw indicates absolute partnership in time or existence, and the order in the rituals is derived from the Prophet's practice, not from the conjunction. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it is the relied-upon view of the school.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The conjunction waw that indicates absolute association (mujarrad al-jam') without any implication of order or simultaneity.
مطلق العطف (mutlaq al-'atf): Absolute conjunction – the basic joining function of waw without any extra meaning like order or togetherness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It indicates absolute conjunction without order or simultaneity.

Key Takeaway
The conjunction waw (و) indicates absolute conjunction without order or simultaneity; any order in rituals is proven from the Sunnah, not from the particle.

Interpreting 'Thumma' in the Oath Expiation Hadith: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Addressing an objection from Shafi'i regarding the order of expiation and oath-breaking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of preferring metaphor in the particle over metaphor in the command to resolve apparent contradictions in hadith.

Core Idea
When literal reading of a particle contradicts a certain legal principle, the particle is interpreted figuratively to preserve the principle.

Imam al-Shafi'i relied on the literal word 'thumma' (then) in a hadith to argue that expiation can precede breaking an oath. The Hanafi school counters that such a reading conflicts with the established legal reality that expiation is only obligatory after the oath is broken. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting narrations by interpreting 'thumma' metaphorically as simple conjunction (wa), thereby preserving the literal meaning of the command and upholding legal principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i claim and its textual basis
Locate the hadith cited by al-Shafi'i: 'فليكفر عن يمينه ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير'. Note that the word 'ثم' appears after the command to expiate, suggesting order.
2
Recognize the Hanafi objection
Understand that a literal reading of 'thumma' would require expiation before the oath is broken, which is impossible because expiation is a consequence of breaking the oath. This conflicts with the legal principle (and consensus) that expiation is only obligatory after hanth.
3
Analyze the Hanafi hermeneutic move
The Hanafis interpret 'thumma' as metaphorical for 'wa' (and). This preserves the literal meaning of the imperative 'ليكفر' (let him expiate) as an obligation, while avoiding the impossible order. The principle invoked: 'metaphor in the particle is preferable to metaphor in the verb' because the imperative is unequivocal in indicating obligation.
The other narration (without 'thumma' or with reversed order) supports this reconciliation.
4
Reconcile the two narrations
The first narration (with 'thumma') is taken to indicate the general obligation of both expiation and breaking the oath without order. The second narration (where breaking the oath comes first) provides the actual order. Thus, the correct sequence is: break the oath, then expiate.
5
State the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the Hanafi school, one cannot expiate before breaking the oath; any pre-emptive expiation is invalid. According to the Shafi'i school, it is permissible. This difference affects how a mufti advises someone who has not yet broken an oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواب سؤال مقدر، وهو: أن الشافعي حاله يقول بجواز تقديم الكفارة بالمال على الحنث؛ لأنه عليه قال: 'من حلف على يمين فرأى غيرها خيراً منها، فليكفر عن يمينه، ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير' فإتيان الخير كناية عن الحنث، وذكرها بلفظ 'ثم' بعد التكفير، فعلم أن تقديم الكفارة على الحنث جائز، فأجاب المصنف له أن لفظ 'ثم' في هذا الحديث استعير بمعنى الواو عملاً بحقيقة الأمر تدل عليه الرواية الأخرى، وهي قوله عليه: 'فليأت بالذي هو ثم ليكفر عن يمينه' فإنه يقتضي تقديم الحنث على الكفارة، فوجب التطبيق بينهما بأن يجعل 'ثم' في الرواية الأولى بمعنى الواو، فيفهم منه وجوب كلا الأمرين أعني الكفارة والحنث من غير تقديم أحدهما على الأخر، ثم يفهم الترتيب وهو تقديم الحنث على الكفارة من الرواية الأخرى. وبهذا البيان انحل عبارة المتن وما أورد الشارح ذيل قول المتن الرواية الأخرى وهي قوله عليه: فليأت إلخ، لم أجده في كتب الحديث الحاضرة وقال ابن الهمام: إن هذا اللفظ غير معروف كذا في الصبح الصادق، وبناء عليه احتاج الشارح إلى التطبيق بين الروايتين قال ما قال وانحر الكلام بالتطويل بل إلى الملال. (القمر) مر تخريجه .
And an answer to an implied question: that al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) holds the permissibility of offering the financial expiation before breaking the oath, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears an oath and sees something better than it, let him expiate for his oath, then let him do that which is better.' Doing that which is better is a metaphor for breaking the oath, and he mentioned it with the word 'thumma' after expiation, so it is known that offering expiation before breaking the oath is permissible. The author answered him that the word 'thumma' in this hadith is used metaphorically in the sense of 'wa' (and) in order to act according to the literal meaning of the command, as indicated by the other narration, which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Let him do that which is better, then let him expiate for his oath.' This requires giving priority to breaking the oath over expiation. So it became necessary to reconcile between them by making 'thumma' in the first narration mean 'wa', so that it is understood from it the obligation of both actions, i.e., expiation and breaking the oath, without prioritizing one over the other. Then the order, i.e., prioritizing breaking the oath over expiation, is understood from the other narration. With this explanation, the phrase of the text is resolved. And what the commentator mentioned at the end of the text's statement 'the other narration, which is his saying: let him do etc.' — I did not find it in the current books of hadith. Ibn al-Humam said: This wording is unknown, as in al-Subh al-Sadiq. Consequently, the commentator needed to reconcile between the two narrations, and he said what he said, dragging the speech at length even to boredom. (al-Qamar) Its takhrij has passed.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage addresses a cross-madhhab dispute, specifically an objection from Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the permissibility of offering expiation (kaffarah) before breaking an oath (hanth). Al-Shafi'i cites a hadith where the Prophet said: 'Whoever swears an oath and sees something better, let him expiate his oath, then do that which is better.' The phrase 'then do that which is better' refers to breaking the oath, and the word 'thumma' (then) indicates order, suggesting that expiation comes before breaking the oath, thus making it permissible to expiate in advance. The Hanafi response, given by the author (likely the commentator of Noorul Anwar), is that the word 'thumma' in this hadith is used metaphorically to mean 'wa' (and). This interpretation is necessitated by the fact that the command to perform expiation (فليكفر) is a legislative command (amr) that implies obligation (wujub). If 'thumma' were taken literally, it would imply that expiation is obligatory before breaking the oath, but that is not the case by scholarly consensus (ijma'). Expiation is only obligatory after the oath is broken, so the command cannot require expiation before the act. Therefore, 'thumma' must be interpreted figuratively as mere conjunction. This is supported by another version of the hadith found in al-Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) where the wording is '... let him expiate his oath and do that which is better' without 'thumma'. The Hanafis reconcile the two narrations by taking the first 'thumma' as 'wa' for general obligation, and the order (breaking the oath first) is derived from the second narration. The passage also notes a textual issue: the second narration as quoted (فليأت بالذي هو ثم ليكفر عن يمينه) is not found in the standard hadith collections, and Ibn al-Humam stated it is unknown. Nevertheless, the interpretation stands on the principle that the literal meaning of the command (amr) must be preserved, and metaphor in the particle (ثم) is preferable to metaphor in the verb (command).

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle indicating conjunction with order (then). In this context, Hanafis interpret it as equivalent to 'wa' (and) to preserve the literal meaning of the command.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for breaking a valid oath; it is obligatory only after the oath is broken.
حنث (hanth): Breaking an oath by doing the opposite of what was sworn to do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the word 'thumma' in the hadith interpreted as 'wa' (and)?
A) Because the hadith is weak and cannot be taken literally.
B) Because a literal reading would require expiation before the oath is broken, which is impossible and contradicts the legal reality.
C) Because the Shafi'i school also interprets it that way.
D) Because there is no other way to reconcile the two narrations.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a particle's literal meaning leads to an impossible or contradictory result, it is interpreted metaphorically to preserve the literal meaning of the verb, as demonstrated in the case of 'thumma' in the oath expiation hadith.

Iqtida' al-Nass: Definition and its Conflict with Dalala
Defines iqtida' al-nass and presents a conflict with dalala resolved by tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define iqtida' al-nass, distinguish it from dalala, and apply the Hanafi rule that dalala is preferred over iqtida' in case of conflict.

Core Idea
The implied requirement of a text (iqtida') is weaker than its clear indication (dalala) because dalala is linguistically universal.

In Hanafi usul, not all meanings derived from a text carry the same weight. This lesson introduces iqtida' al-nass—an implied requirement necessary for the text's validity—and shows how it differs from the clear indication (dalala). Using a well-known hadith about washing impurities, we will see why Hanafi scholars give precedence to dalala over iqtida'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of textual meaning
From the passage, extract the definitions of dalala (clear indication) and iqtida' (implied requirement). Note that both derive from the same text but through different mechanisms: dalala is based on common linguistic understanding, while iqtida' is necessary for the text's coherence.
See the key terms for formal definitions.
2
Analyze the hadith example
The hadith 'scratch it, then rub it with water' explicitly mentions water. By iqtida', this implies that only water suffices. However, the common understanding (dalala) of the command is purification, which can be achieved with any liquid. Trace this reasoning in the source text.
The hadith is cited from Bukhari and Tirmidhi.
3
Apply the tarjih rule
The author states clearly that when dalala and iqtida' conflict, dalala is preferred. The reason given is that dalala is established linguistically from all aspects, while iqtida' is established only for legal necessity. Confirm this by reading the commentary section.
The preference is based on the epistemological strength of linguistic common knowledge.
4
Distinguish iqtida' from ishara
The passage also compares iqtida' with ishara (allusion). Unlike ishara, the text's meaning depends on iqtida'; if iqtida' is invalid, the explicit wording becomes meaningless. Therefore, iqtida' is stronger than ishara, but both are weaker than dalala.
This ranking is unique to Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان اقتضاء النص
بيان أقسام التقسيم الرابع
القطعي إلّا أنّه يترجّح الدلالة على الاقتضاء عند المعارضة. :مثاله: قوله عليها لعائشة حتّيه ثمّ ،اقرصيه، ثمّ اغسليه بالماء"، فإنه يدلّ باقتضاء النص على أن لا يجوز غسل النّجس بغير الماء من المائعات؛ لأنه لما أوجب الغسل بالماء فيقتضي صحته أن لا يجوز بغير الماء، ولكنه بعينه يدلّ بدلالة النص على أنه يجوز غسله بالمائعات، وذلك ؛ لأنّ المعنى المأخوذ منه الذي يعرفه كلّ أحد هو التطهير، وذلك يحصل بهما جميعًا، ألا ترى أنّ من ألقى الثوب النجس لا يؤاخذ باستعمال الماء فيه؛ لأنّ في الماء المقصود وهو إزالة النجاسة حاصل على كل حال فترجّحت الدلالة على الاقتضاء.
أسماء
يترجح الدلالة إلخ لثبوت الدلالة بالمعنى لغةً فكان ثابتا من كل وجه. والمقتضى إنما يثبت به شرعًا للحاجة إلى إثبات الحكم؛ فكان ضروريًا، فصار ثابتا من وجه دون وجه كذا قيل. ولمّا كانت الإشارة مرجحة على الدلالة؛ فصارت مرجّحة على الاقتضاء أيضًا، كذا قالوا وفيه أنّ المقتضى يتوقف عليه مدلول النظم فببطلانه يبطل مدلول النظم، بخلاف الثابت بالإشارة فإنه ببطلانه لا يبطل مدلول النظم؛ فصار الثابت بالاقتضاء أولى من الثابت بالإشارة. (القمر) مثاله: أي مثال التعارض بين الدلالة والاقتضاء مع ترجيح الدلالة (القمر) حتيه إلخ: روى الترمذي عن ابنة أبي بكر الصديق لها، أن امرأة سألت النبي الثوب يصيبه الدّم من الحيضة؟ فقال رسول الله : حتيه، ثم اقرصيه بالماء ثم رشيه، وصلّي فيه "والحت: الحك"، حتيه أي حكيه. والقرص "الدلك بأطراف الأصابع والأظفار مع صب الماء عليه حتى ذهب أثره. وقال الخطابي : أصل القرص أن تقبض أصبعين على الشيء، ثمّ تغمزه غمرًا جيدًا. ورشيه أي صبي عليه الماء بالماء لأنه لو جاز بغير الماء لاكتفى بقوله: "فاغسليه" ولا حاجة إلى قوله : "بالماء" بل يكون حشوا. المحشي بهما : أي بالماء وبغيره من المائعات. (القمر)
عن
غريب بهذا اللفظ. كذا قال الزيلعي في شرح "الهداية". [إشراق الأبصار: ١٤] وأخرج البخاري في صحيحه رقم: ۳۰۱ باب غسل دم المحيض، عن رقم: ۳۰۱ باب غسل دم المحيض، عن أسماء بنت أبي بكر لها أنها قالت: سألت امرأة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت يا رسول الله ، أرأيت إحدانا إذا أصاب ثوبها الدم من الحيضة كيف تصنع؟ فقال رسول الله : إذا أصاب ثوب إحداكن الدّم من الحيضة فلتقرصه، ثم لتنضحه بماء، ثم لتصلي فيه. وأخرج الترمذي رقم: ۱۳۸ ، باب ما جاء في غسل دم الحيض من الثوب، عن أسماء بنت أبي بكر له أن امرأة سألت عن الثوب يصيبه الدم من الحيضة؟ فقال رسول الله حتيه، ثم اقرصيه بالماء، ثم رشيه، وصلّي فيه.
النبي
قال الترمذي حديث حسن صحيح.
Explanation of the requirement of the text. Explanation of the sections of the fourth division. ... Definitive, except that the indication (dalala) is preferred over the requirement (iqtida') when they conflict. Example: His statement about Aisha: "Scratch it, then rub it, then wash it with water." This indicates by requirement of the text that it is not permissible to wash impurity with other than water from liquids; because when he obligated washing with water, its correctness requires that it is not permissible with other than water. But the same text indicates by its indication that it is permissible to wash it with liquids, because the meaning taken from it known to everyone is purification, and that is achieved by both. Do you not see that one who throws the impure garment is not blamed for using water because the purpose—removal of impurity—is obtained in any case? So the indication prevailed over the requirement. ...
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage type is a definition and explanation of iqtida' al-nass (the implied requirement of a text). The author first states that when the clear indication (dalala) and the implied requirement (iqtida') conflict, the clear indication takes precedence. He then provides the example of the hadith about washing menstrual blood from a garment. The text explicitly commands washing with water, which by iqtida' implies that washing with other liquids is not allowed. However, the clear indication (dalala) of the text—based on the common understanding that the purpose is purification—shows that purification can be achieved with any liquid, so the command is not exclusive to water. Thus, dalala outweighs iqtida'. The commentary then discusses why dalala is stronger: it is established linguistically from all aspects, while iqtida' is established only for necessity. The author also compares iqtida' with ishara (allusion) and argues that iqtida' is stronger than ishara because the validity of the text depends on iqtida'. The hadith narrations from Bukhari and Tirmidhi are cited as evidence.

Key Terms
اقتضاء النص (iqtiḍāʾ al-naṣṣ): The implied requirement of a text: a meaning that is not explicitly stated but is necessary for the validity of the explicit wording.
دلالة النص (dalālat al-naṣṣ): The clear indication of the text based on the common understanding of its meaning (e.g., purification from the command to wash).
إشارة النص (ishārat al-naṣṣ): The allusion of the text: a meaning derived not from the wording but from the context, yet weaker than iqtida'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator prefer dalala over iqtida' in the example of washing impurity?
A) Because iqtida' is derived by qiyas, which is weak.
B) Because dalala is established linguistically and universally understood, while iqtida' is only for necessity.
C) Because the hadith is weak.
D) Because iqtida' leads to contradicting the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the clear indication (dalala) of a text takes precedence over its implied requirement (iqtida') because dalala is linguistically universal and independent of necessity.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Definition of Sunnah: Usul al-Fiqh Perspective and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Definition of Sunnah and dispute over its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sunnah according to Hanafi usul, state its ruling (matlub but not fard/wajib), and explain why the Hanafi school includes the practices of the Companions in the unqualified term 'Sunnah'.

Core Idea
Sunnah is a required path in religion—not fard, not wajib—and for Hanafis, it includes the Prophet's and the Companions' ways.

Welcome to this exploration of a foundational concept in usul al-fiqh: Sunnah. We will unpack the Hanafi definition, understand its unique ruling (matlub without being fard or wajib), and then dive into a classical dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over the scope of the term 'Sunnah' when used absolutely. This dispute has practical implications for how we derive rulings from the practices of the Companions. By the end, you will be able to articulate the Hanafi position and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Define Sunnah and identify its ruling
Read the definition: Sunnah is 'the path followed in the religion'. Its ruling is: a person is required to establish it (yutlabu bi iqamatiha) without it being fard or wajib. That means reward for doing, no punishment for leaving.
2
Distinguish between Sunnah al-Huda and Sunan al-Zawa'id
The given definition applies only to Sunnah al-Huda (guided practices). Sunan al-Zawa'id (habitual actions) are not required in the same way. This distinction is crucial for accurate application.
3
State the Hanafi position on the absolute term 'Sunnah'
When 'Sunnah' is used without qualification, Hanafis hold that it includes the ways of the Prophet and the Companions. The Shafi'i position restricts it to the Prophet alone.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proofs
Key proofs: (1) The hadith 'Man sanna sunnatan hasanatan...' where the general word 'man' indicates anyone. (2) The Prophet's command: 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.'
5
Compare the Shafi'i proofs and evaluate the response
Shafi'i relied on Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's usage and the principle that absolute terms refer to perfect individuals. The Hanafi response: absolute terms are unrestricted; context may specify but does not restrict inherently. The example of diyah (blood money) illustrates the practical difference.

فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
تعريف السنة وحكمها
والثالث: سنة، وهي الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين، وحكمها أن يطالب المرء بإقامتها من غير افتراض ولا وجوب فاحترز بقوله أن يطالب عن النفل، وبقوله: "من غير افتراض ولا وجوب" عن الفرض والواجب، وكان ينبغي أن يذكر هذه القيودات في التعريف، إلا أنه اكتفى عنها بالحكم، ولكن قالوا: إن هذا التعريف والحكم لا يصدقان إلا على سنة الهدى، والتقسيم الآتي إنما هو لمطلق السنة.
إلا أن السنة تقع على طريقة النبي عليه وغيره يعني الصحابة فيه، وهي الطريقة المسلوكة إلخ: أي سوى الفرض والواجب، والقرينة على هذا التقييد كون السنة مقابل الفرض والواجب، والمراد من الطريقة المسلوكة الطريقة الحسنة التي سلكها النبي والصحابة [؟] وتكون مطالبًا بها. (القمر) أن يُطالب إلخ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانْتَهُوا﴾ (الحشر: ٧) (القمر) من غير افتراض إلخ أي ليس مطالبتها مطالبة الفرض والواجب حتى يستحق تاركها العقاب. (القمر) هذه القيودات أي كونها مطالبًا بها، وكون مطالبتها غير مطالبة الفرض والواجب. (القمر) ولكن قالوا إلخ لما كان يتوهم من الكلام السابق أن التعريف المذكور والحكم المسطور لمطلق السنة دفعه الشارح بقوله: ولكن قالوا إلخ (القمر) إلا على سنة الهدى فإنها طريقة مسلوكة في الدين ومطالب بها، وأما سنن الزوائد فمسلوكة على وجه العادة لا العبادة. (القمر) والتقسيم الآتي إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن هذا التعريف والحكم لما لم يصدقا إلا على سنة الهدى فكيف يصح تقسيم هذه السنة فيما سيأتي إلى نوعين سنة الهدى وسنن الزوائد؟ وحاصل الدفع: أن التقسيم الآتي ليس تقسيما لهذه السنة، بل هو تقسيم لمطلق السنة، وإليه أشار الشارح له فيما سيأتي بقوله: لمطلق السنة إلخ. (القمر) لمطلق السنة إلخ سواء كانت سنة الهدى أو سنة زائدة (السنبلي) إلا أن السنة إلخ توضيحه أنه لا خلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي له في تعريف السنة وحكمها المذكورين، إنما الخلاف بيننا وبينه أن لفظ السنة إذا أطلق هل يطلق على طريقة غير النبي أو لا؟ الثاني مختاره، والأول مختارنا، ودليلنا: قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام "من سن سنة حسنة فله أجرها وأجر من عمل بها" فإن كلمة "من" تعمّ الناس. (القمر) وغيره إلخ أي لا خلاف في نفسها وحكمها، إنما الخلاف في إطلاقها، فعندنا يقع على طريقة النبي كما قال عليه السلام: "عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين". (السنبلي)
وغيره يقال: سنة أبي بكر وعمر وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين. وقال الشافعي بحله مطلقها طريقة النبي عليه السلام، يعني إذا يطلق لفظ السنة بلا قرينة لا يطلق على طريقة الصحابة كما روي أن سعيد بن المسيب رضي الله عنه قال: "ما دون الثلث من الدية لا ينصف وهو السنة"، أراد بها سنة النبي عليه السلام، وهي أن الدية إذا لم تبلغ ثلثا فالرجل والأنثى فيه سواء، وإذا بلغ الثلث فصاعدًا يؤخذ للمرأة نصف ما يؤخذ للرجل، وإذا أريدت سنة غير النبي عليه السلام يقال: هذه سنة الشيخين لهما أو سنة أبي بكر أو سنة أبي بكر له ونحوه.
يقال سنة أبي بكر إلخ ذكر هذا القول لا يفيد؛ فإن هذا القول مقيّد، والخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي له إنما هو في مطلق السنة كأن يقول الراوي من السنة كذا؛ فعنده على سنة النبي عليه السلام و عندنا لا يدل إلا على أنه طريقة مسلوكة في الدين أعم من أن يكون سنته أو سنة الصحابة منه (القمر) لا يطلق إلخ: لأن المطلق يتبادر منه الفرد الكامل، ونحن نقول: إن المطلق يفيد الإطلاق؛ فلا يتقيد بلا دليل وكمال الفرد ليس بدليل التقييد، فيقع على طريقة وغيره، وأما إرادة سنة النبي عليه السلام في قول سعيد بن المسيب رضي الله عنه فلعله باقتضاء المقام. كذا قيل، فتأمل. (القمر) فتأمل.(القمر)
النبي في لا يطلق على إلخ قلنا مطلقة فلا تُقيّد بلا دليل كذا في "الدائر". (السنبلي) سنة النبي عليه السلام وهذا ممنوع قال في "الكفاية": إنه أراد بها سنة زيد بن ثابت رضي الله عنه؛ فإنه إمام سعيد بن المسيب هذا القول، فتأمل. (القمر) وهي أن الدية إلخ: اعلم أن دية المرأة على النصف من دية الرجل عندنا مطلقا في النفس، وكذا في أطرافها، وقال الشافعي له: إن الجناية التي لم تبلغ الدية فيها ثلثا فالرجل والأنثى فيها سواء كما أن في أحد أشفار العينين ربع الدية، وفي كل إصبع من أصابع اليدين أو الرجلين عشر الدية، وإذا بلغت الدية ثلثا فصاعدًا يؤخذ للمرأة نصف ما يؤخذ للرجل كما أن في كل واحد من العينين نصف الدية، كذا في "الهداية"، وفي "النهاية" أن الشافعي له يقول: إن الثلث وما دونه لا يتنصف وإذا زاد على الثلث يتنصف. وقد مرّ بيان الدية وما يجب فيه الدية فتذكر. (القمر) يقال أي بالإضافة لا بالإطلاق. (القمر)
غريب بهذا اللفظ، ولكن روى عنه مالك له في "الموطأ" في باب عقل المرأة أنه كان يقول: تعاقل المرأة الرجل إلى ثلث الدية إصبعها كأصعبه وسنّها كسنّه وموضحتها كموضحته، ومنقلتها كمنقلته. وروي عن عروة بن الزبير والزهري له مثل ذلك، وفيه: فإذا بلغت ثلث دية الرجل كانت إلى النصف مثل دية الرجل.
أخرج النسائي في "سننه" رقم: ٤۸۰۵ ، باب عقل المرأة، عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: عقل المرأة مثل عقل الرجل حتى يبلغ الثلث من ديتها.
Chapter on Rulings of the Legally Prescribed. Definition of Sunnah and its Ruling. The third is Sunnah: it is the path followed in the religion, and its ruling is that a person is required to establish it without it being fard or wajib. He restricted by his saying 'is required' to exclude nafal (voluntary), and by his saying 'without it being fard or wajib' to exclude fard and wajib. It would have been fitting to mention these restrictions in the definition, but he sufficed with the ruling. However, they said: This definition and ruling apply only to Sunan al-Huda (guided sunnah), and the following division is for absolute Sunnah. Except that Sunnah applies to the way of the Prophet and others, meaning the Companions. 'It is the path followed' etc.: i.e., other than fard and wajib. The indication for this restriction is that Sunnah is contrasted with fard and wajib. What is meant by 'path followed' is the good path which the Prophet and the Companions [؟] and one is required to follow it. (Al-Qamar) 'Is required' etc. due to His statement: 'And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it, and whatever he forbids you, refrain from it' (59:7). (Al-Qamar) 'Without it being fard or wajib' i.e., its requirement is not the requirement of fard or wajib such that the abandoner deserves punishment. (Al-Qamar) 'These restrictions' i.e., that it is required and that its requirement is not that of fard or wajib. (Al-Qamar) 'But they said' etc. Since it might be understood from the previous speech that the mentioned definition and ruling are for absolute Sunnah, the commentator rebuts it by saying 'but they said' etc. (Al-Qamar) 'Except upon Sunan al-Huda' because it is a path followed in the religion and required, while the Sunan al-Zawa'id (supererogatory sunan) are followed out of habit, not worship. (Al-Qamar) 'And the following division' etc.: This rebuts an inferred objection: Since this definition and ruling apply only to Sunan al-Huda, how is it correct to later divide this Sunnah into two types: Sunan al-Huda and Sunan al-Zawa'id? The summary of the rebuttal is that the following division is not a division of this specific Sunnah, but rather a division of absolute Sunnah. The commentator pointed to this later by his saying 'for absolute Sunnah' etc. (Al-Qamar) 'For absolute Sunnah' etc., whether it is Sunan al-Huda or Sunan Zawa'id. (Al-Sunbuli) 'Except that Sunnah' etc.: Explanation: There is no disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i in the definition of Sunnah and its ruling mentioned. The only disagreement is that when the word 'Sunnah' is used absolutely, does it apply to the way of one other than the Prophet or not? The second is his choice, and the first is our choice. Our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah will have its reward and the reward of those who act upon it.' For the word 'whoever' (man) encompasses people. (Al-Qamar) 'And others' etc.: i.e., no disagreement in its essence and ruling, only in its application. According to us, it applies to the way of the Prophet as he said: 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.' (Al-Sunbuli) And others say: 'The sunnah of Abu Bakr and Umar and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.' Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said that its absolute meaning is the way of the Prophet (peace be upon him), meaning that when the word 'Sunnah' is used without a qualifier, it does not apply to the way of the Companions. As narrated that Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'What is less than one-third of the blood money (diyah) is not divided equally, and that is the sunnah.' He meant by it the sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him), which is that when the blood money does not reach one-third, the male and female are equal, and when it reaches one-third and above, half of what is taken for the male is taken for the female. And if one intends a sunnah other than that of the Prophet, one says: 'This is the sunnah of the two shaykhs' or 'the sunnah of Abu Bakr' etc. The saying 'the sunnah of Abu Bakr' etc. is mentioned; this statement is not useful because it is restricted, and the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i is only about the absolute Sunnah, as when the narrator says 'from the Sunnah is such-and-such.' According to him, it is the sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and according to us, it only indicates that it is a path followed in the religion, more general than being his sunnah or that of the Companions. (Al-Qamar) 'Does not apply' etc.: Because the absolute is understood to be the perfect individual, and we say: The absolute conveys absoluteness, so it is not restricted without evidence, and perfection is not evidence for restriction. So it applies to his way and that of others. As for the intention of the Prophet's sunnah in the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib (may Allah be pleased with him), perhaps it is due to the context. Thus it is said, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'Reflect.' (Al-Qamar) 'The Prophet' after 'in' 'does not apply' etc. We say it is absolute, so it is not restricted without evidence. (Al-Sunbuli) 'The sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him)' and this is denied. In 'al-Kifayah' it is said: He meant by it the sunnah of Zaid ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with him), for he was the imam of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib; this statement, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'And that the blood money' etc.: Know that the blood money of a woman is half that of a man according to us absolutely in cases of life and similarly in limbs. Al-Shafi'i said that in an injury where the blood money does not reach one-third, the male and female are equal, as in the case of one eyelid (one-fourth of the blood money), and in each finger of the hands or feet (one-tenth). When the blood money reaches one-third and above, half of what is taken for the male is taken for the female, as in the case of each eye (half the blood money). (Al-Qamar) 'It is said' i.e., by way of addition, not absolutely. (Al-Qamar) Strange in this wording, but Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated in al-Muwatta' in the chapter on the blood money of women that he used to say: 'The blood money of a woman equals that of a man up to one-third of the blood money; her finger is like his finger, her tooth like his tooth, her scalp wound like his scalp wound, her cranial wound like his cranial wound.' And similar is narrated from 'Urwa ibn al-Zubayr and al-Zuhri. And in it: 'When it reaches one-third of the blood money of a man, it becomes half, like the blood money of a man.' Al-Nasa'i narrated in his Sunan, no. 4805, chapter on the blood money of a woman, from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The blood money of a woman is like the blood money of a man until it reaches one-third of her blood money.'
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This is a combined definition and dispute passage from a Hanafi usul text. It defines Sunnah as a 'path followed in the religion' and states its ruling: it is required (yutlabu) but not to the level of obligation (fard or wajib), so one is rewarded for doing it but not punished for leaving it. The commentator clarifies that this definition actually applies only to 'Sunnah al-Huda' (the guided sunnah, i.e., religiously encouraged practices), not to 'Sunnah al-Zawa'id' (the Prophet's habitual actions). The main point of the passage is the madhhab dispute: when the term 'Sunnah' is used absolutely, does it include the practices of the Companions? The Hanafi position (ours) is that it does, based on the Prophet's hadith 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah...' where 'man' is general. Also the hadith 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.' The Shafi'i position is that it only applies to the Prophet. The text provides the example of blood money (diyah) for women to illustrate the difference: Hanafi says a woman's diyah is always half that of a man; Shafi'i says it is equal until it reaches one-third of the full diyah, then becomes half. The passage then discusses the proper interpretation of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's statement, with some debate whether he meant the Prophet's sunnah or that of Zaid ibn Thabit. The commentary (Al-Qamar and Al-Sunbuli) reinforces the Hanafi view that the absolute term is unrestricted.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): The path followed in the religion, required but not obligatory; it includes the ways of the Prophet and the Companions (Hanafi view).
سنة الهدى (sunnat al-huda): The guided sunnah – the religiously encouraged practices that one is required to follow, as opposed to Sunan al-Zawa'id (habitual actions).
سنة الزوائد (sunan al-zawa'id): Supererogatory sunnah or habitual actions of the Prophet; not required in the same way as sunnat al-huda.
مطالب (matlub): Required or demanded; the ruling of sunnah al-huda: one is required to follow it, but not to the level of fard or wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what does the unqualified term 'Sunnah' refer to?
A) Only the practices of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
B) Both the practices of the Prophet and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them).
C) Only the practices of the Companions.
D) Any good deed performed by a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
For the Hanafis, Sunnah in its unqualified sense includes the Prophet's and the Companions' practices, and its ruling is demand (talab) without the severity of obligation.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Absolute Usage of 'Sunnah' – Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Defines Sunnah and refutes Shafi'i claim about absolute usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the unqualified term 'Sunnah', cite the evidence from early usage, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The absolute 'Sunnah' is not restricted to the Prophet – context, not the word itself, determines scope.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar addresses a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh: when a narrator says 'this is from the Sunnah', does it necessarily refer to the Prophet's practice? Imam al-Shafi'i argued yes; the Hanafi school argues that the absolute term includes practices of the Companions and rightly-guided caliphs. The difference has significant implications for deriving rulings from early Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested term
Understand that the dispute is about the word 'Sunnah' when used without any qualifying context (muṭlaq al-sunnah). Hanafis say it means any established religious path; Shafi'is say it means exclusively the Prophet's way.
The key is the absence of a qarīna (contextual indicator).
2
Locate the evidence for each position
Hanafi evidence: actual usage like 'Sunnah of Abu Bakr and Umar'. Shafi'i evidence: the common understanding and the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib who said 'it is the Sunnah' when explaining a diya ruling.
The Hanafi evidence is linguistic; Shafi'i is based on default understanding.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis argue that Sa'id's statement is context-dependent; the absolute term remains absolute. They also suggest Sa'id might have meant the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit, not the Prophet.
The Hanafi principle: al-muṭlaq yabqa ʿalā iṭlāqihi (the absolute remains absolute) until a qarīna restricts it.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a narrator says 'this is from the Sunnah', a Shafi'i would take it as Prophetic; a Hanafi would consider it could be from a Companion. This affects the authority level of the reported practice.
The diya ruling example in the text illustrates how this difference plays out in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف السنة وحكمها
فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
يقال: سنة أبي بكر وعمر وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين. وقال الشافعي بحله مطلقها طريقة النبي عليه، يعني إذا يطلق لفظ السنة بلا قرينة لا يطلق على طريقة الصحابة كما روي أن سعيد بن المسيب قال: "ما دون الثلث من الدية لا ينصف وهو السنة"، أراد بها سنة النبي عليه، وهي أن الدية إذا لم تبلغ ثلثا فالرجل والأنثى فيه سواء، وإذا بلغ الثلث فصاعدًا يؤخذ للمرأة نصف ما يؤخذ للرجل، وإذا أريدت سنة غير النبي عليه يقال : هذه سنة الشيخين لهما أو سنة أبي بكر أو سنة أبي بكر له ونحوه.
يقال سنة أبي بكر إلخ ذكر هذا القول لا يفيد؛ فإن هذا القول مقيّد، والخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي له إنما هو في مطلق السنة كأن يقول الراوي من السنة كذا؛ فعنده على سنة النبي الله و عندنا لا يدل إلا على أنه طريقة مسلوكة في الدين أعم من أن يكون يكون سنته أو سنة الصحابة منه (القمر) لا يطلق إلخ: لأن المطلق يتبادر منه الفرد الكامل، ونحن نقول : إن المطلق يفيد الإطلاق؛ فلا يتقيد بلا دليل وكمال الفرد ليس بدليل التقييد، فيقع على طريقة وغيره، وأما إرادة سنة النبي الله في قول سعيد بن المسيب الله فلعله باقتضاء المقام. كذا قيل، فتأمل. (القمر) فتأمل.
النبي في لا يطلق على إلخ قلنا مطلقة فلا تُقيّد بلا دليل كذا في "الدائر". (السنبلي) سنة النبي عليها وهذا ممنوع قال في "الكفاية": إنه أراد بها سنة زيد بن ثابت له ؛ فإنه إمام سعيد بن المسيب هذا القول، فتأمل. (القمر) وهي أن الدية إلخ : اعلم أن دية المرأة على النصف من دية الرجل عندنا مطلقا في النفس، وكذا في أطرافها، وقال الشافعي له : إن الجناية التي لم تبلغ الدية فيها ثلثا فالرجل و الأنثى فيها سواء كما أن في أحد أشفار العينين ربع الدية، وفي كل إصبع من أصابع اليدين أو الرجلين عشر الدية، وإذا بلغت الدية ثلثا فصاعدًا يؤخذ للمرأة نصف ما يؤخذ للرجل كما أن في كل واحد من العينين نصف الدية، كذا في "الهداية"، وفي النهاية أن الشافعي له يقول : إن الثلث وما دونه لا يتنصف وإذا زاد على الثلث يتنصف. وقد مرّ بيان الدية وما يجب فيه الدية فتذكر. (القمر) يقال أي بالإضافة لا بالإطلاق. (القمر)

** أخرج النسائي في "سننه" رقم: ٤۸۰۵ ، باب عقل ،المرأة، عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده قال: قال رسول الله : عقل المرأة مثل عقل الرجل حتى يبلغ الثلث من ديتها.
Definition of Sunnah and its ruling. Section on revealed rulings. It is said: 'Sunnah of Abu Bakr and Umar' and 'Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.' Al-Shafi'i argued that its absolute usage is the way of the Prophet—meaning, when the word 'Sunnah' is used without a qualifying context, it does not apply to the way of the Companions. It is narrated that Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib said: 'What is less than one-third of the blood-money is not halved, and that is the Sunnah'—he intended by it the Sunnah of the Prophet, namely that when the blood-money does not reach two-thirds, the man and woman are equal; and when it reaches one-third and above, the woman receives half of what the man receives. And when a Sunnah other than the Prophet's is intended, it is said: 'This is the Sunnah of the two Shaykhs' or 'Sunnah of Abu Bakr' etc. (Commentary continues). It is said 'Sunnah of Abu Bakr' etc.—mentioning this statement is not beneficial because this statement is restricted, and the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i is only concerning the unqualified Sunnah, like when a narrator says 'from the Sunnah such and such'. According to him, it refers to the Sunnah of the Prophet; according to us, it only indicates a pursued way in the religion, whether it be the Sunnah of the Prophet or of the Companions. (al-Qamar) 'It is not applied' etc.: because the absolute is understood from the perfect individual. And we say: the absolute conveys absoluteness; thus it is not restricted without evidence, and perfection is not evidence for restriction, so it applies to the Prophet's way and others. As for the intention of the Prophet's Sunnah in the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, perhaps it is due to the context. Thus it is said, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'Reflect.' The Prophet—it is not applied to etc. We say: it is absolute, so it is not restricted without evidence, as in al-Da'ir. (al-Sanbali) 'Sunnah of the Prophet'—and this is denied. He said in al-Kifayah: He intended by it the Sunnah of Zayd ibn Thabit, for he was the imam of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib—this statement, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'And that is the blood-money' etc.: Know that the blood-money of a woman is half of the blood-money of a man according to us absolutely in life (i.e., for murder), and similarly for her limbs. Al-Shafi'i said: For an injury that does not reach one-third of the blood-money, the man and woman are equal, as in one eyelash of the two eyes there is one-quarter of the blood-money, and in each finger of the hands or feet one-tenth of the blood-money; and when it reaches one-third and above, the woman receives half of what the man receives, as in each of the two eyes half of the blood-money. Thus in al-Hidayah, and in al-Nihayah that al-Shafi'i says: One-third and below is not halved; when it exceeds one-third it is halved. The explanation of blood-money and what requires blood-money has passed, so recall. (al-Qamar) 'It is said' i.e., by addition, not by absolute usage. (al-Qamar) It is strange in this wording, but Malik narrated from him in al-Muwatta' in the chapter on the blood-money of a woman that he used to say: The woman and man are equal in blood-money up to one-third: her finger like his finger, her tooth like his tooth, her head wound like his head wound, and her fracture like his fracture. And it is narrated from 'Urwa ibn al-Zubayr and al-Zuhri similarly, and in it: When it reaches one-third of the man's blood-money, it becomes halved like the blood-money of the man. **Al-Nasa'i narrated in his Sunan, no. 4805, chapter on the blood-money of a woman, from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: The blood-money of a woman is like the blood-money of a man until it reaches one-third of her blood-money.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This is a usul dispute passage. The author defines the term 'Sunnah' and addresses a key disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i. The issue: when the word 'Sunnah' is used absolutely (e.g., 'this is from the Sunnah'), does it refer exclusively to the Prophet's Sunnah or does it include the practices of the rightly-guided caliphs and other early Muslims? Al-Shafi'i held that absolute usage is confined to the Prophet's way, based on the common understanding that 'Sunnah' unqualified defaults to the Prophet. The Hanafi position, argued here, is that the absolute term does not automatically restrict to the Prophet; it simply means an established path in religion. Evidence: Even early authorities used 'Sunnah of Abu Bakr' or 'Sunnah of the caliphs'. The author critiques the Shafi'i view by noting that if a restriction were intended, it would need explicit qualification. The passage also uses the blood-money (diya) ruling as a concrete example: the Shafi'i rule partially equalizes man and woman below a threshold, while the Hanafi position is that woman's blood-money is always half. The commentary (by al-Qamar, al-Sanbali, etc.) expands on the proofs, noting that Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's statement might actually refer to Zayd ibn Thabit's practice, not the Prophet's. The hadith from al-Nasa'i is cited to support the threshold equalization, but the author treats it as a rare transmission. All examples are purely from Hanafi fiqh to illustrate the usul point.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The established way (ṭarīqa) in the religion, whether from the Prophet, the Rightly Guided Caliphs, or other Muslims.
مطلق السنة (muṭlaq al-sunnah): The word 'Sunnah' used without any qualifying context (qarīna).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when a narrator says 'this is from the Sunnah', what does it indicate?

C) It refers specifically to the practice of the two Shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar).

Key Takeaway
The absolute term 'Sunnah' in Hanafi usul does not automatically refer to the Prophet; it denotes a general established religious practice, and any restriction requires an explicit context.

The Two Types of Sunnah: Huda and Zawaid
Definition of Sunnah and its two categories with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sunnah in Hanafi usul, distinguish between Sunnat al-Huda and Sunnat al-Zawaid, and apply the ruling for each type to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Sunnah in Hanafi usul is twofold: one whose abandonment incurs blame (Sunnat al-Huda) and one that does not (Sunnat al-Zawaid).

In Hanafi legal theory, the term 'Sunnah' covers both emphasized acts of worship and the Prophet's personal habits. This lesson unpacks the two categories—Sunnat al-Huda and Sunnat al-Zawaid—their respective rulings, and an important internal Hanafi debate about enforcing the first type. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly weighing the legal force of different Prophetic practices.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Two Categories
Locate in the passage the two types of Sunnah: Sunnat al-Huda and Sunnat al-Zawaid. Identify the criteria used to distinguish them (e.g., intention of worship vs. habit).
The passage states Sunnat al-Huda is performed as worship; Sunnat al-Zawaid are habitual actions.
2
Determine the Ruling for Each
For Sunnat al-Huda, note that abandonment incurs blame (isaa'ah). For Sunnat al-Zawaid, there is no blame, but reward for doing. Compare this to the degrees of obligation (fard/wajib).
Blame is not sin; it is reproach and lowering of rank.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Identify the two positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding fighting those who persist in abandoning Sunnat al-Huda. Understand the basis for each view (symbols of religion vs. strict obligation distinction).
The passage mentions fighting only at Muhammad's view; Abu Yusuf restricts it to fard/wajib.
4
Classify Examples
Apply the categories to examples: congregational prayer, adhan (Sunnat al-Huda); the Prophet's style of dress, sitting postures (Sunnat al-Zawaid). Test your ability to distinguish based on criteria.
The passage explicitly lists these.
5
Connect to Usul Framework
Reflect on how this classification fits within the broader Hanafi usul: Sunnah as a source of hukm, with different levels of bindingness. Note that Sunnat al-Huda is sometimes called mu'akkadah (emphasized).
The passage distinguishes absolute Sunnah from earlier definition.
