فصل في الأحكام المشروعة
تعريف السنة وحكمها
وهي نوعان أي مطلق السنة لا التي مضى تعريفها وحكمها على نوعين: الأول: سنة الهدى، وتاركها يستوجب إساءةً، أي جزاء إساءة كاللوم والعتاب، أو سمي جزاء الإساءة إساءة كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَزَاءُ سَيِّئَةٍ سَيِّئَةٌ مِثْلُهَا (الشورى: ٤٠)﴾ كالجماعة والأذان والإقامة؛ فإن هؤلاء كلها من جملة شعائر الدين وإعلام الإسلام؛ ولهذا قالوا: إذا أصرّ أهل مصر على تركها يُقاتلوا بالسلاح من جانب الإمام، وقد وردت في كل منها آثار لا تُحصى. والثاني: الزوائد، وتاركها لا يستوجب إساءة كسير النبي علية في لباسه وقعوده وقيامه؛ فإن هؤلاء كلها لا تصدر منه علينا على وجه العبادة وقصد القربة، بل على سبيل العادة؛ فإنه عالية كان يلبس جُبّة حمراء وخضراء وبيضاء طويل الكمين، وربما يلبس عمامة سوداء وحمراء، صد الله سنته هي، لا التي إلخ فإن التي مضى تعريفها وحكمها هي سنة الهدى (القمر) سنة الهدى هي التي واظب عليها النبي تعبدا وابتغاء مرضات الله تعالى مع الترك مرّةً أو مرتين بلا عذر أو لم يترك أصلاً لكنه لم يُنكر على التارك. والإضافة في قول المصنف : "سنة الهدى" بيانية أي: هدى، والحمل مبالغة. (القمر) سنة الهدى إلخ قلت: هي التي واظب عليها النبي على وجه التعبد وابتغاء رضاء الله تعالى، وهذه السنة مختلفة في التأكيد، فبعضها أشد تأكيداً مثل الجماعة والأذان وسنة الفجر وصلاة الكسوف وغيرها، وبعضها أضعف تأكيدًا وإن كان فيها تأكيد في نفسه كسنة الظهر وغيرها. ومن سنن الهدى علم أحكام الدين، وعلى تركها يُقاتل كما يقاتل أهل البلدة التي تركوا الأذان من "تنوير المنار". (السنبلي) كاللوم بأنه يقال له وقت الحساب : لمَ لَمْ تفعل هذه السنة؟ ويكون له انخفاض من الدرجة العليا. (القمر) يقاتلوا إلخ ولذا كان من عاداته أنه لا يغير على موضع يسمع منه الأذان، ويُغير على موضع لا كذا في صحيح البخاري. ثم اعلم أن قتال المُصرِّين على ترك هذه السنن عند محمد الله بناءً على أنها من إعلام الدين؛ فتركها استخفاف بالدين، وقال أبو يوسف حه لا يقاتلون بل يؤدبون، وإنما القتال لمن ترك الفرض والواجب وأصرّ به فرقًا بين الواجب والفرض وبين السنة (القمر) آثار كما شحن بفضائلها كتب الحديث فطالعها. (القمر) منه يسمع الأذان. الزوائد: اختيار لفظ الجمع ههنا ولفظ الإفراد في الأول إيماء إلى قلة سنة الهدى وكثرة الزوائد.(القمر) فإنه عليا كان إلخ: هذا إرخاء العنان وما رأيت في كتب الحديث أنه كان يلبس جبة حمراء وعمامة حمراء نعم أنه عليها لبس حلة حمراء، أي كان فيها خطوط حمر. رواه البراء بن عازب . (القمر) وكان مقدارها سبعة اَذْرُع أو اثني عشر ذراعًا أو أقل أو أكثر، وكان يقعد مُحتباً تارةً ومربعًا للعذر ، وعلى هيئة التشهد أكثر ، ** فهذا كلها من سنن الزوائد، يُثاب المرء على فعلها ولا يعاقب على تركها، وهو في معنى المستحب إلا أن المستحب ما أحبّه العلماء، وهذا ما اعتاد به النبي عليه.
Chapter on Legal Rulings. Definition of Sunnah and its ruling. It is two types, i.e., absolute Sunnah, not the one whose definition and ruling have passed, are of two types: First: Sunnah of guidance, and its abandoner incurs evil, i.e., penalty of evil like blame and reproach, or the penalty of evil is called evil as in His statement: 'And the recompense of evil is an evil like it' (Ash-Shura: 40), such as congregation, adhan, and iqamah; for all these are among the religious rites and symbols of Islam; hence they said: if the people of a city persist in abandoning them, they are fought with weapons by the imam, and countless traditions have been reported concerning each. Second: The extras, and their abandoner does not incur evil, like the Prophet's habit in his clothing, sitting, and standing; for all these do not issue from him on the basis of worship and pursuit of nearness, but rather by way of custom; for he would wear a red, green, and white robe with long sleeves, and sometimes a black and red turban. Allah's truth, his Sunnah is... not the one, etc. For the one whose definition and ruling have passed is Sunnah of guidance. (Al-Qamar) Sunnah of guidance is that which the Prophet consistently performed as worship and seeking Allah's pleasure, while leaving it once or twice without excuse or not leaving it at all, but he did not rebuke the abandoner. The addition in the author's statement 'Sunnah of guidance' is explanatory, i.e., guidance, and the construct is hyperbolic. (Al-Qamar) Sunnah of guidance, etc. I say: it is that which the Prophet consistently performed as worship and seeking Allah's pleasure, and this Sunnah varies in emphasis, some are more emphasized like congregation, adhan, sunnah of Fajr, eclipse prayer, etc., and some are less emphasized though they have emphasis in themselves like the sunnah of Zuhr, etc. Among the Sunnah of guidance is the knowledge of religious rulings, and for abandoning it one is fought as is fought the people of a town that abandons adhan, from 'Tanwir al-Manar'. (As-Sunbuli) Like blame, that it will be said to him on the Day of Reckoning: 'Why did you not perform this sunnah?' and he will have a lowering from the highest rank. (Al-Qamar) 'they are fought' etc. Hence it was his custom that he would not attack a place from which he heard the adhan, and he would attack a place where he did not, as in Sahih al-Bukhari. Then know that fighting those who persist in abandoning these sunnahs, according to Muhammad, is based on the fact that they are symbols of religion; so abandoning them is contempt for religion. Abu Yusuf said: they are not fought but rather disciplined, and fighting is only for one who abandons an obligatory act (fard or wajib) and persists in it, making a distinction between wajib/fard and sunnah. (Al-Qamar) Traditions, as the books of hadith are filled with their virtues, so study them. (Al-Qamar) from which the adhan is heard. The extras: the choice of the plural form here and the singular form in the first part indicates the scarcity of Sunnah of guidance and the abundance of extras. (Al-Qamar) For he would wear a red, etc.: this is a relaxation of the rein, and I have not seen in hadith books that he wore a red robe and red turban; indeed, he wore a red garment, i.e., it had red stripes. Narrated by al-Bara' ibn 'Azib. (Al-Qamar) And its length was seven cubits or twelve cubits or less or more, and he would sit squatting sometimes and cross-legged due to excuse, and in the posture of tashahhud most of the time, so all these are from the extras of sunnah: one is rewarded for doing them and not punished for leaving them, and it is in the sense of mustahabb except that mustahabb is what the scholars love, and this is what the Prophet accustomed himself to.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage is a definition of Sunnah in the Hanafi usul framework. It begins by stating that Sunnah (the term as used in fiqh) is of two types: Sunnat al-Huda (Sunnah of guidance) and Sunnat al-Zawaid (Sunnah of extras). Sunnat al-Huda refers to acts that the Prophet consistently performed out of devotion, such as congregational prayer, adhan, and iqamah. Leaving such acts incurs blame (isaa'ah), and if an entire city persists in abandoning them, the imam may fight them according to Imam Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf holds that they should only be disciplined. This is because these acts are symbols of Islam. Sunnat al-Zawaid includes the Prophet's personal habits, like the way he dressed or sat. There is no blame for leaving these, but one is rewarded for performing them. The text compares Sunnat al-Zawaid to mustahabb, noting the subtle difference: mustahabb is what scholars deem desirable, while these are the Prophet's customs. The commentary clarifies details on the varying degrees of emphasis within Sunnat al-Huda and provides hadith evidence for the Prophet's attire. The ikhtilaf between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on fighting is recorded in the commentary.

Key Terms
سنة الهدى (Sunnat al-Huda): Sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed as worship, leaving incurs blame
سنة الزوائد (Sunnat al-Zawaid): Prophet's habitual actions, leaving has no blame, reward for doing
إساءة (isaa'ah): Blame or reproach for abandoning a sunnah, not punishment
شعائر الدين (sha'air al-din): Symbols and rites of religion, e.g., adhan, congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a city that persistently abandons the adhan?
A) They are left alone as it is only recommended.
B) They are fought by the imam according to Imam Muhammad.
C) They are executed according to all scholars.
D) They are only given a verbal warning.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, Sunnah is not monolithic: Sunnat al-Huda demands adherence and incurs blame for abandonment, while Sunnat al-Zawaid is commendable but not blameworthy if left.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Rukhsah as a Pure Remission: The Case of Qasr
Explaining rukhsah through the qasr example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats qasr (shortening prayer) as a pure remission (isqat) from Allah that does not require the servant's acceptance, and refute the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A rukhsah from Allah is a sovereign gift; acceptance is not optional.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar introduces the concept of rukhsah (concession) through the famous hadith where the Prophet (saw) calls shortening prayer a 'sadaqah' (charity) from Allah. The Hanafi commentator argues that this sadaqah is a pure remission (isqat mahd) of the obligation to complete the prayer, which does not require acceptance (qabul) by the believer—unlike ordinary charity. This raises a key usul distinction: when Allah grants a concession, it is not contingent on the servant's choice; it is an act of divine sovereignty that must be accepted and acted upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category
Recognise that the passage defines rukhsah as a type of hukm that replaces the original 'azimah (determination) under an excuse. Here, the original ruling is the obligation to complete four rak'ahs; the rukhsah is shortening to two rak'ahs.
2
Analyse the hadith proof
Examine the hadith where Umar (ra) questions the verse about shortening under fear, and the Prophet (saw) clarifies it is a sadaqah from Allah. Focus on the term 'sadaqah' and how the Hanafi school interprets it as a pure remission (isqat) because it does not admit ownership (tamlik).
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Sunan al-Tirmidhi; its transmission is zanni, but its meaning is considered qat'i for the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the Hanafi reasoning
Understand why the Hanafis argue that qasr does not require acceptance: charity that cannot be owned (like the shortening of prayer) is a pure remission, similar to a guardian pardoning retaliation. Since Allah's concession comes from One whose obedience is obligatory, it cannot be rejected.
4
Engage the Shafi'i counter-argument
Consider the Shafi'i objection: since sadaqah normally requires acceptance, the servant may choose not to accept the rukhsah and instead complete the prayer. Then see how the Hanafi response refutes this by distinguishing between ordinary charity and divine remission.
The Shafi'i view is grounded in the general rule that charity needs acceptance; the Hanafi response carves out an exception based on the nature of the object (non-ownable) and the giver (Allah).
5
Extract the usul principle
Formulate the principle: 'A rukhsah from Allah, when it involves a pure remission of an obligation, is not subject to the servant's acceptance; it must be acted upon.' This is derived from the Prophet's command: 'Accept His charity.'
This principle is distinct from the usual fiqh principle that a gift requires acceptance; it is specific to divine concessions.

بيان الرخصة وأنواعها فصل في الأحكام المشروعة فعلم أن الأولى هو الإكمال ونحن نقول: إنه لما نزلت الآية قال عمر : يا رسول الله، ما بالنا نقصر ونحن آمنون؟ فقال عليها: "هذه صدقة تصدق الله تعالى بها عليكم، فاقبلوا صدقته" أي قصر الصلاة سمتاه صدقة والصدقة بما لا يحتمل التمليك إسقاط محض لا يحتمل الرد عن جهة العباد كولي القصاص إذا عفا عن الجناية لا يحتمل الرد ، وإن كان المتصدق ممن لا تلزم طاعته فممن تلزم طاعته وهو الله تعالى أولى بأن لا يرد، وأما نفي الجناح عنهم فإنما هو لتطييب أنفسهم؛ فعلم أن الأولى إلخ ولبعض تلامذة أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام الأعظمي ه: جواب بديع، وهو أنه إذا نفي الجناح في القصر، فعلم أن الإكمال ليس بواجب، وقد مرّ أنه إذا عدم الوجوب لا يبقى صفة الجواز، فيلزم أن لا يكون الإكمال جائزاً. سماه صدقة إلخ : هذا وجه الاستدلال بهذا الحديث، لكنّ للخصم أن يقول: إن حقيقة الصدقة التمليك بلا عوض وهي متعذرة ههنا فيراد بالصدقة الفضل والمنة مجازا، فإن التمليك بلا عوض يلزمه المنة، فحينئذ كيف يتم الاستدلال؟ (القمر) بما لا يحتمل إلخ احترز بهذا القيد عن الصدقة بالدين على من عليه الدين؛ فإن الدين يحتمل التمليك ممن عليه الدين؛ فهذه الصدقة ليست بإسقاط؛ فيحتاج إلى قبول من عليه الدين وترتد برده. (القمر) إسقاط محض إلخ أي لا يتوقف على قبول العبد، فيكون معنى قوله فاقبلوا صدقته، واعملوا بها، واعتقدوها كما يقال : فلان قبل الشرائع أي اعتقدها وعمل بها، وأراد بقوله: "بما لا يحتمل "التمليك" ما لا يحتمله من كل وجه، فالتصدق به وتمليكه لا يكون إسقاطا محضا حتى لو قال لمديونه: تصدّقتُ الدين عليك، فقبل أو سكت يسقط الدين، ولو قال: "لا أقبل" يرتد؛ لأن الدين يحتمل التمليك من المديون ولا يحتمله من غيره؛ لأنه مال من وجه دون وجه فلا يكون التصدق به إسقاط محض فيه معنى التمليك وإنما قال الشارح: إن التصدق بما لا يحتمل التمليك إسقاط محض؛ لأن التصدق أحد أسباب التمليك والتمليك المضاف إلى محل يقبله مثل أن يقول الآخر: وهبت لك هذا العبد أو ملكتكه أو تصدّقت به عليك إذا صدر من العباد قد يقبل الردّ حتى لو قال الآخر: لا أقبل، لا تثبت له ولاية التصرف فيه، وإذا صدر من الله تعالى لا يرتدّ بالردّ؛ لأنه مفترض الطاعة، لا يمكن ردّ ما أثبته وأوجبه، سواء كان لنا أو علينا مثل الإرث؛ فإنه تمليك من الله تعالى، فلا يعتبر قول الوارث لا أقبله، فافهم (السنبلي) لا يحتمل الرد إلخ فلا تقتضي القبول من المتصدق عليه، فاندفع ما روي عن الشافعي له أن القصر صدقة، والصدقة لا تتم بدون قبول المتصدق عليه، فللعبد اختيار قبل الصدقة أو لم يقبلها، فكان له اختيار إكمال الصلاة أيضًا. (القمر) أخرج مسلم في صحيحه رقم ٦٨٦ ، باب صلاة المسافرين وقصرها والترمذي رقم: ٣٠٣٤، باب ومن سورة النساء عن يعلى بن أمية قال: قلت لعمر بن الخطاب فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلاةِ إِنْ خِفْتُمْ أَنْ يَفْتِنَكُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا (النساء: ١٠١) فقد أمن الناس، فقال: عجبتُ مما عجبت منه، فسألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك، فقال: صدقة تصدق الله بها عليكم، فاقبلوا صدقته. فصل في الأحكام المشروعة بيان الرخصة وأنواعها لأنهم كانوا مظنة أن يخطروا ببالهم أن عليهم جناحًا في القصر. وبه علم أن قيد الخوف أيضًا اتفاقي لا موقوفا عليه القصر. وسقوط حرمة الخمر والميتة في حق المضطرّ والمكره، فإن حرمتها لم تبق وقت الاضطرار والإكراه أصلاً، وإن بقيت في حق غيرهما؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَدْ فَصَّلَ لَكُمْ مَا حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِلَّا مَا اضْطُرِرْتُمْ إِلَيْهِ﴾ (الأنعام: ۱۱۹). قيل: وقد فصل لكم ما حَرّم عليكم في جميع الأحوال إلا حال الضرورة؛ فإن لم يأكل الميتة أو لم يشرب الخمر حينئذ ومات، يموت آثماً، بخلاف الإكراه على كلمة الكفر، فإنه وإن ذكر فيه الاستثناء أيضًا بقوله: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنَّ بِالْإِيمَانِ﴾ (النحل: ١٠٦) لكنه ليس استثناء من الحرمة بل من الغضب أو العذاب؛ إذ التقدير : من كفر بالله من بعد إيمانه فعليهم غضب من ولهم عذاب عظيم، إلا من أكره وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف والشافعي له: أنه لا تسقط الحرمة ولكن لا يؤاخذ بها كما في الإكراه على الكفر، لأنهم كانوا إلخ: لا لفهم بالأربع (القمر) وبه أي بما مر من أن القصر صدقة فلا بد من قبولها. (القمر) اتفاقي أي لا مفهوم لهذا القيد أي الشرط، وقد أقرّ به الشافعية أيضًا حيث قال البيضاوي: شريطة باعتبار الغالب في ذلك الوقت؛ ولذلك لم يعتبر مفهومها، وقد تظاهرت السنن على جوازه أيضًا في حال الأمن. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ : دليل لقوله : لم تبق . (القمر) استثناء من قوله ما حرم عليكم إلخ: ههنا قد زلّ قدم الشارح؛ فإنه لا يجوز أن يكون المستثنى منه ما حرم عليكم، فإن الاستثناء حينئذ يكون إخراجًا عن حكم التفصيل لا عن حكم التحريم، وهذا لا يناسب الكلام الإلهي؛ فإن المقصود بيان الأحكام، لا الإخبار عن عدم التفصيل. (القمر) يموت :آثماً لأنه كان له سبيل الخلاص، فألقى نفسه في تهلكة، وفي "التيسير": أن الإثم بشرط علم الإباحة، وإن لم يعلم الإباحة فليس بآثم؛ لأن الإباحة نظرية؛ فيعذر بالجهل (القمر) إذ التقدير إلخ: قال الله تعالى: مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلَكِنْ مَنْ شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْراً فَعَلَيْهِمْ غَضَبٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ) (النحل : ١٠٦) (القمر) والشافعي : أي في رواية عن الشافعي له. (القمر) الحرمة: أي حرمة الخمر والميتة عند الاضطرار. (القمر) ولكن لا يؤاخذ بها : فلو امتنع المضطر عن الخمر والميتة كان ما جوراً. (القمر)
Explanation of Concession and Its Types - Chapter on Prescribed Rulings: So it is known that the better [preference] is completion [of prayer]. We say: When the verse was revealed, Umar said: O Messenger of Allah, why do we shorten while we are secure? He said: 'This is a charity that Allah has given to you as charity, so accept His charity' meaning shortening of prayer. He called it charity, and charity of that which does not admit ownership is a pure remission that does not admit rejection from the side of servants, like the guardian of retaliation if he pardons the crime does not admit rejection. And if the one giving charity is not one whose obedience is obligatory, then one whose obedience is obligatory—and He is Allah Almighty—is more worthy of not being rejected. As for the negation of sin upon them, it is only to soothe their hearts. So it is known that the better is etc. And for some of the students of the greatest scholars, our master Abd al-Salam al-Azami: a wonderful answer, which is that when sin is negated in shortening, it is known that completion is not obligatory, and it has passed that when obligation is absent, the attribute of permissibility does not remain, so it follows that completion is not permissible. He called it charity etc.: This is the aspect of inference from this hadith, but the opponent may say that the reality of charity is ownership without compensation, and that is impossible here, so by charity is meant favor and grace metaphorically, since ownership without compensation entails favor. Then how is the inference complete? (al-Qamar) 'with that which does not admit ownership etc.' He restricted with this qualification to avoid charity of debt upon the debtor; for debt admits ownership from the debtor; so this charity is not a remission; it requires acceptance from the debtor and is void upon rejection. (al-Qamar) 'a pure remission etc.' i.e., it does not depend on the acceptance of the servant, so the meaning of his saying 'accept His charity' is: act upon it and believe in it, as it is said: so-and-so accepted the laws, i.e., believed and acted upon them. He meant by his saying 'that which does not admit ownership' what does not admit it from any aspect, so giving it as charity and owning it is not a pure remission, such that if he says to his debtor: I have given the debt to you as charity, and he accepts or remains silent, the debt falls; but if he says 'I do not accept', it returns; because debt admits ownership from the debtor and does not admit it from others; because it is wealth in one sense but not in another, so giving it as charity is not a pure remission with a meaning of ownership. The commentator only said: giving charity of that which does not admit ownership is a pure remission; because giving charity is one of the causes of ownership, and ownership added to a place that accepts it—like when one says: I have gifted you this slave, or made you owner, or given it as charity to you—if it occurs from servants, it may accept rejection, such that if the other says: I do not accept, he does not establish authority to dispose of it. But when it occurs from Allah Almighty, it is not void by rejection; because He is one whose obedience is obligatory; it is impossible to reject what He has established and made obligatory, whether in our favor or against us—like inheritance; for it is an ownership from Allah Almighty, so the heir's saying 'I do not accept' is not considered. Understand. (al-Sanbali) 'does not admit rejection etc.' so it does not necessitate acceptance from the one receiving charity. Thus what is narrated from al-Shafi'i is refuted: that shortening is a charity, and charity is not complete without the acceptance of the recipient, so the servant has choice whether to accept the charity or not, so he also has choice to complete the prayer. (al-Qamar) Muslim narrated in his Sahih no. 686, Chapter on prayer of travelers and its shortening, and al-Tirmidhi no. 3034, Chapter from Surah al-Nisa', from Ya'la ibn Umayyah who said: I said to Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'And there is no sin upon you if you shorten the prayer if you fear that those who disbelieve may harm you' (4:101) but people are secure; he said: I wondered at what you wondered, so I asked the Messenger of Allah about that, and he said: 'It is a charity that Allah has given to you as charity, so accept His charity.' Chapter on Prescribed Rulings - Explanation of Concession and Its Types: Because they were likely to think in their minds that they had sin in shortening. And by this it is known that the condition of fear is also contingent, not that shortening is dependent on it. And the falling away of the prohibition of wine and carrion for the one in necessity and the one coerced, for their prohibition does not remain at the time of necessity and coercion at all, though it remains for others; due to His saying: 'And He has detailed for you what He has forbidden to you except that which you are compelled to' (6:119). It is said: He detailed for you what He has forbidden to you in all circumstances except the state of necessity; so if he does not eat carrion or drink wine then and dies, he dies sinful, unlike coercion to the word of disbelief, because although exception is mentioned there too in His saying: 'Except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith' (16:106), it is not an exception from the prohibition but from wrath or punishment; for the implied meaning is: Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his faith, upon them is wrath from Allah and they have a great punishment, except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith. And in a narration from Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: that the prohibition does not fall away, but he is not held accountable for it as in coercion to disbelief. Because they were etc.: not understood by the four. (al-Qamar) 'And by this' i.e., by what has passed that shortening is a charity, so it must be accepted. (al-Qamar) 'contingent' i.e., this condition has no concept; indeed the Shafi'is also acknowledged this where al-Baydawi said: conditioned considering the majority at that time; therefore its concept was not considered. And the sunnahs have successively reported its permissibility also in safety. (al-Qamar) 'due to His saying etc.' evidence for his saying 'does not remain.' (al-Qamar) 'exception from His saying: what He has forbidden to you etc.: here the commentator's foot slipped; for it is not permissible that the excepted-from is 'what He has forbidden to you'; for the exception would then be a removal from the ruling of detailing, not from the ruling of prohibition, and this does not suit divine speech; for the purpose is to explain rulings, not to inform about lack of detailing. (al-Qamar) 'dies sinful' because he had a way of deliverance but threw himself into destruction. In al-Taysir: sin is conditional on knowledge of permissibility; if he did not know permissibility, he is not sinful; because permissibility is theoretical, so he is excused by ignorance. (al-Qamar) 'for the implied meaning etc.' Allah said: 'Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his faith, except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith, but whoever opens his chest to disbelief, then upon them is wrath from Allah and for them a great punishment' (16:106). (al-Qamar) 'and al-Shafi'i' i.e., in a narration from al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar) 'the prohibition' i.e., prohibition of wine and carrion in necessity. (al-Qamar) 'but he is not held accountable for it': so if the one in necessity refrains from wine and carrion, he is not considered wrong.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains the concept of rukhsah (concession) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, using two primary examples: shortening prayer (qasr) during travel and the permissibility of consuming forbidden things (like wine and carrion) under necessity or coercion. The author begins by referencing the famous hadith where the Prophet (saw) tells Umar (ra) that shortening prayer is a sadaqah (charity) from Allah, which should be accepted. The commentator clarifies that this sadaqah is a pure remission (isqat mahd) of the obligation to complete the prayer, not a transfer of ownership, and therefore does not require acceptance (qabul) by the servant—unlike ordinary charity which requires acceptance. The condition of fear in the Qur'anic verse about shortening prayer (4:101) is deemed incidental (ittifaqi), not a condition for the concession, as established by the sunnah. The passage then addresses a potential objection from those who argue that since charity requires acceptance, the servant could choose to reject it and complete the prayer. The Hanafi response is that Allah's concession is an act of His sovereignty; its acceptance is not optional. The second part discusses the falling of prohibition (hurmah) of wine and carrion for the one in necessity (mudtarr) and the one coerced (mukrah). Citing Qur'an 6:119, the author asserts that the prohibition is lifted entirely at the time of necessity. For coercion to utter disbelief (kufr), the exception in Qur'an 16:106 is not from the prohibition but from punishment, so the prohibition remains but the coerced person is not sinning if he utters it. The commentator notes a debate between Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i on whether the prohibition falls or not. The passage concludes with subtle points about the construction of the exception in the verse and the condition for sin for not partaking of forbidden things when necessary.

Key Terms
إسقاط محض (isqat mahd): A pure remission; cancellation of an obligation without any transfer of ownership, not requiring acceptance from the beneficiary.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity; in this context, a metaphor for a divine favour/remission that is not ownership-based.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith in this lesson, why does shortening prayer (qasr) not require the servant's acceptance?
A) Because it is a voluntary act that can be done anytime.
B) Because it is a pure remission (isqat mahd) that does not admit ownership, unlike ordinary charity.
C) Because the Prophet (saw) did not ask for acceptance.
D) Because the verse allows it unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
A rukhsah from Allah that is a pure remission (isqat) is not optional; it must be accepted and acted upon.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Rukhsah and the Fall of Prohibition: Dharurah vs Ikrah
Explaining the fall of prohibition under necessity vs coercion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi ruling on the fall of prohibition (hurmah) under necessity (dharurah) and coercion (ikrah), and explain the different treatments using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Necessity lifts the prohibition entirely; coercion on speech only lifts punishment.

This passage continues the discussion of rukhsah by examining two situations where normally forbidden acts become permissible: necessity (eating carrion or drinking wine) and coercion (uttering disbelief). The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction: in necessity, the prohibition itself falls away; under coercion for speech, the prohibition remains but the person is not punished. The commentator supports this with two Quranic verses: 6:119 for necessity and 16:106 for coercion, and notes an intra-Hanafi variance from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Recognise that the passage treats two distinct excuses: dharurah (necessity) for eating haram, and ikrah (coercion) for uttering kufr. In the first, the prohibition falls; in the second, the prohibition remains but punishment is waived.
2
Analyse the Quranic evidence for dharurah
Examine verse 6:119: 'He has detailed for you what He has forbidden except that which you are compelled to.' The Hanafi reading: the exception removes the prohibited items themselves from the category of haram when under necessity. The commenter notes that the exception is from the ruling of prohibition (hurmah), not just from punishment.
The commentator criticises a possible misinterpretation that the exception is from 'detailing' rather than from 'forbidden'.
3
Analyse the Quranic evidence for ikrah
Examine verse 16:106: 'except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith.' The Hanafi position: this exception is from the punishment (wrath and great torment) that follows the description of disbelief, not from the prohibition itself. The act of uttering kufr remains haram, but the coerced person is not sinful.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi and Shafi'i view
A narration from Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i holds that even in necessity, the prohibition does not fall; rather, the person is not held accountable (like in ikrah). The passage mentions this as an alternative view.
The commentator (al-Qamar) distinguishes between the two positions.
5
Extract the usul principle
Formulate: 'The exception in a prohibition verse may either lift the prohibition itself (as in dharurah) or only lift the punishment (as in ikrah). Determination depends on the context and the wording of the text.'

بيان الرخصة وأنواعها فصل في الأحكام المشروعة فعلم أن الأولى هو الإكمال ونحن نقول: إنه لما نزلت الآية قال عمر : يا رسول الله، ما بالنا نقصر ونحن آمنون؟ فقال عليها: "هذه صدقة تصدق الله تعالى بها عليكم، فاقبلوا صدقته" أي قصر الصلاة سمتاه صدقة والصدقة بما لا يحتمل التمليك إسقاط محض لا يحتمل الرد عن جهة العباد كولي القصاص إذا عفا عن الجناية لا يحتمل الرد ، وإن كان المتصدق ممن لا تلزم طاعته فممن تلزم طاعته وهو الله تعالى أولى بأن لا يرد، وأما نفي الجناح عنهم فإنما هو لتطييب أنفسهم؛ فعلم أن الأولى إلخ ولبعض تلامذة أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام الأعظمي ه: جواب بديع، وهو أنه إذا نفي الجناح في القصر، فعلم أن الإكمال ليس بواجب، وقد مرّ أنه إذا عدم الوجوب لا يبقى صفة الجواز، فيلزم أن لا يكون الإكمال جائزاً. سماه صدقة إلخ : هذا وجه الاستدلال بهذا الحديث، لكنّ للخصم أن يقول: إن حقيقة الصدقة التمليك بلا عوض وهي متعذرة ههنا فيراد بالصدقة الفضل والمنة مجازا، فإن التمليك بلا عوض يلزمه المنة، فحينئذ كيف يتم الاستدلال؟ (القمر) بما لا يحتمل إلخ احترز بهذا القيد عن الصدقة بالدين على من عليه الدين؛ فإن الدين يحتمل التمليك ممن عليه الدين؛ فهذه الصدقة ليست بإسقاط؛ فيحتاج إلى قبول من عليه الدين وترتد برده. (القمر) إسقاط محض إلخ أي لا يتوقف على قبول العبد، فيكون معنى قوله فاقبلوا صدقته، واعملوا بها، واعتقدوها كما يقال : فلان قبل الشرائع أي اعتقدها وعمل بها، وأراد بقوله: "بما لا يحتمل "التمليك" ما لا يحتمله من كل وجه، فالتصدق به وتمليكه لا يكون إسقاطا محضا حتى لو قال لمديونه: تصدّقتُ الدين عليك، فقبل أو سكت يسقط الدين، ولو قال: "لا أقبل" يرتد؛ لأن الدين يحتمل التمليك من المديون ولا يحتمله من غيره؛ لأنه مال من وجه دون وجه فلا يكون التصدق به إسقاط محض فيه معنى التمليك وإنما قال الشارح: إن التصدق بما لا يحتمل التمليك إسقاط محض؛ لأن التصدق أحد أسباب التمليك والتمليك المضاف إلى محل يقبله مثل أن يقول الآخر: وهبت لك هذا العبد أو ملكتكه أو تصدّقت به عليك إذا صدر من العباد قد يقبل الردّ حتى لو قال الآخر: لا أقبل، لا تثبت له ولاية التصرف فيه، وإذا صدر من الله تعالى لا يرتدّ بالردّ؛ لأنه مفترض الطاعة، لا يمكن ردّ ما أثبته وأوجبه، سواء كان لنا أو علينا مثل الإرث؛ فإنه تمليك من الله تعالى، فلا يعتبر قول الوارث لا أقبله، فافهم (السنبلي) لا يحتمل الرد إلخ فلا تقتضي القبول من المتصدق عليه، فاندفع ما روي عن الشافعي له أن القصر صدقة، والصدقة لا تتم بدون قبول المتصدق عليه، فللعبد اختيار قبل الصدقة أو لم يقبلها، فكان له اختيار إكمال الصلاة أيضًا. (القمر) أخرج مسلم في صحيحه رقم ٦٨٦ ، باب صلاة المسافرين وقصرها والترمذي رقم: ٣٠٣٤، باب ومن سورة النساء عن يعلى بن أمية قال: قلت لعمر بن الخطاب فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلاةِ إِنْ خِفْتُمْ أَنْ يَفْتِنَكُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا (النساء: ١٠١) فقد أمن الناس، فقال: عجبتُ مما عجبت منه، فسألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك، فقال: صدقة تصدق الله بها عليكم، فاقبلوا صدقته. فصل في الأحكام المشروعة بيان الرخصة وأنواعها لأنهم كانوا مظنة أن يخطروا ببالهم أن عليهم جناحًا في القصر. وبه علم أن قيد الخوف أيضًا اتفاقي لا موقوفا عليه القصر. وسقوط حرمة الخمر والميتة في حق المضطرّ والمكره، فإن حرمتها لم تبق وقت الاضطرار والإكراه أصلاً، وإن بقيت في حق غيرهما؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَدْ فَصَّلَ لَكُمْ مَا حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِلَّا مَا اضْطُرِرْتُمْ إِلَيْهِ﴾ (الأنعام: ۱۱۹). قيل: وقد فصل لكم ما حَرّم عليكم في جميع الأحوال إلا حال الضرورة؛ فإن لم يأكل الميتة أو لم يشرب الخمر حينئذ ومات، يموت آثماً، بخلاف الإكراه على كلمة الكفر، فإنه وإن ذكر فيه الاستثناء أيضًا بقوله: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنَّ بِالْإِيمَانِ﴾ (النحل: ١٠٦) لكنه ليس استثناء من الحرمة بل من الغضب أو العذاب؛ إذ التقدير : من كفر بالله من بعد إيمانه فعليهم غضب من ولهم عذاب عظيم، إلا من أكره وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف والشافعي له: أنه لا تسقط الحرمة ولكن لا يؤاخذ بها كما في الإكراه على الكفر، لأنهم كانوا إلخ: لا لفهم بالأربع (القمر) وبه أي بما مر من أن القصر صدقة فلا بد من قبولها. (القمر) اتفاقي أي لا مفهوم لهذا القيد أي الشرط، وقد أقرّ به الشافعية أيضًا حيث قال البيضاوي: شريطة باعتبار الغالب في ذلك الوقت؛ ولذلك لم يعتبر مفهومها، وقد تظاهرت السنن على جوازه أيضًا في حال الأمن. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ : دليل لقوله : لم تبق . (القمر) استثناء من قوله ما حرم عليكم إلخ: ههنا قد زلّ قدم الشارح؛ فإنه لا يجوز أن يكون المستثنى منه ما حرم عليكم، فإن الاستثناء حينئذ يكون إخراجًا عن حكم التفصيل لا عن حكم التحريم، وهذا لا يناسب الكلام الإلهي؛ فإن المقصود بيان الأحكام، لا الإخبار عن عدم التفصيل. (القمر) يموت :آثماً لأنه كان له سبيل الخلاص، فألقى نفسه في تهلكة، وفي "التيسير": أن الإثم بشرط علم الإباحة، وإن لم يعلم الإباحة فليس بآثم؛ لأن الإباحة نظرية؛ فيعذر بالجهل (القمر) إذ التقدير إلخ: قال الله تعالى: مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ أُكْرِهَ وَقَلْبُهُ مُطْمَئِنٌ بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلَكِنْ مَنْ شَرَحَ بِالْكُفْرِ صَدْراً فَعَلَيْهِمْ غَضَبٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ) (النحل : ١٠٦) (القمر) والشافعي : أي في رواية عن الشافعي له. (القمر) الحرمة: أي حرمة الخمر والميتة عند الاضطرار. (القمر) ولكن لا يؤاخذ بها : فلو امتنع المضطر عن الخمر والميتة كان ما جوراً. (القمر)
Explanation of Concession and Its Types - Chapter on Prescribed Rulings: So it is known that the better [preference] is completion [of prayer]. We say: When the verse was revealed, Umar said: O Messenger of Allah, why do we shorten while we are secure? He said: 'This is a charity that Allah has given to you as charity, so accept His charity' meaning shortening of prayer. He called it charity, and charity of that which does not admit ownership is a pure remission that does not admit rejection from the side of servants, like the guardian of retaliation if he pardons the crime does not admit rejection. And if the one giving charity is not one whose obedience is obligatory, then one whose obedience is obligatory—and He is Allah Almighty—is more worthy of not being rejected. As for the negation of sin upon them, it is only to soothe their hearts. So it is known that the better is etc. And for some of the students of the greatest scholars, our master Abd al-Salam al-Azami: a wonderful answer, which is that when sin is negated in shortening, it is known that completion is not obligatory, and it has passed that when obligation is absent, the attribute of permissibility does not remain, so it follows that completion is not permissible. He called it charity etc.: This is the aspect of inference from this hadith, but the opponent may say that the reality of charity is ownership without compensation, and that is impossible here, so by charity is meant favor and grace metaphorically, since ownership without compensation entails favor. Then how is the inference complete? (al-Qamar) 'with that which does not admit ownership etc.' He restricted with this qualification to avoid charity of debt upon the debtor; for debt admits ownership from the debtor; so this charity is not a remission; it requires acceptance from the debtor and is void upon rejection. (al-Qamar) 'a pure remission etc.' i.e., it does not depend on the acceptance of the servant, so the meaning of his saying 'accept His charity' is: act upon it and believe in it, as it is said: so-and-so accepted the laws, i.e., believed and acted upon them. He meant by his saying 'that which does not admit ownership' what does not admit it from any aspect, so giving it as charity and owning it is not a pure remission, such that if he says to his debtor: I have given the debt to you as charity, and he accepts or remains silent, the debt falls; but if he says 'I do not accept', it returns; because debt admits ownership from the debtor and does not admit it from others; because it is wealth in one sense but not in another, so giving it as charity is not a pure remission with a meaning of ownership. The commentator only said: giving charity of that which does not admit ownership is a pure remission; because giving charity is one of the causes of ownership, and ownership added to a place that accepts it—like when one says: I have gifted you this slave, or made you owner, or given it as charity to you—if it occurs from servants, it may accept rejection, such that if the other says: I do not accept, he does not establish authority to dispose of it. But when it occurs from Allah Almighty, it is not void by rejection; because He is one whose obedience is obligatory; it is impossible to reject what He has established and made obligatory, whether in our favor or against us—like inheritance; for it is an ownership from Allah Almighty, so the heir's saying 'I do not accept' is not considered. Understand. (al-Sanbali) 'does not admit rejection etc.' so it does not necessitate acceptance from the one receiving charity. Thus what is narrated from al-Shafi'i is refuted: that shortening is a charity, and charity is not complete without the acceptance of the recipient, so the servant has choice whether to accept the charity or not, so he also has choice to complete the prayer. (al-Qamar) Muslim narrated in his Sahih no. 686, Chapter on prayer of travelers and its shortening, and al-Tirmidhi no. 3034, Chapter from Surah al-Nisa', from Ya'la ibn Umayyah who said: I said to Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'And there is no sin upon you if you shorten the prayer if you fear that those who disbelieve may harm you' (4:101) but people are secure; he said: I wondered at what you wondered, so I asked the Messenger of Allah about that, and he said: 'It is a charity that Allah has given to you as charity, so accept His charity.' Chapter on Prescribed Rulings - Explanation of Concession and Its Types: Because they were likely to think in their minds that they had sin in shortening. And by this it is known that the condition of fear is also contingent, not that shortening is dependent on it. And the falling away of the prohibition of wine and carrion for the one in necessity and the one coerced, for their prohibition does not remain at the time of necessity and coercion at all, though it remains for others; due to His saying: 'And He has detailed for you what He has forbidden to you except that which you are compelled to' (6:119). It is said: He detailed for you what He has forbidden to you in all circumstances except the state of necessity; so if he does not eat carrion or drink wine then and dies, he dies sinful, unlike coercion to the word of disbelief, because although exception is mentioned there too in His saying: 'Except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith' (16:106), it is not an exception from the prohibition but from wrath or punishment; for the implied meaning is: Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his faith, upon them is wrath from Allah and they have a great punishment, except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith. And in a narration from Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: that the prohibition does not fall away, but he is not held accountable for it as in coercion to disbelief. Because they were etc.: not understood by the four. (al-Qamar) 'And by this' i.e., by what has passed that shortening is a charity, so it must be accepted. (al-Qamar) 'contingent' i.e., this condition has no concept; indeed the Shafi'is also acknowledged this where al-Baydawi said: conditioned considering the majority at that time; therefore its concept was not considered. And the sunnahs have successively reported its permissibility also in safety. (al-Qamar) 'due to His saying etc.' evidence for his saying 'does not remain.' (al-Qamar) 'exception from His saying: what He has forbidden to you etc.: here the commentator's foot slipped; for it is not permissible that the excepted-from is 'what He has forbidden to you'; for the exception would then be a removal from the ruling of detailing, not from the ruling of prohibition, and this does not suit divine speech; for the purpose is to explain rulings, not to inform about lack of detailing. (al-Qamar) 'dies sinful' because he had a way of deliverance but threw himself into destruction. In al-Taysir: sin is conditional on knowledge of permissibility; if he did not know permissibility, he is not sinful; because permissibility is theoretical, so he is excused by ignorance. (al-Qamar) 'for the implied meaning etc.' Allah said: 'Whoever disbelieves in Allah after his faith, except one who is coerced while his heart is firm in faith, but whoever opens his chest to disbelief, then upon them is wrath from Allah and for them a great punishment' (16:106). (al-Qamar) 'and al-Shafi'i' i.e., in a narration from al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar) 'the prohibition' i.e., prohibition of wine and carrion in necessity. (al-Qamar) 'but he is not held accountable for it': so if the one in necessity refrains from wine and carrion, he is not considered wrong.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains the concept of rukhsah (concession) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, using two primary examples: shortening prayer (qasr) during travel and the permissibility of consuming forbidden things (like wine and carrion) under necessity or coercion. The author begins by referencing the famous hadith where the Prophet (saw) tells Umar (ra) that shortening prayer is a sadaqah (charity) from Allah, which should be accepted. The commentator clarifies that this sadaqah is a pure remission (isqat mahd) of the obligation to complete the prayer, not a transfer of ownership, and therefore does not require acceptance (qabul) by the servant—unlike ordinary charity which requires acceptance. The condition of fear in the Qur'anic verse about shortening prayer (4:101) is deemed incidental (ittifaqi), not a condition for the concession, as established by the sunnah. The passage then addresses a potential objection from those who argue that since charity requires acceptance, the servant could choose to reject it and complete the prayer. The Hanafi response is that Allah's concession is an act of His sovereignty; its acceptance is not optional. The second part discusses the falling of prohibition (hurmah) of wine and carrion for the one in necessity (mudtarr) and the one coerced (mukrah). Citing Qur'an 6:119, the author asserts that the prohibition is lifted entirely at the time of necessity. For coercion to utter disbelief (kufr), the exception in Qur'an 16:106 is not from the prohibition but from punishment, so the prohibition remains but the coerced person is not sinning if he utters it. The commentator notes a debate between Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i on whether the prohibition falls or not. The passage concludes with subtle points about the construction of the exception in the verse and the condition for sin for not partaking of forbidden things when necessary.

Key Terms
اضطرار (idhtirar): A state of dire necessity where one is compelled to do something otherwise forbidden due to fear of death or severe harm.
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion where one is forced to perform an act under threat of immediate harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 6:119, what is the effect of necessity on the prohibition of wine and carrion?
A) The prohibition remains but the person is not sinful.
B) The prohibition is removed entirely, making the act permissible.
C) The act becomes obligatory.
D) The act remains haram but the person is rewarded for sacrificing.

Key Takeaway
Necessity lifts the prohibition entirely; coercion on speech only removes the punishment.

Deriving the Ruling on Washing Feet During Mas-h Period
Usul rule on washing feet during mas-h period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the textual and qiyasi evidence for the ruling that washing the foot is not prescribed during mas-h, and explain the difference between the usuliyyun and the author of al-Hidayah regarding removal of khuff and washing.

Core Idea
The khuff prevents hadath transmission, so washing the foot is not required; but removing it to wash is meritorious.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar explores the ruling on washing the feet while wearing khuffs during the valid period of mas-h. It presents two perspectives: the majority usuliyyun hold that washing is not prescribed and would be sinful, while the author of al-Hidayah holds that if one removes the khuff and washes, they are rewarded. This lesson unpacks the textual proof (hadith) and the qiyas (analogy) that underlie the ruling, and then examines the basis for the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that washing the foot is not prescribed (lā yushra'u al-ghusl) during the mas-h period. Determine what this implies about the obligation.
Compare with the obligation for those not wearing khuffs.
2
Locate the textual evidence
The hadith of Ali (رضي الله عنه) shows the Prophet wiping over the top of the khuff. This establishes the permissibility of wiping and implicitly that washing is superseded.
Consider the thubut (zanni) and dalala (qati) of the hadith.
3
Apply the qiyas
The original obligation is washing the foot; the khuff covers the foot and prevents the transmission of hadath. Therefore, wiping suffices as an alternative. This is a clear qiyas jaliy.
Identify the asl, far', and illa as shown in the qiyas panel.
4
Note the difference in perspectives
The usuliyyun conclude that washing is sinful because it violates the concession; the author of al-Hidayah argues that if one removes the khuff and washes, it is rewarded because washing is the original and more intense act.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference based on emphasis.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: is it recommended or sinful to wash the foot after removing the khuff within the period? The author of al-Hidayah considers it rewarded, while the usuliyyun would consider it sinful without removal.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice often follows al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسقوط غسل الرّجل في مدة المسح، فإن استتار القدم بالخف يمنع سراية الحدث إليه، وقد كان طاهراً، وما حل فوق الخفّف فقد زال بالمسح، فلا يشرع الغسل في هذه المدة وإن بقي في حق غير اللابس، وهذا على رواية الأصوليين، وأما صاحب "الهداية" فقد قال: إن نزع الخفّ في المدة، وغسل الرّجل يكون مأجورًا.
And the falling away of washing the foot during the period of wiping (mas-h). For the concealment of the foot by the khuff prevents the transmission of the hadath to it, and it was pure, and what is above the khuff has been removed by wiping, so washing is not prescribed during this period, although it remains for one not wearing khuffs. This is according to the narration of the usuliyyun. As for the author of al-Hidayah, he said that if he removes the khuff within the period and washes the foot, he is rewarded.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
The passage discusses the fiqh ruling regarding washing the feet when one is in the state of wiping over khuffs. The core issue: during the valid period of mas-h (one day and night for residents, three days and nights for travelers), the foot is considered protected from hadath by the khuff. Since the foot was pure before the hadath, and only the area above the khuff is affected by hadath (which is removed by wiping), there is no requirement to wash the foot as long as the khuff remains on. The ruling is specific to the one wearing khuffs; for others not wearing them, washing the foot remains obligatory. According to the usuliyyun (scholars of usul), washing the foot without removing the khuff would be sinful. However, the author of al-Hidayah (Marghinani) holds that if one removes the khuff within the period and washes the foot, it is meritorious because washing is more strenuous and thus more rewarding. This shows consideration of the principle that the default ruling for muff is washing, and wiping is a concession; thus, reverting to washing by removing the khuff is encouraged.

Key Terms
المسح (al-masḥ): Wiping over the khuff as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock worn over the foot that meets conditions for wiping.
مدة المسح (muddah al-masḥ): The duration of validity of wiping: one day and night for resident, three days and nights for traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a person who washes his foot without removing the khuff during the mas-h period?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is recommended and rewarded.
C) It is sinful (according to the usuliyyun).
D) It is permissible but disliked.

Key Takeaway
The khuff prevents hadath, so washing is not required; but the original ruling of washing remains commendable if done after removing the khuff.

Defining the Sunnah in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Defining Sunnah and its scope in usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Sunnah in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and distinguish its scope from the fiqh definition.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, Sunnah includes the Prophet's statements, actions, and tacit approvals, plus the Companions' statements and actions.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar begins the chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah. It explains how the term 'Sunnah' is defined in usul al-fiqh, noting its broad scope that includes the Prophet's words, deeds, and approvals, as well as those of the Companions. The commentator then refines this definition for the current chapter, restricting it to prophetic statements to avoid overlap with later sections. Understanding this definition is crucial because the Sunnah, as the second primary source of legislation, interacts with the Quran and carries the same categories of general, specific, command, and prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of Sunnah in usul
Read the opening sentence: 'Sunnah is applied to the statement of the Messenger, his action, his tacit approval, and to the statements of the Companions and their actions.' Note the four components: qawl (statement), fi'l (action), sukut (tacit approval), and the inclusion of the Companions' statements and actions.
Hanafi usul uniquely includes Companions' actions as part of the Sunnah via taqrir.
2
Note the restriction for this chapter
The commentator says it is appropriate (yanbaghi) to restrict 'Sunnah' here to the Prophet's statements only. Why? Because the author will later discuss prophetic actions and Companion actions in separate sections. This is a contextual narrowing to avoid repetition.
The commentator uses 'yanbaghi' (appropriate) not 'yajib' (obligatory), indicating it is a preference, not a necessity.
3
Distinguish the usul definition from the fiqh definition
The passage explicitly contrasts the usul definition with the fiqh one: in fiqh, Sunnah refers to an act the Prophet consistently performed (i.e., a supererogatory or commendable act). In usul, it is a source of law, not a category of obligation.
This distinction prevents confusion when reading fiqh texts that use 'sunnah' to mean 'recommended'.
4
Understand the relationship between Quran and Sunnah
The passage states that the divisions of the Quran (general, specific, command, prohibition) also run in the Sunnah. This means the same tools of interpretation (takhsis, taqyid, etc.) apply to Sunnah texts.
The chapter aims to clarify what is unique to the Sunnah, i.e., rulings not found in the Quran.
5
Interpret the phrase 'what is specific to the Sunnahs'
The commentator resolves a grammatical issue: the phrase means matters that are only found in the Sunnah, not in the Quran. This ensures the chapter's purpose is to highlight distinctive Sunnah rulings.
This is an example of how scholars carefully parse language to avoid misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب أقسام السنة
تعريف السنة
ولما فرغ عن بيان أقسام الكتاب شرع في بيان أقسام السنة، فقال:
[تعريف السنة]
[باب أقسام السنة]
السنة تطلق على قول الرسول عليه، وفعله، وسكوته، وعلى أقوال الصحابة، وأفعالهم، والحديث
أي عند أمر يعانيه
يطلق على قول الرسول علي خاصة، ولكن ينبغي أن يكون المراد بالسنة ههنا هو هذا فقط؛ لأن المصنف له ذكر أفعال النبي عليا، وأفعال الصحابة وأفعال الصحابة عليه وأقوالهم بعد هذا الباب في فصل آخر . الأقسام التي سبق ذكرها في بحث الكتاب من الخاص والعام والأمر والنهي وغير ذلك كلها ثابتة في السنة فيعلم حالها بالمقايسة عليه، وهذا الباب لبيان ما تختص به الكتاب السنن ولم يوجد في الكتاب قط.
شرع إلخ: وأخر بحث السنة؛ لأنها ثابتة من الكتاب. (القمر) باب أقسام السنة إلخ: شرع في السنة بعد بيان الكتاب لتأخرها عن الكتاب ،رتبة وتقدمها على الباقين والسنة في اللغة العادة ،والسيرة وهي في الأصول ما ذكره الشارح، وهو احتراز عن السنة في الفقه، فهي عبارة هناك عن فعل وَاظَبَ عليه رسول الله عن فعل وَاظَبَ عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم "شرح مسلم" لمولانا بحر العلوم (السنبلي تطلق أي في اصطلاح الأصول. (القمر) والحديث يطلق إلخ كذا في "التوضيح" وفي بعض حواشي شرح "النخبة": أن الخبر مرادف للحديث، وهو مرادف للسنة، ويعم كعموم السنة. (القمر) هو هذا : أي قول الرسول خاصة . (القمر) ذكر إلى أي بطريق الإلحاق والتبع، ويمكن أن يقال: إن الذكر بعد هذا الباب ليس بطريق الإلحاق والتبع، بل وقع مقصودًا، فحينئذٍ يمكن أن يكون المراد بالسنة ههنا أعم من قول الرسول ، وفعله، وسكوته، وأقوال الصحابة الله وأفعالهم؛ ولذا قال الشارح له: ينبغي، ولم يقل: يجب. (القمر) الأقسام التي إلخ اعتذار من المصنف له لعدم ذكر الأقسام التي ذكرت في الكتاب في السنة. (القمر) في السنة أي في السنة القولية لا الفعلية ولا السكوتية. (القمر)
طاالله
ما تختص به السنن: لما كان أصل الباء أن تدخل على المختص به فصار السنن مختصة، وما بين في هذا الباب مختصة به وهذا لا يستقيم؛ لأن السنن لا تختص به الجريان أقسام الكتاب في السنن أيضا، فلا بد من الصرف عن الظاهر بأن يقال: إن الباء داخلة على المختص، فيكون المعنى ما يختص بالسنن أي لا يتجاوز عن السنن، ولا يوجد في غير السنن وهذا معنى مستقيم، وإليه أشار الشارح حله بقوله : "ولم يوجد في الكتاب". (القمر)
Chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah. Definition of the Sunnah. When he finished explaining the divisions of the Book, he began explaining the divisions of the Sunnah, and said: [Definition of the Sunnah] [Chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah] The Sunnah is applied to the statement of the Messenger (peace be upon him), his action, his tacit approval, and to the statements of the Companions and their actions. And the hadith is applied specifically to the statement of the Messenger (peace be upon him). But it is appropriate that what is meant by the Sunnah here is only this; because the author mentions the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the actions of the Companions and their statements after this chapter in another section. The divisions that were previously mentioned in the discussion of the Book—of the general, specific, command, prohibition, and others—all are established in the Sunnah, and their status is known by analogy with it. And this chapter is to clarify what is specific to the Sunnah and is not found in the Book at all. (al-Qamar): 'He began' etc.: He delayed the discussion of the Sunnah because it is established from the Book. (al-Qamar): 'Chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah' etc.: He began with the Sunnah after explaining the Book because it is after the Book in rank and precedes others. And the Sunnah in language is custom and way; and in usul it is what the commentator mentioned, which is a precaution against the Sunnah in fiqh, for there it is an expression for an act that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) consistently performed. (al-Sunbuli): 'It is applied' i.e., in the terminology of usul. (al-Qamar): 'And the hadith is applied' etc. Thus in al-Tawdih, and in some glosses of Sharh al-Nukhbah: that khabar is synonymous with hadith, and it is synonymous with Sunnah, and it is general like the generality of the Sunnah. (al-Qamar): 'It is this' i.e., the statement of the Messenger specifically. (al-Qamar): 'Mentions' i.e., by way of attachment and following. And it can be said that the mention after this chapter is not by way of attachment and following, but rather it occurred intentionally; then it is possible that what is meant by the Sunnah here is more general than the statement of the Messenger, his action, his tacit approval, and the statements of the Companions and their actions. For this reason the commentator said: 'it is appropriate' and did not say 'it is necessary'. (al-Qamar): 'The divisions that' etc. This is an apology from the author for not mentioning the divisions that were mentioned in the Book in the Sunnah. (al-Qamar): 'in the Sunnah' i.e., in the verbal Sunnah, not the practical nor the tacit. (al-Qamar): 'What is specific to the Sunnahs': Since the rule of the letter ba' is that it enters upon that which is specific, it would imply that the Sunnahs are specific, and what is explained in this chapter is specific to it. This is not correct because the Sunnahs are not specific to it, as the divisions of the Book also run in the Sunnah. So it is necessary to turn from the apparent meaning by saying that the ba' enters upon that which is specific, so the meaning is 'what is specific to the Sunnahs' i.e., it does not go beyond the Sunnahs, and is not found in other than the Sunnahs. This is a straightforward meaning, and the commentator indicated it by his saying: 'and it is not found in the Book.' (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition of 'Sunnah'. It begins the chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah, explaining that in usul, Sunnah applies to the Prophet's statements, actions, and tacit approvals (sukut), as well as to the statements and actions of the Companions. However, the commentator notes that it is appropriate here to restrict Sunnah to the Prophet's statements only, because the author will later discuss actions of the Prophet and Companions in separate sections. The passage also distinguishes the usul definition from the fiqh definition: in fiqh, Sunnah is an act that the Prophet consistently performed. The term 'hadith' is often synonymous with Sunnah, but here it is specifically the Prophet's words. A key point is that the divisions of the Quran (general, specific, command, prohibition) also apply to the Sunnah, and this chapter aims to clarify what is unique to the Sunnah as opposed to the Quran. The commentary resolves a grammatical issue: the phrase 'what is specific to the Sunnahs' means matters that are only found in the Sunnah, not in the Quran. The passage reflects standard Hanafi usul, emphasizing the primacy of the Quran and the subsidiary role of the Sunnah.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): In usul al-fiqh, it is applied to the Prophet's statements, actions, and tacit approvals, and to the statements and actions of the Companions; but in this context, it may be restricted to the Prophet's statements.
الحديث (al-hadith): Here it is said to be applied specifically to the statement of the Prophet, but often it is synonymous with Sunnah and khabar.

Definition of Mutawatir Khabar
Defines mutawatir as the first division of khabar with conditions of large number, diversity, and justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mutawatir khabar and identify its three conditions as mentioned in the text.

Core Idea
Mutawatir gives certain knowledge because narrators are too many and too diverse to conspire on a lie.

This passage marks the beginning of the discussion on how reports from the Prophet reach us. The author introduces the first and highest category: mutawatir. Understanding this definition is foundational because it determines which narrations yield absolute certainty in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines 'al-mutawatir' as a type of khabar (report). Note that it is introduced as 'the first division' in terms of how reports reach us from the Prophet.
Mutawatir is the highest category of narration.
2
List the three conditions mentioned
The definition gives three conditions: (1) an uncountable number of narrators, (2) geographical diversity making collusion improbable, (3) justice ('adalah) of the narrators.
All three conditions must be met for tawatur.
3
Understand the legal effect
The purpose of these conditions is to produce certain knowledge (qat'i) – there is no room for doubt. This is why mutawatir reports are binding without further inquiry into chains.
Certain knowledge is the consequence (athar) of tawatur.
4
Contextualize within the four divisions
The text mentions 'four divisions' of khabar. Mutawatir is the first (complete connection). The remaining divisions (ahad etc.) will follow.
Mutawatir is the only division that gives certainty; others give probability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك أربعة أقسام. التقسيم الأول في كيفية الاتصال بنا من رسول الله عليه السلام: إما أن يكون كاملاً كالمتواتر. وهو الخبر الذي رواه قوم لا يُحصى عددهم ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب؛ لكثرتهم وتباين أماكنهم وعدالتهم.
And that is four divisions. The first division is concerning the manner of connection to us from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): either it is complete, like the mutawatir. And it is the report which a group narrated whose number cannot be counted, and collusion on falsehood cannot be imagined, due to their large number, diversity of locations, and their justice.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage introduces the first division of khabar (reports) in terms of how they reach us from the Prophet. The author states that there are four divisions (detailed later). The first is the 'complete' connection, which is the mutawatir. The definition of mutawatir is given: a narration transmitted by a group so large that it is impossible to count them, and it is inconceivable that they all agreed to lie because of their great number, geographical diversity, and trustworthiness (justice). This definition is taken from the Hanafi usul tradition, though some scholars do not require diversity of location or justice as conditions for tawatur.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawātir): الخبر الذي رواه قوم لا يُحصى عددهم ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب لكثرتهم وتباين أماكنهم وعدالتهم
الخبر (al-khabar): ما يروى عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) A narration transmitted by so many that collusion on falsehood is impossible
D) A narration that is weak

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir khabar is a report with an uncountable number of narrators, diverse locations, and justice, yielding certain knowledge.

Definition and Conditions of Mutawatir Hadith
Defines mutawatir and sets conditions for certain knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mutawatir hadith, identify its essential condition (impossibility of collusion), and differentiate between silent tawatur, meaningful tawatur, and ahad reports.

Core Idea
A mutawatir report yields certain knowledge because collusion on falsehood is impossible, regardless of exact numbers.

In this lesson, we explore the first classification of hadith: mutawatir. The text defines it by the impossibility of collusion rather than a fixed number of narrators. We also encounter subtypes like silent and meaningful tawatur, and a key condition that the certainty must persist across generations. Understanding these nuances is essential for assessing the epistemological weight of prophetic reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of mutawatir
Find the key phrase: 'al-khabar alladhi rawahu qawm la yutawwaham tawatu'uhum 'ala al-kadhib' and note the three factors: multitude, diverse locations, integrity.
The definition is the foundation for all subsequent discussion.
2
Note the conditions debate
The commentary clarifies that location and integrity are not prerequisites; knowledge can arise from multiple narrators even without these.
This shows the Hanafi emphasis on the rational certainty threshold.
3
Recognize the subtypes
Distinguish silent tawatur (tasawwut sukuti) and meaningful tawatur (ma'nawi) from the basic definition.
These expand the scope of mutawatir beyond explicit word-for-word transmission.
4
Understand the persistence condition
The text stresses that the condition of non-collusion must continue in every generation; otherwise the report becomes mashhur.
This ensures that the certainty remains available to later generations.
5
Consider the dispute with al-Jassas
Al-Jassas held that persistence is not required; the majority requires it. This affects classification of reports.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

التقسيم الأول في كيفية الاتصال بنا من رسول الله ، أي كيف يتصل بنا هذا الحديث منه بطريق التواتر وغيره. إما أن يكون كاملاً كالمتواتر. وهو أي الاتصال
بيان خبر المتواتر]
وهو الخبر الذي رواه قوم لا يُحصى عددهم ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب؛ لكثرتهم وتباين أماكنهم وعدالتهم. وذلك: أي البيان أربع تقسيمات بالاستقراء. (القمر) لا أصول الحديث إلخ وسيجيء بعض بيان المخالفة بين اصطلاح الأصوليين أي أصول الفقه وأصول الحديث. (القمر)
الإتصال: وهو عدم انقطاع واسطة بينه وبين الراوي. (القمر) كالمتواتر أورد كاف التمثيل، لأن الاتصال الكامل قد يكون بغير التواتر كالسماع من في رسول الله الله مشافهة. (القمر) وهو في اللغة من التواتر، وهو تتابع أشياء بينها مهلة [فتح الغفار ۳۲۹] رواه قوم سواء كانوا كفارًا أو مسلمين عدولاً أو فُساقًا، إلا أن الرواة إذا كانوا عدولاً فبالعدد القليل منهم يحصل العلم، وإذا كانوا فساقًا فلابد للعلم من العدد الكثير منهم، فلو أخبر كل واحد من الجماعة بخبر وسكت الباقون، وعلم بالأمارات أنهم لو كانوا مترددين في هذا الخبر لما سكتوا، فهذا الخبر أيضًا في حكم المتواتر يفيد العلم، ويسمى هذا تواترا سكوتيا، ولو أخبر كل واحد من الجماعة بخبر بألفاظ مختلفة لكن جميع الأخبار مشتركة في حكم وإن كانت دلالتها على ذلك الحكم بالالتزام حصل العلم بذلك الحكم، ويسمى هذا تواتراً معنويا وكل خبر منها يسمى خبر الآحاد، والأحاديث على هذا الدِّيدن كثيرة كحديث المسح على الخفين وغيره. (القمر)
ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم: أي اتفاقهم على الكذب لا عمدا، ولا سهوا، ولا خطاً، وهذا تفسير لكثرة عدد الرواة. (القمر) وتباين أماكنهم إلخ فيه أن تباين الأمكنة أي تباعدها وعدالة الرواة ليستا بشرطين في التواتر على مذهب العامة وإن قال باشتراطهما قوم لأن العلم قد يحصل بكثرة الرواة وإن كانوا فجارا ومتوطنى بقعة واحدة. (القمر)

باب أقسام السنة
بيان خبر المتواتر
ولم يشترط فيه تعين عدد كما قيل: إنها سبعة وقيل أربعون وقيل: سبعون، بل كل ما يحصل به العلم الضروري فهو من أمارة التواتر.
ويدوم فيه هذا الحد، فيكون آخره كأوّله، وأوّله كآخره، وأوسطه كطرفيه، يعني يستوي جميع الأزمنة من أوّل ما نشأ ذلك الخبر إلى آخر ما بلغ إلى هذا الناقل، فالأول هو زمان ظهور الخبر، والآخر هو زمان كل ناقل يتصوره آخرًا، فلو لم يكن في الأول أي الخبر كذلك كان آحاد الأصل، فسمي مشهوراً إن انتشر في الأوسط والآخر، ولو لم يكن في أي على هذا الحد الأوسط والآخر كذلك كان منقطعًا.
ولم يشترط إلخ لما كان يرد على قول المصنف: "لا يحصى عدهم أن عدم إحصاء عدد الرواة ليس بشرط في المتواتر عند الجمهور، فإنه قد يحصل العلم واليقين بخبر عشرة من الرجال إذا كانوا ثقات عدولاً فالمتواتر ما يكون رواته بحيث لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب وإن كانوا محصورين فالصواب حذف قوله: "لا يُحصى عددهم" فالشارح صرف عنانه إلى توجيه هذا القول؛ فقال: ولم يشترط إلخ إيماء إلى أن المراد منه أنه ليس يشترط في المتواتر تعيين العدد فإن ما ذكر المعتبرون للعدد المعين ليس بشبهة فضلاً أن يكون حجة، وليس المراد منه أن عدم إحصاء عدد الرواة شرط في التواتر كما هو مذهب البعض. (القمر) أنها سبعة قياسًا على غسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب سبع مرات كما ورد في الحديث. (القمر) وقيل: أربعون؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ حَسْبُكَ اللَّهُ وَمَنِ اتَّبَعَكَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾ ، (الأنفال: ٦٤) وكان المؤمنون في ذلك الزمان أربعين. (القمر) وقيل سبعون لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاخْتَارَ مُوسَى قَوْمَهُ سَبْعِينَ رَجُلاً لِمِيقَاتِنَا (الأعراف: ١٥٥) وقيل: أربعة كعدد شهود الزنا، وقيل: عشرة؛ لأن ما دون العشرة أحاد، وقيل: عشرون؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن يَكُنْ مِنْكُمْ عِشْرُونَ صَابِرُونَ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْن له (الأنفال : ٦٥) (القمر) ويدوم هذا الحد أي عدم توهم اجتماع الرواة على الكذب، ثم اعلم أن هذا الشرط عند الجمهور خلافًا للجصاص؛ فإن المشهور عنده من المتواتر.(القمر) يستوي فيه أي في هذا الحد، وهو عدم توهم اجتماع الرواة على الكذب والمراد بالاستواء أن لا ينقص الكثرة عن العدد الذي أحالت العادة تواطؤهم على الكذب وليس المراد به أن لا تزيد؛ إذ الزيادة مطلوبة من باب الأولى، وقيل: إنه يشترط أن يكون مستند انتهاء المتواتر الأمر المشاهد بالبصر، أو المسموع بالسمع، لا ما يثبت بالعقل الصرف، فإنه لو اتفق أهل إقليم على مسألة عقلية لم يحصل لنا اليقين بل تطالبهم بالبرهان. (القمر)
ولو لم يكن في الأوسط والآخر كذلك أي منتشر ، وكان في الأول على حد التواتر كان إلخ. (القمر)
Chapter: Sections of the Sunnah. 499. Explanation of the First Division, Explanation of Mutawatir Report. That is four divisions, i.e., four classifications, and under each division are multiple sections. This explanation in this chapter follows the principles of fiqh (usul al-fiqh), not the principles of hadith, even if they share some names and rules. [Explanation of the First Division] The first division concerns how [the report] reaches us from the Messenger of God, i.e., how this hadith reaches us from him by way of tawatur or otherwise. Either it is complete, like mutawatir. And it (the connection) is... Explanation of Mutawatir Report: It is the report narrated by a group whose number cannot be counted, and collusion on lying is not imagined, due to their multitude, diversity of locations, and their integrity. That is: the explanation is four divisions by induction. (al-Qamar) 'Not the principles of hadith' etc., and some explanation of the difference between the terminology of the usuliyyun (i.e., usul al-fiqh) and usul al-hadith will come later. (al-Qamar) 'Connection': it is the absence of an intermediary between it and the narrator. (al-Qamar) 'Like mutawatir' – the kaaf is for exemplification, because complete connection may be other than tawatur, like hearing directly from the Messenger of God orally. (al-Qamar) It is linguistically from tawatur, which is the succession of things with intervals between them. [Fath al-Ghaffar 329] 'Narrated by a group' whether they are disbelievers or Muslims, upright or sinful, except that if the narrators are upright, knowledge is obtained from a small number of them, and if they are sinful, knowledge requires a large number from them. So if each one of a group reports a report and the rest remain silent, and it is known by indications that if they had been uncertain about this report they would not have remained silent, then this report is also in the ruling of mutawatir, giving knowledge, and this is called 'silent tawatur'. And if each one of a group reports a report with different wordings, but all the reports share a ruling, even if their indication of that ruling is by implication, knowledge of that ruling is obtained, and this is called 'meaningful tawatur'. Each such report is called khabar al-ahad, and hadiths of this type are many, like the hadith of wiping over the khuffayn and others. (al-Qamar) 'And collusion on lying is not imagined': i.e., their agreement on lying, not intentionally, nor forgetfully, nor mistakenly. This is an interpretation of the large number of narrators. (al-Qamar) 'Diversity of their locations' etc. – therein [it is mentioned] that diversity of locations, i.e., their distance, and the integrity of narrators are not conditions for tawatur according to the majority, although some people made them conditions, because knowledge may be obtained by multitude of narrators even if they are sinners and inhabitants of one place. (al-Qamar) [Page 501] Chapter: Sections of the Sunnah. Explanation of Mutawatir Report. And a specific number was not stipulated for it, as it was said: it is seven, and it was said: forty, and it was said: seventy; rather, everything by which necessary knowledge is obtained is an indication of tawatur. And this condition persists, so its last is like its first, and its first like its last, and its middle like its ends, meaning all times are equal from the first time that report originated until the last that reached this transmitter. So the first is the time of the emergence of the report, and the last is the time of each transmitter that he imagines as last. So if it was not like that in the first (i.e., the report), it was ahad al-asl, so it is called mashhur if it spread in the middle and last. And if it was not like that in the middle and last, it was munqati'. 'And a specific number was not stipulated' etc. – because an objection might be raised against the author's statement: 'Their number cannot be counted' that the lack of enumeration of the number of narrators is not a condition for mutawatir according to the majority, for knowledge and certainty may be obtained from a report of ten men if they are reliable and upright. So mutawatir is that whose narrators are such that collusion on lying is not imagined, even if they are limited. So the correct thing is to delete his statement: 'Their number cannot be counted.' So the commentator directed his attention to justify this statement; he said: 'And a specific number was not stipulated' etc., indicating that what is meant is that specifying a particular number is not required for mutawatir, for what has been mentioned by those who consider a specific number is not even a conjecture, let alone be a proof. And it is not meant that lack of enumeration of the number of narrators is a condition for tawatur, as is the opinion of some. (al-Qamar) 'It is seven' by analogy with washing the vessel from the dog's lapping seven times as came in the hadith. (al-Qamar) 'And it was said: forty' because of His statement: 'O Prophet, sufficient for you is Allah and [for] those who follow you among the believers' (al-Anfal: 64), and the believers at that time were forty. (al-Qamar) 'And it was said: seventy' because of His statement: 'And Moses chose from his people seventy men for Our appointment' (al-A'raf: 155). And it was said: four like the number of witnesses for adultery; and it was said: ten because what is less than ten is ahad; and it was said: twenty because of His statement: 'If there are among you twenty steadfast, they will overcome two hundred' (al-Anfal: 65). (al-Qamar) 'And this condition persists' i.e., the non-imagination of collusion of narrators on lying. Then know that this condition according to the majority is contrary to al-Jassas, for the well-known [view] with him is from mutawatir. (al-Qamar) 'It is equal in it' i.e., in this condition, which is the non-imagination of collusion of narrators on lying. What is meant by equality is that the multitude does not decrease below the number that customarily makes their collusion on lying impossible; and it is not meant that it does not increase, for increase is desirable a fortiori. And it was said: it is required that the basis of the termination of mutawatir be something witnessed by sight or heard by hearing, not what is established by pure reason; for if the people of a region agreed on an intellectual matter, it would not give us certainty, but we would demand proof from them. (al-Qamar) 'And if it was not like that in the middle and last' i.e., widespread, and it was in the first at the limit of tawatur, then it is... etc. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is an expanded definition of mutawatir from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author begins by distinguishing between usul al-fiqh and usul al-hadith, noting that the analysis here follows fiqh principles. The first division concerns how reports reach us: complete transmission (mutawatir) or incomplete (ahad). The core definition of mutawatir is given as a report narrated by a group too numerous to be counted and whose collusion on falsehood is inconceivable due to their large number, diverse locations, and integrity. The commentary (from 'al-Qamar') clarifies that this definition is not strictly dependent on numbers or specific conditions like location and integrity; rather, any situation that yields necessary knowledge qualifies. The passage then introduces subtypes: 'silent tawatur' (when some narrators remain silent but indications show agreement) and 'meaningful tawatur' (when multiple reports with different wordings all point to the same ruling). The text insists that no fixed number is required; the condition is simply that the report produces necessary knowledge. This condition must persist across all generations; if the condition existed only in the first generation but not later, the report is considered mashhur (well-known) rather than mutawatir. A dispute is noted with al-Jassas, who apparently held that the condition need not persist. The passage concludes by restricting mutawatir to empirical matters (seen or heard) as opposed to rational ones, because reason requires proof rather than testimony.

Key Terms
خبر متواتر (khabar mutawatir): الخبر الذي رواه قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب لكثرتهم وتباين أماكنهم وعدالتهم
تواتر سكوتي (tawatur sukuti): خبر يرويه البعض ويسكت الباقون مع قرائن تدل على موافقتهم، فيفيد العلم
تواتر معنوي (tawatur ma'nawi): أخبار متعددة بألفاظ مختلفة تشترك في حكم واحد بالالتزام، تفيد العلم بذلك الحكم
خبر آحاد (khabar ahad): كل خبر لا يبلغ درجة التواتر، وهو ظني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what is the essential condition for a hadith to be considered mutawatir?
A) The narrators must be from different locations and be upright.
B) The number of narrators must be at least 40.
C) The report must be such that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
D) The report must be transmitted in every generation by at least 10 narrators.

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith produces certain knowledge because the possibility of collusion is rationally impossible, regardless of specific numbers or other conditions.
