Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
15 min
The Mutawatir Report: Definition, Conditions, and Epistemological Certainty
Definition, conditions, and epistemological analysis of mutawatir report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions of a mutawatir report according to Hanafi usul, explain why no specific number of narrators is required, and evaluate the epistemological claim that mutawatir yields necessary certainty.

Core Idea
Mutawatir yields certain knowledge by impossibility of collusion, not by a fixed number.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar defines the mutawatir report and clarifies a common misunderstanding: that a specific number of narrators is required. The Hanafi position is that the condition is the impossibility of collusion, which produces necessary certainty (ilm daruri). The passage also addresses the epistemological dispute with the Mu'tazila and others, defending the immediate certainty of mutawatir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and its definition
The mutawatir report is defined by its effect (necessary knowledge) and condition (impossibility of collusion). Note that no fixed number is required.
The text explicitly states: 'ولم يشترط فيه تعين عدد'.
2
Extract the conditions of tawatur
Conditions are: (a) impossibility of collusion, (b) persistence of that condition in all generations (beginning, middle, end), (c) the report must be based on sensory observation (not pure reason).
The text: 'ويدوم فيه هذا الحد' and 'أن يكون مستنده الأمر المشاهد بالبصر أو المسموع بالسمع'.
3
Understand the classification of reports based on these conditions
If the condition fails in the first generation, the report is ahad (mashhur if spreads later); if it fails in middle or end, it is munqati'.
The text: 'فلو لم يكن في الأول ... فسمي مشهوراً' and 'ولو لم يكن في الأوسط والآخر ... كان منقطعاً'.
4
Analyze the epistemological claim
Hanafis argue that mutawatir yields necessary certainty (ilm daruri) like direct observation, using the analogy of a rope made of hairs. The Mu'tazila say it gives only tranquility (tumaninah), and others say it gives inferential knowledge (istidlali).
The text refutes these opposing views and uses the example of knowing Mecca and Baghdad.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is acceptance of proofs of prophethood and miracles. Rejecting mutawatir's certainty leads to denial of the foundations of religion.
The text: 'الأنبياء ومعجزاتهم لا تثبت إلا بالتواتر فحينئذ لا يثبت العلم ... وهذا كفر'.

باب أقسام السنة
بيان خبر المتواتر
ولم يشترط فيه تعين عدد كما قيل: إنها سبعة وقيل أربعون وقيل: سبعون، بل كل ما يحصل به العلم الضروري فهو من أمارة التواتر.
ويدوم فيه هذا الحد، فيكون آخره كأوّله، وأوّله كآخره، وأوسطه كطرفيه، يعني يستوي جميع الأزمنة من أوّل ما نشأ ذلك الخبر إلى آخر ما بلغ إلى هذا الناقل، فالأول هو زمان ظهور الخبر، والآخر هو زمان كل ناقل يتصوره آخرًا، فلو لم يكن في الأول أي الخبر كذلك كان آحاد الأصل، فسمي مشهوراً إن انتشر في الأوسط والآخر، ولو لم يكن في الأوسط والآخر كذلك كان منقطعًا.
ولم يشترط إلخ لما كان يرد على قول المصنف: "لا يحصى عدهم أن عدم إحصاء عدد الرواة ليس بشرط في المتواتر عند الجمهور، فإنه قد يحصل العلم واليقين بخبر عشرة من الرجال إذا كانوا ثقات عدولاً فالمتواتر ما يكون رواته بحيث لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب وإن كانوا محصورين فالصواب حذف قوله: "لا يُحصى عددهم" فالشارح صرف عنانه إلى توجيه هذا القول؛ فقال: ولم يشترط إلخ إيماء إلى أن المراد منه أنه ليس يشترط في المتواتر تعيين العدد فإن ما ذكر المعتبرون للعدد المعين ليس بشبهة فضلاً أن يكون حجة، وليس المراد منه أن عدم إحصاء عدد الرواة شرط في التواتر كما هو مذهب البعض. (القمر) أنها سبعة قياسًا على غسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب سبع مرات كما ورد في الحديث. (القمر) وقيل: أربعون؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ حَسْبُكَ اللَّهُ وَمَنِ اتَّبَعَكَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾، (الأنفال: ٦٤) وكان المؤمنون في ذلك الزمان أربعين. (القمر) وقيل سبعون لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاخْتَارَ مُوسَى قَوْمَهُ سَبْعِينَ رَجُلاً لِمِيقَاتِنَا (الأعراف: ١٥٥) وقيل: أربعة كعدد شهود الزنا، وقيل: عشرة؛ لأن ما دون العشرة أحاد، وقيل: عشرون؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن يَكُنْ مِنْكُمْ عِشْرُونَ صَابِرُونَ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْنِ (الأنفال : ٦٥) (القمر) ويدوم هذا الحد أي عدم توهم اجتماع الرواة على الكذب، ثم اعلم أن هذا الشرط عند الجمهور خلافًا للجصاص؛ فإن المشهور عنده من المتواتر.(القمر) يستوي فيه أي في هذا الحد، وهو عدم توهم اجتماع الرواة على الكذب والمراد بالاستواء أن لا ينقص الكثرة عن العدد الذي أحالت العادة تواطؤهم على الكذب وليس المراد به أن لا تزيد؛ إذ الزيادة مطلوبة من باب الأولى، وقيل: إنه يشترط أن يكون مستند انتهاء المتواتر الأمر المشاهد بالبصر، أو المسموع بالسمع، لا ما يثبت بالعقل الصرف، فإنه لو اتفق أهل إقليم على مسألة عقلية لم يحصل لنا اليقين بل تطالبهم بالبرهان. (القمر)
ولو لم يكن في الأوسط والآخر كذلك أي منتشر ، وكان في الأول على حد التواتر كان إلخ. (القمر)
بيان خبر المتواتر
باب أقسام السنة كنقل القرآن والصلوات الخمس مثال لمطلق المتواتر دون متواتر السنة؛ لأن في وجود السنة المتواترة اختلافًا، قيل: لم يوجد منها شيء، وقيل: "إنما الأعمال بالنيات وقيل: "البينة على المدعى واليمين على من أنكر". **
أي المتواتر
وأنه يوجب علم اليقين كالعيان علمًا ضروريًا، لا كما يقول المعتزلة: إنه يوجب علم طمأنينة يرجّح جانب الصدق ولا يفيد اليقين، ولا كما يقوله أقوام إنه يوجب علمًا استدلاليًا ينشأ من ملاحظة المقدمات لا ضروريًا؛ وذلك لأن وجود مكة وبغداد أوضح وأجلى من أن يقام عليه دليل يعتري الشك في إثباته، ويحتاج في دفعه إلى مقدمات غامضة ظنية.
الشك
السنة المتواترة: أي بالتواتر اللفظي، وأما السنة المتواترة المعنى فهي كثيرة، ولا اختلاف في وجودها، ومنها حديث المسح على الخفين، رواه سبعون من الصحابة الكبار وهم أجمعين. (القمر) لم يوجد منها شيء ولعله لاشتراط عدم إحصاء عدد الرواة (القمر) وقيل : إنما الأعمال إلخ: هذا حديث مشهور صرّح به الثقات، وقد مر. (القمر) وقيل إلخ وقيل: "من كذب علي متعمدا فليتبوأ مقعده من النار"؛ لأن رواته أزيد من مائة. كذا قال بعض المحدثين. (القمر) يوجب علم اليقين خلافًا للبراهمة فإنهم أنكروا إفادة المتواتر اليقين؛ فإن خبر كل واحد محتمل الكذب وبضم المحتمل إلى المحتمل يزداد الاحتمال قلنا: قد يحصل بالجمع أمر لم يحصل بالواحد كقوة الحبل المؤلّف من الشعرات ليست في شعرة. (القمر كالعيان أي كما يوجب العيان علما يقينيًا. (القمر)
علمًا ضروريًا: فإن هذا العلم يحصل لمن لا يقدر على الكسب وترتيب المقدمات كالصبيان. (القمر) المعتزلة منهم النظام، وردّ قولهم بأن الأنبياء عليا ومعجزاتهم لا تثبت إلا بالتواتر فحينئذ لا يثبت العلم واليقين بنبوتهم، وهذا كفر . (القمر) أقوام منهما أبو بكر الدقاق الشافعية. (القمر) علمًا استدلاليًا بأن تقول: هذا خبر جماعة صادقة وكل ما هذا شأنه فهو صادق، قطعي، ونحن نقول: إن ترتيب المقدمات يكون في البديهي أيضًا، وبهذا لا يكون نظريًا، بل النظري ما يتوقف حصوله عليه، وههنا ليس كذلك من الحصول العلم لمن لا يقدر على الكسب. (القمر) وذلك أي حصول اليقين من المتواتر ضرورةً (القمر)
تخريجه.
** أخرج البيهقي ٢٥٢/١٠، عن ابن عباس ما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: لو يعطى الناس بدعواهم لادعى رجال أموال قوم ودماءهم، ولكن البينة على المدّعي واليمين على من أنكر ، أخرجه أحمد في مسنده" رقم: ۳۱۸۸ ، ومسلم في "صحيحه" رقم: ۱۷۱۱ ، باب اليمين على المدعى عليه، وفيه ولكن اليمين على المدعى عليه، وأخرج الدار قطني في "سننه" عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: البيئة على المدّعي واليمين على من أنكر إلا في القسامة.
عن
Chapter on Divisions of Sunnah. Explanation of the Mutawatir Report. And a specific number is not required for it, as it is said: it is seven, and it is said: forty, and it is said: seventy. Rather, everything that produces necessary knowledge is a sign of tawatur. And this condition (of impossibility of collusion) persists throughout, so its end is like its beginning, its beginning like its end, and its middle like its two extremes. That is, all times are equal from the first emergence of that report to the last transmission to the current narrator. The first is the time of the report's appearance, and the last is the time of each narrator who conceives it as last. So if it was not like that in the first (i.e., the report), it is ahad in origin, and is called mashhur if it spread in the middle and the end. And if it was not like that in the middle and the end, it is munqati'. [Commentary continues with discussion of conditions, various opinions on numbers, and then the epistemological status of mutawatir, stating it yields necessary certainty like direct observation, refuting the Mu'tazila who say it yields only tranquility, and others who say it yields inferential knowledge. Examples of mutawatir sunnah are given, including the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' and 'The burden of proof is on the claimant.' The text also criticizes the Brahmins who deny certainty from mutawatir.]
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage defines the mutawatir hadith and its conditions. The author begins by stating that a specific number of narrators is not required; rather, whatever produces necessary certainty (al-ilm al-daruri) is a sign of tawatur. The condition of impossibility of collusion on a lie must persist in all generations. If the report lacks that condition in the first generation, it is ahad in origin and becomes mashhur if it spreads later; if it lacks it in the middle or later, it is munqati'. The commentary clarifies that the text corrects an earlier statement that mutawatir requires an uncountable number. In fact, the condition is that the narrators be such that collusion is impossible, even if they are limited in number. Various opinions on the minimum number (seven, forty, seventy, etc.) are given with supports from Quran and hadith, but the author dismisses these as not authoritative. A second condition is that the source of mutawatir must be sensory (seen or heard), not rational, because rational matters require proof. The passage then addresses the existence of mutawatir sunnah: some deny any exists, but examples like 'Actions are but by intentions' and 'The burden of proof is on the claimant' are cited, though the latter is actually mashhur. Mutawatir in meaning is abundant, e.g., the hadith on wiping over khuffs. Finally, the passage asserts that mutawatir yields necessary certainty (ilm al-yaqin) like direct observation, refuting the Mu'tazila (who say it gives only tranquility) and others (like the Brahmins) who deny certainty. The argument uses the analogy of a rope made of individual hairs: the combined strength exceeds that of a single hair. This knowledge is daruri because it occurs even to those incapable of reasoning, like children.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report with such numerous narrators in every generation that collusion on a lie is impossible, producing necessary certainty.
العلم الضروري (al-ilm al-daruri): Knowledge that is immediate and unavoidable, like sensory perception, not dependent on reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition of mutawatir according to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage?
A) The narrators must be more than 100.
B) The report must be based on sensory observation (seen or heard).
C) The report must be transmitted in every generation by at least 40 narrators.
D) The report must be transmitted by both Shia and Sunni narrators.

Key Takeaway
The mutawatir report is defined by the impossibility of collusion across all generations, yielding necessary certainty like direct observation, and no fixed number of narrators is required.

Mutawatir: Definition and Certainty
definition and defense of mutawatir's certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir and explain why it yields necessary certain knowledge (ilm dharuri) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mutawatir yields necessary certain knowledge, not mere probability.

This passage defines mutawatir khabar and establishes its epistemic status. The Hanafi school argues that mutawatir produces certain knowledge (علم اليقين) directly, akin to sense perception. This refutes claims by the Mu'tazila and others that it provides only probability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and conditions of mutawatir
Locate where the text defines mutawatir, typically as a report narrated by a number that cannot conspire on falsehood in every generation.
Examples: Quran, five daily prayers.
2
Understand the epistemological claim: necessary knowledge (ilm dharuri)
Recognize that Hanafis classify the knowledge from mutawatir as necessary, intuitive, not requiring inference.
Contrast with 'ilm istidlali (inferential knowledge).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: analogies and refutations
Examine the rope-from-hairs analogy and the argument that rejecting mutawatir would undermine prophethood.
The text also cites impossibility of conspiracy among many narrators.
4
Compare with opposing views
Identify the Mu'tazila view (tama'ninah) and the Brahmin view (probability). Note their flawed reasoning.
Also mentions a Shafi'i group claiming inferential knowledge.
5
Note the consequence: rejecting mutawatir leads to kufr
Understand that denying the certainty of mutawatir would undercut the proofs for prophethood and the Quran, thus becoming apostasy.
This shows the high stakes of this usul position.

Section on the divisions of the Sunna. Explanation of mutawatir khabar. Like the transmission of the Quran and the five daily prayers is an example of absolute mutawatir, not the mutawatir of the Sunna; because concerning the existence of the mutawatir Sunna there is disagreement. It is said: none of it exists, and it was said: 'Deeds are by intentions' and it was said: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies.' ** That is, the mutawatir, and that it necessitates certain knowledge like direct observation, necessary knowledge, not as the Mu'tazila say: it necessitates knowledge of tranquility that gives weight to the side of truth and does not yield certainty, nor as a group say: it necessitates inferential knowledge arising from consideration of premises, not necessary. That is because the existence of Mecca and Baghdad is clearer and more obvious than to need a proof that admits doubt in establishing it and requires obscure speculative premises to remove that doubt. The doubt. The mutawatir Sunna: meaning by verbal tawatur. As for the mutawatir Sunna in meaning, it is abundant, and there is no disagreement concerning its existence. Among it is the hadith of wiping over the leather socks, narrated by seventy of the great Companions, and they all agree. (al-Qamar) 'None of it exists' perhaps due to the condition of not counting the number of narrators? (al-Qamar) And it was said: 'Deeds are by intentions' etc.: this is a famous hadith declared authentic by trustworthy scholars, and it has passed. (al-Qamar) And it was said: 'Whoever deliberately lies about me, let him take his seat in Hellfire' because its narrators are more than one hundred. Thus said some hadith scholars. (al-Qamar) It necessitates certain knowledge contrary to the Brahmins, for they denied that mutawatir yields certainty. For each individual report is possibly false, and combining the possible with the possible increases possibility. We say: something may be obtained from the combination that is not obtained from the single, like the strength of a rope made of hairs is not in a single hair. (al-Qamar) Like direct observation: i.e., as direct observation yields certain knowledge. (al-Qamar) Necessary knowledge: for this knowledge occurs to one who is not capable of acquisition and arranging premises, like children. (al-Qamar) The Mu'tazila, among them al-Nazzam, and his statement is refuted by the fact that the prophets, peace be upon them, and their miracles are only established through tawatur; then knowledge and certainty of their prophethood would not be established, and this is kufr. (al-Qamar) A group, among them Abu Bakr al-Daqqaq al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar) Inferential knowledge: by saying: this is a report of a truthful group, and everything of this nature is truthful, conclusive. And we say: arranging premises occurs also in the intuitive, and by this it is not theoretical. Rather, theoretical is that which depends on it for its occurrence, and here it is not like that. The occurrence of knowledge to one who is not capable of acquisition. (al-Qamar) That is, the occurrence of certainty from mutawatir is necessary. (al-Qamar) Its takhrij. ** Al-Bayhaqi 10/252, from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him said: 'If people were to be given whatever they claim, men would claim the wealth and blood of others, but the burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies.' Ahmad in his Musnad no. 3188, and Muslim in his Sahih no. 1711, chapter of oath on the defendant, and in it: 'but the oath is on the defendant.' And al-Daraqutni in his Sunan from Amr ibn Shuayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him said: 'The evidence is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies, except in the case of qasama.'
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage defines mutawatir (متواتر) khabar. The text begins by stating that mutawatir is like the transmission of the Quran and the five daily prayers—these are examples of absolute mutawatir. However, there is disagreement on whether any part of the Sunna is mutawatir in wording. Some say none exists; others cite hadiths like 'Deeds are by intentions' and 'The burden of proof is on the claimant' as possible examples. The author then clarifies that mutawatir yields certain knowledge (علم اليقين) directly, like seeing something with one's own eyes. This is a necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) that does not require reflection. The text refutes three opposing views: (1) The Mu'tazila claim that mutawatir only gives tranquility (طمأنينة), a strong probability but not certainty. (2) The Brahmins argue that each individual report is possibly false, so combining them only increases probability, not certainty. The Hanafi response uses the analogy of a rope made of hairs: the combined strength is not found in any single hair. (3) A group, including some Shafi'is, claim that mutawatir yields inferential knowledge (استدلالي) requiring premises. The author responds that even intuitive knowledge involves premises implicitly; theoretical knowledge requires explicit deduction. Since mutawatir knowledge occurs even to children, it is necessary, not inferential. The text also notes that rejecting the certainty of mutawatir would undermine the proof of prophethood, thus amounting to kufr. Finally, the takhrij (source citation) of the hadith 'al-bayyinah ala al-muddai' is given as an example of a hadith that some consider mutawatir.

Key Terms
خبر متواتر (khabar mutawatir): A report transmitted by a multitude in each generation such that it is impossible for them to agree upon a falsehood.
علم ضروري (ilm dharuri): Knowledge that occurs necessarily without reflection or inference.
طمأنينة (tama'ninah): Tranquility/strong probability, not full certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of knowledge does mutawatir produce according to the Hanafi school?
A) Speculative knowledge (zann)
B) Necessary certain knowledge (ilm dharuri)
C) Tranquility (tama'ninah)
D) Inferential knowledge (istidlali)

Key Takeaway
According to Hanafi usul, mutawatir yields necessary certain knowledge, and rejecting this leads to kufr.

Defining Mashhur Khabar: From Ahad to Widespread
Defines mashhur khabar with conditions and contrasts with hadith scholar taxonomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mashhur khabar according to Hanafi usul scholars, identify its three conditions (originally ahad, spread to a group impossible to conspire, restricted to second/third generations), and distinguish it from the hadith scholar classification.

Core Idea
Mashhur is a report that started as ahad but became widely transmitted by a group impossible to conspire on falsehood.

In the Hanafi usul tradition, not all widely-known reports are mutawatir. The category of mashhur occupies a critical middle ground: it began as a solitary report in the Companions' generation but later gained widespread transmission in the Followers' generation. Understanding its precise definition – including the temporal boundaries and the condition that the later transmitters must be beyond collusion – is essential for evaluating the epistemic weight of such reports. This lesson unpacks that definition with the full commentary from our text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the temporal origin
Confirm that the report was originally narrated by only one or a few Companions (ahad) in the first generation. If it had tawatur from the start, it is mutawatir, not mashhur.
The text says: 'مما كان من الآحاد في الأصل، أي في القرن الأول'.
2
Verify the spread condition
Check that in the second or third generation, the report was transmitted by a group so large that it is impossible to imagine they conspired on a falsehood. The group must be sufficient to prevent collusion.
The condition is 'حتى ينقله قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب'.
3
Apply the generational boundary
Note that only fame achieved in the second and third generations (Followers and Followers of the Followers) counts. Fame after the third generation is disregarded because falsehood becomes more common later.
The text states: 'ولا اعتبار للشهرة بعد ذلك فإن عامة أخبار الآحاد قد اشتهرت في هذا الزمان'.
4
Distinguish from hadith scholar classification
Recognize that hadith scholars define mashhur differently: within khabar wahid, if each level has at least three narrators it is mashhur; two is 'aziz; one is ghareeb. This is a classification of chains, not a condition of original ahad status.
The author quotes al-Nukhba: 'إن كان له أسانيد محصورة بما فوق الاثنين فهو المشهور'.

Section on the divisions of the Sunna. Explanation of the mashhur khabar. Or its chain has a formal ambiguity, i.e., due to the lack of tawatur in the first generation even if that meaning does not remain. Explanation of mashhur khabar] Like mashhur: it is what was originally ahad, i.e., in the first generation, which is the generation of the Companions with it, then it spread until it is transmitted by a group that cannot be imagined to conspire on falsehood, and that is the second generation and those after them, meaning the generation of the Followers and the Followers of the Followers. There is no consideration for fame after that, for most ahad reports have become famous in this time, so nothing remains of them as ahad. And that it necessitates knowledge of tranquility, i.e., reassurance that gives weight to the side of truth, so it is below mutawatir and above the solitary report. Its level. 'Or its chain has' etc. is in the accusative, conjuncted to 'its chain has' in the accusative in the phrase 'either its chain has etc.' (al-Qamar) 'Even if that meaning does not remain' etc. due to the agreement of the second generation and those after them to accept it and act upon it. And 'generation' is the people of every period in which there is a prophet, or in which there is knowledge, whether the years are few or many. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'It is what was originally ahad': i.e., its narration from the Companions is less than the number of tawatur, whether its narrator is one or more. This is according to the usul scholars. As for the hadith scholars, the Sunna is divided into two: mutawatir, which has many chains without a specific number such that it is impossible for them to conspire on falsehood; and solitary report (khabar wahid), which is not like that. If it has chains limited to more than two, i.e., its narrators in every level of its chain are not less than three, then it is mashhur. If it has chains limited to two, i.e., its narrators in a level are two, then it is 'aziz. If it has chains limited to one, i.e., its narrators in a level are one, then it is ghareeb. Thus in al-Nukhba and its commentary. (al-Qamar) 'Until it is transmitted by a group' etc.: the word 'group' is general indicating that if a report is transmitted by one Companion from the Prophet, peace be upon him, then it spreads until a group from the first generation that cannot be imagined to conspire on falsehood transmits it, then it is also mashhur. (al-Qamar) 'There is no consideration' etc. because after that, falsehood spreads after the three generations, and from here the reason for the author inserting his statement 'the second generation and those after them' becomes clear. (al-Qamar) 'So nothing remains of them as ahad': they become mashhur even though they are not called mashhur, and it is not permissible to add them to the Book. (al-Qamar) 'And that it necessitates knowledge' etc., i.e., insofar as it is a mashhur report. If the report is mashhur and consensus occurs on it, and the consensus is transmitted to us by tawatur, then it yields certainty, but not by virtue of being mashhur, rather by the accompanying consensus; so there is no problem. (al-Qamar) 'i.e., reassurance that gives weight' etc.: i.e., a strong weighting, so the possibility of the narrator's lying remains, although the possibility of error is extremely unlikely, as if that possibility does not exist, because its people shun the stain of lying, meaning that the preponderant is =
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage defines mashhur (مشهور) khabar. The text explains that mashhur is originally an ahad (individual) report in the first generation (the Companions), but then becomes widespread in the second and third generations (the Followers and their Followers) such that it is transmitted by a group that cannot be imagined to conspire on falsehood. It is below mutawatir in certainty but above a solitary report. The text notes that fame after the third generation is not considered because falsehood spreads later. It also distinguishes between the definition of usul scholars and hadith scholars. According to hadith scholars, the Sunna is divided into mutawatir (many chains) and khabar wahid (one chain). Within khabar wahid, if the number of narrators in each level is three or more, it is mashhur; if two, it is 'aziz; if one, it is ghareeb. The text further clarifies that mashhur yields knowledge of tranquility (اطمينان), i.e., a strong probability of truth, but not absolute certainty. However, if consensus (ijma) occurs on the content of a mashhur report, then it yields certainty due to the consensus, not due to the report itself. The commentator (al-Qamar) adds that the possibility of the narrator lying is extremely remote, as the reporters are known for their integrity.

Key Terms
خبر مشهور (khabar mashhur): A report that was ahad in the first generation (sahaba) but later became widely transmitted in the second and third generations.
آحاد (ahad): A report that does not reach the level of tawatur; in this context, any report narrated by less than the number that would constitute tawatur.
قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب (qoum la yutawahhamu tawatu'uhum 'ala al-kadhib): A group impossible to conspire on falsehood, i.e., sufficiently large and trustworthy that collusion is rationally impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the distinguishing feature of a mashhur hadith according to the Hanafi usul definition in this passage?
A) It has a continuous chain of narrators in every generation
B) It was initially narrated by one or few in the first generation but later became widely transmitted
C) Its narrators are all trustworthy
D) It is considered equivalent to mutawatir

Key Takeaway
Mashhur khabar is defined by its historical trajectory: it begins as ahad in the first generation and becomes widespread in the second or third generation, transmitted by a group that cannot conspire on falsehood.

The Epistemic Weight of Mashhur: Knowledge of Tranquility
Explains epistemic value of mashhur as tranquility, contrasts with mutawatir and ahad, and notes exception with ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that mashhur yields knowledge of tranquility (ilm tama'ninah), contrast its epistemic value with mutawatir (certainty) and ahad (speculation), and identify the exception when consensus (ijma) adds certainty.

Core Idea
Mashhur gives strong probability but not absolute certainty unless supported by ijma.

Knowing that a report is mashhur is not enough; we must understand what kind of knowledge it produces. The Hanafi school assigns mashhur an intermediate epistemic status: it creates tranquility (tama'ninah) in the heart, a strong weighting toward truth, but leaves a remote possibility of error. This lesson unpacks that concept and shows how it differs from the certainty of mutawatir and the mere probability of a solitary report.

Guided Path
1
Understand the epistemic scale
Recognize that reports are ranked: mutawatir yields 'ilm al-yaqin (certain knowledge), mashhur yields ilm tama'ninah (tranquil knowledge), and ahad yields zann (speculative probability). Mashhur is below mutawatir and above ahad.
The text says: 'فهو دون المتواتر وفوق الواحد'.
2
Define 'ilm tama'ninah
Tranquility is a psychological state of strong conviction, not absolute certainty. It is based on the improbability of the narrators colluding in falsehood. The possibility of error remains but is extremely unlikely.
Commentary: 'اطمينان يرجّح جهة الصدق ترجيحا قويًا، فيكون فيه احتمال كذب الراوي، وإن كان خطأ احتمالا مرجوحًا غاية المرجوحية'.
3
Identify the exception with ijma
If a mashhur report is accompanied by consensus (ijma) of the scholars, and that consensus is transmitted to us by tawatur, then the report yields certainty. However, this certainty comes from the ijma, not from the mashhur status itself.
The text: 'ولو كان الخبر مشهورًا، ووقع الإجماع عليه، ونقل الإجماع إلينا بالتواتر فهو يفيد اليقين، لكن لا من حيث أنه خبر مشهور، بل بعارض الإجماع'.
4
Evaluate practical implications
A mashhur report without ijma is binding for action (wajib al-'amal) but does not establish creedal certainty. In fiqh, it can be used to establish rulings but not to establish matters of faith beyond doubt.
This is an inference from the epistemic status; the passage does not explicitly state this but it is a standard Hanafi position.

Commentary
This passage defines mashhur (مشهور) khabar. Key Terms
علم طمأنينة (ilm tama'ninah): Knowledge that brings about strong probability and tranquility of the heart, but not absolute certainty.
يقين (yaqin): Absolute certainty, produced by mutawatir reports and by mashhur reports only when accompanied by ijma.
ظن (zann): Speculative probability, produced by ahad reports.

Mashhur yields ilm tama'ninah (tranquility), a strong probability below certainty, which can be elevated to certainty only if accompanied by ijma transmitted by tawatur.

Khabar Mashhur: Definition and Epistemological Status
Defining khabar mashhur and its epistemological weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar mashhur according to Hanafi usul, identify its epistemological weight ('ilm al-tuma'nina), and distinguish it from mutawatir and ahad.

Core Idea
Khabar mashhur yields tranquility, not certainty; its denier is misguided, not a disbeliever.

In Hanafi usul, reports from the Prophet are classified by their transmission patterns and epistemological strength. One key category is khabar mashhur (the famous report), which sits between mutawatir (massively transmitted) and khabar wahid (solitary). This lesson unpacks its definition, how it arises, and what kind of knowledge it produces. Understanding this category is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists weigh evidence and justify rulings like adding restrictions to the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining features of khabar mashhur
From the passage, note that khabar mashhur is originally ahad (solitary) in the first generation (Companions), then spreads in the second and third generations (Tabi'un and Atba' al-Tabi'in) to the point where collusion on falsehood is inconceivable. This is its key characteristic.
It is not defined by a specific number of narrators, but by the pattern of transmission over time.
2
Determine its epistemological status
The passage states that khabar mashhur yields 'ilm al-tuma'nina (knowledge of tranquility) — a strong preponderance of truth that gives confidence but not absolute certainty. Compare this to mutawatir (yaqin) and ahad (zann).
'Ilm al-tuma'nina is a distinctive Hanafi category; it obligates action but does not reach the level of certainty required for creedal matters like takfir.
3
Contrast with other report categories
Mutawatir gives certainty (yaqin) and its denier is a disbeliever. Ahad gives speculation (zann) and is not sufficient for adding to the Quran. Khabar mashhur is in between: it allows addition to the Quran but its denier is only misguided, not a disbeliever.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi hierarchy of proofs.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute with al-Jassas
Al-Jassas considered khabar mashhur a type of mutawatir and argued it gives yaqin. The majority Hanafi position disagrees, relying on its ahad origin. The passage sides with the majority: 'on the soundest view, its denier is not declared a disbeliever, but is misguided.'
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is the ruling on takfir of the denier.
5
Apply the definition to a real example
Consider the hadith on wiping over khuffs (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). It was reported by a few Companions initially, then became widely transmitted in the next generations. According to the passage, this qualifies as khabar mashhur and can be used to restrict the Quranic wudu verse.
This shows how khabar mashhur functions as a proof in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب أقسام السنة
٥٠٢
بيان خبر المشهور
أو يكون اتصالاً فيه شبهة صورة أي من حيث عدم تواتره في القرن الأول وإن لم يبق ذلك معنى. بيان خبر المشهور]
كالمشهور، وهو ما كان من الآحاد في الأصل، أي في القرن الأول، وهو قرن الصحابة معها، ثم انتشر حتى ينقله قوم لايتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب، وهو القرن الثاني ومن بعدهم يعني قرن التابعين وتبع التابعين ولا اعتبار للشهرة بعد ذلك فإن عامة أخبار الآحاد قد اشتهرت في هذا الزمان فلم يبق شيء منها آحادًا، وأنه يوجب علم طمأنينة أي اطمينان يرجّح جهة الصدق فهو دون المتواتر وفوق الواحد،
طبقه
أو يكون إلخ بالنصب عطف على "يكون المنصوب في قوله: إما إن يكون إلخ. (القمر) وإن لم يبق إلخ لاتفاق القرن الثاني ومن بعدهم على قبوله والعمل به، والقرن أهل كل مدة كان فيها نبي، أو فيها من العلم، قلت السنون أو كثرت كذا قيل. (القمر) وهو ما كان من الآحاد في الأصل: أي كان رواية من الصحابة له أقل من عدد التواتر واحدا كان راويه أو أكثر، وهذا على رأي الأصوليين، وأما على رأي أهل الحديث فالسنة قسمان متواتر وهو ما يكون له أسانيد كثيرة بلا حصر عدد معين والعادة أحالت تواطؤهم على الكذب وخبر واحد وهو ما لا يكون كذلك، فإن كان له أسانيد محصورة بما فوق الاثنين، أي لا يكون رواته في كل مرتبة في سنده أقل من ثلاثة فهو المشهور، وإن كان له أسانيد محصورة بالاثنين أي يكون رواته في مرتبة من المراتب اثنين فهو العزيز، وإن كان له أسانيد محصورة بواحد أي يكون رواته في مرتبة من المراتب واحدًا فهو الغريب كذا في "النخبة" وشرحها.(القمر) حتى ينقله قوم إلخ : عمّم القوم إيماء إلى أن الخبر لو نقله واحد من الصحابة صح عن النبي عليه، ثم انتشر حتى نـ قوم من القرن الأول لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب فهو أيضًا مشهور (القمر) ولا اعتبار إلخ فإنه عليها أخبر: يفشو الكذب بعد القرون الثلاثة، ومن ههنا ظهر وجه إقحام المصنف له قوله : هو القرن الثاني ومن بعدهم. (القمر) فلم يبق شيء منها آحادًا: فتصير مشهورة مع أنها لا تسمى مشهورة ، ولا يجوز الزيادة بها على الكتاب. (القمر) وأنه يوجب علم إلخ أي من حيث أنه خبر مشهور، ولو كان الخبر مشهورًا، ووقع الإجماع عليه، ونقل الإجماع إلينا بالتواتر فهو يفيد اليقين، لكن لا من حيث أنه خبر مشهور ، بل بعارض الإجماع؛ فلا ضير فيه. (القمر) أي اطمينان يرجّح إلخ : أي ترجيحا قويًا، فيكون فيه احتمال كذب الراوي، وإن كان خطأ احتمالا مرجوحًا غاية المرجوحية كأنه ليس ذلك الاحتمال؛ لأن أصحابه للتنزهوا عن وصمة الكذب بمعنى أن الغالب الراجح =  حتى جازت الزيادة به على كتاب الله تعالى، ولا يكفّر جاحده، بل يضلل على الأصح. وقال الجصاص: إنه أحد قسمي المتواتر، فيفيد علم اليقين ويكفّر جاحده كالمتواتر على ما مرّ.
Chapter on Divisions of Sunnah. Explanation of the Famous Report: Or it has a connection with a formal uncertainty, meaning due to its non-mutawatir status in the first generation, even if that does not remain in meaning. Explanation of the Famous Report: Like the famous report, which is what was originally a solitary report, i.e., in the first generation, which is the generation of the Companions, then it spread until it is transmitted by a group whose collusion on falsehood is not conceivable, and that is the second generation and those after them, meaning the generation of the Followers and the Followers of the Followers. No consideration is given to fame after that, for most solitary reports have become famous in this time, so nothing remains solitary. And it necessitates 'ilm al-tuma'nina, i.e., tranquility that gives preponderance to the side of truthfulness, so it is below mutawatir and above solitary. Explanation of 'like the famous report'... (continues with commentary from al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage defines khabar mashhur (the famous report) according to Hanafi usul. It begins by distinguishing it from mutawatir and ahad. Khabar mashhur is originally ahad in the first generation (Companions), but then becomes widely transmitted in the second and third generations (Followers and their Followers) such that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable. The text notes that fame after these generations is irrelevant because most ahad reports have become widespread. The epistemological status of khabar mashhur is that it yields 'ilm al-tuma'nina (knowledge of tranquility), which is a strong preponderance of truth but not absolute certainty; it is below mutawatir (which gives yaqin) and above khabar wahid (which gives zann). The commentary from al-Qamar elaborates on the definition, contrasts it with the terminology of hadith scholars (where mashhur requires at least three chains), and discusses the ruling that a denier of khabar mashhur is not declared a disbeliever but is misguided. Al-Jassas's opinion that khabar mashhur is a type of mutawatir and thus gives certainty is mentioned but not adopted; the text maintains that it only gives tuma'nina unless supported by consensus.

Key Terms
خبر المشهور (khabar mashhur): A report that was originally ahad in the first generation (Companions), then became widely transmitted in the second and third generations such that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
علم الطمأنينة (‘ilm al-ṭuma'nīna): Knowledge of tranquility; a strong preponderance of truth that gives confidence but not absolute certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the epistemological status of khabar mashhur according to the majority of Hanafi scholars?
A) It yields 'ilm al-yaqin (certainty) and its denier is a disbeliever.
B) It yields 'ilm al-tuma'nina (tranquility) and its denier is not a disbeliever but is misguided.
C) It yields zann (speculation) and its denier is a disbeliever.
D) It yields 'ilm al-yaqin but its denier is only a sinner.

Key Takeaway
Khabar mashhur is an epistemological category between mutawatir and ahad, yielding tranquility (tuma'nina) and allowing addition to the Quran, but its denier is not declared a disbeliever.

Khabar Wahid: Definition and Acceptance
Definition and conditions of khabar wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar wahid, identify its position in the Hanafi hierarchy, and explain why the number of narrators is not a condition for its acceptance.

Core Idea
Khabar wahid binds in action, not in creed; its denier is mistaken, not a disbeliever.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar clarifies the essential concept of khabar al-wahid (solitary report). It distinguishes it from mashhur and mutawatir, addresses the Mu'tazilite objection that two narrators are needed, and explains the epistemological weight: khabar wahid yields zann (speculation) and must be acted upon, but its denier is not a disbeliever. Understanding this definition is foundational for Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition
Locate the passage's definition: khabar wahid is any report narrated by one, two, or more that does not reach the level of mashhur or mutawatir in the three virtuous generations.
The text emphasizes that number alone does not remove it from being solitary.
2
Analyze the Number Condition
Notice the explicit rejection of number as a condition ('la 'ibra lil-'adad'). The text refutes al-Jubba'i, who required two narrators for religious matters.
Hanafis accept a single trustworthy narrator; the key is that the report remains below mashhur.
3
Determine the Epistemological Outcome
Recognize that khabar wahid yields zann (speculation), not certainty. It obligates action but does not make its denier a disbeliever, unlike mutawatir.
Denial is only a mistake (khata') or misguidance (dalal), not kufr.
4
Place in the Hierarchy
Compare khabar wahid with mashhur (yields tuma'nina/assurance) and mutawatir (yields certainty). Note that addition to the Quran is allowed only via mashhur, not wahid.
This hierarchy determines legal weight and consequences of rejection.

Source Text

Or it has a connection with uncertainty in both form and meaning because it did not become famous in any of the three generations that were testified to be the best. Explanation of the Solitary Report: Like the solitary report, which is every report narrated by one or two or more. He said that in response to one who distinguished between them and said that the report of two is accepted but not the report of one. There is no consideration of number in it after it is below the famous and mutawatir, meaning in the three generations when its narrators did not reach the limit of famous and mutawatir, so no consideration after that of any number; because all are equal in that number does not remove it from being solitary. ... (continues with commentary from al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage defines khabar al-wahid (solitary report). It is any report that is narrated by one, two, or more people but does not reach the level of mashhur or mutawatir. The text refutes the Mu'tazilite al-Jubba'i who argued that a report from two narrators is accepted but not from one. According to Hanafis, number alone does not matter as long as the report remains below mashhur. The commentary explains that khabar wahid yields zann (speculation) unless it gains acceptance that raises it to tuma'nina. It cannot be used to add to the Quran text (unlike mashhur) nor does it necessitate takfir of its denier. The denier of khabar wahid is only considered mistaken, not a disbeliever, because he may be rejecting the opinion of scholars, not directly denying the Prophet. The passage also reiterates that khabar mashhur is superior to khabar wahid, and that khabar mutawatir is above both.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A report that does not meet the conditions of mutawatir or mashhur; narrated by one or more but remaining below those categories in the three virtuous generations.
زيادة على الكتاب (ziyāda ‘alā al-kitāb): Adding a restriction or specification to the Quran based on khabar wahid (not allowed) or khabar mashhur (allowed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, what is the ruling on accepting a report narrated by a single trustworthy person for religious matters?
A) It is not accepted; at least two narrators are required.
B) It is accepted, and number is not a condition for acceptance.
C) It is accepted only if it is also transmitted by the majority.
D) It is accepted only for worldly matters, not religious.

Key Takeaway
Khabar wahid is a solitary report that does not reach mashhur or mutawatir; it is accepted and binding for practice, but its denier is not a disbeliever.

Definition and Status of Khabar al-Wahid
Defining khabar al-wahid and its classification in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar al-wahid, distinguish it from mashhur and mutawatir, and state the Hanafi ruling on its acceptance and the status of its denier.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid obligates action but not certainty; its denier is astray, not a disbeliever.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines the third category of Sunnah: khabar al-wahid. Understanding its precise definition and epistemological weight is crucial for Hanafi usul, because it determines whether a report can add to the Quran or how we treat those who reject it. The author clarifies why number alone does not elevate a report, and explains the practical consequences of classifying a hadith as ahad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of Sunnah
The passage presupposes mutawatir and mashhur; khabar al-wahid is the third. Note that mashhur is between mutawatir and ahad.
The hadith 'Khair al-qurun qarni' establishes the criterion of the first three generations.
2
Define khabar al-wahid precisely
Khabar al-wahid is any report narrated by one or more narrators that did not reach the level of tawatur or shuhrah in the first three generations.
Number alone does not matter once it is below that level.
3
Apply the definitional criteria
The key is not the number of narrators in later generations, but the absence of widespread transmission in the first three generations.
If it became widespread in the second or third generation, it becomes mashhur.
4
Distinguish the epistemological status
Khabar al-wahid produces zann (speculation) not yaqin (certainty). Therefore its denier is not a kafir but is considered dall (astray).
Denying mutawatir is kufr because it rejects definitive proof.
5
Note the dispute with al-Jubba'i
Al-Jubba'i required two narrators for acceptance. The Hanafis accept a single narrator. The Hanafi response: religious matters are more important, so single narration suffices.
This dispute shows the thamarah al-khilaf: accepting hadiths from single Companions.

Chapter on Divisions of the Sunnah. Statement of Khabar al-Wahid: Such that increase upon the Book of Allah is permitted by it, and its denier is not declared a disbeliever, but is declared astray according to the most correct view. Al-Jassas said: It is one of the two types of mutawatir, thus it yields certain knowledge and its denier is a disbeliever like mutawatir as previously. Or its chain has a semblance in form and meaning because it was not widespread in any of the three generations that were testified to as being the best. Abu Bakr. Statement of Khabar al-Wahid: Like khabar al-wahid, which is every report narrated by one or two or more. He said this in response to one who differentiated between them and said: The report of two is accepted but not that of one. And there is no consideration of number in it once it is below the level of mashhur and mutawatir, meaning in the three generations, since its narrators did not reach the level of mashhur and mutawatir; so thereafter no consideration is given to whatever number it may be, because all are equal in that it does not remove it from being ahad. Or increased. That is the hadith. From their state of truthfulness, so suspicion is obtained by mere transmission from the Prophet, then increase and preference occur by the report entering the limit of tawatur in the other two generations, causing tranquility. In al-Da'ir: Tranquility is knowledge by which the soul is at ease, and one thinks it certain, but would not be at ease if one reflected deeply. (al-Qamar) Such that increase is permitted etc., by restricting the absolute of the Book with the mashhur report, for example restricting the fasting of expiation for an oath to consecutiveness by Ibn Mas'ud's reading; because it is like mutawatir in meaning due to acceptance by the two generations, and it is not permitted to abrogate the text of the Quran with it due to its lower rank in form because of the semblance in form. (al-Qamar) And its denier is not declared a disbeliever because it is ahad in origin and has a semblance in form, so in denying it there is only an error of the people of the second and third centuries, not a lie against the Messenger, and erring of scholars is sin and misguidance, not disbelief, unlike mutawatir, for its denier is a disbeliever because in denying it there is a lie against the Messenger. So the mashhur report is below it, and increase by ahad reports upon the Book is not permitted, for it is above it and yields certain knowledge but not necessarily, rather by inference. (al-Qamar) And its denier is declared a disbeliever because the ummah received it with acceptance, and they are just and pious, so it is like mutawatir. (al-Qamar) As previously, i.e. in the section on definition of Quran (al-Qamar). And meaning: where the ummah did not receive it with acceptance. [Fath al-Ghaffar 272] From the three generations: i.e. the generation of the Companions, Allah be pleased with them, which is his generation, and the generation of the Followers, and the generation of their Followers, may Allah be pleased with them all. (al-Qamar) Testified etc.: 'Ali said: The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them. (al-Qamar) Like the hadith of the one who added is omitted, and the estimated phrase is: like the connection of khabar al-wahid, so that the example matches the exemplified. (al-Qamar) For one who differentiated etc., and he is al-Jubba'i from the Mu'tazila. (al-Qamar) Accepts etc. because matters of religion are more important than transactions, so they are more deserving of requiring number in them. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage defines khabar al-wahid and clarifies its epistemological and legal status. The author distinguishes it from mutawatir and mashhur. Khabar al-wahid is a report by one or more narrators that does not reach the level of widespread transmission in the first three generations, which were the best generations as per the hadith. Such a report obligates action (yujibu al-'amal) but does not produce certainty (la yufidu al-yaqin). The Hanafi position is that its denier is not declared a disbeliever (la yukaffar) but is considered astray (yudallal), because denying it involves rejecting the consensus of the second and third generations, not directly denying the Messenger. This contrasts with mutawatir, whose denier is a disbeliever. The text also rejects al-Jassas's view that khabar al-wahid is a type of mutawatir. There is a dispute with the Mu'tazilite al-Jubba'i, who accepted reports from two but not from one; the Hanafis respond that number is irrelevant once it is below the level of tawatur. The example of restricting the absolute of the Book with a mashhur report (like the consecutiveness of fasting in expiation for an oath from Ibn Mas'ud's qira'ah) shows that mashhur can add to the Quran but cannot abrogate its text due to its lower rank in form.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report narrated by one or more narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur or mashhur in the first three generations.
المشهور (al-mashhur): A report that became widespread in the second or third generation but not in the first; it is below mutawatir but above ahad.
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report narrated by so many narrators at each level that collusion on falsehood is impossible, producing certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of a person who denies a khabar al-wahid that has been accepted by the ummah?
A) He is declared a disbeliever (kafir) because he rejects the Sunnah.
B) He is declared astray (dall) but not a disbeliever.
C) He is considered a sinner (fasiq) but no further action.
D) He is treated as a hypocrite (munafiq).

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-wahid is defined by its absence of widespread transmission in the first three generations; it obligates action but not certainty, so its denier is astray, not a disbeliever.

Quranic Evidence for Khabar al-Wahid: Analysis of Ayah 9:122
Derivation of khabar al-wahid's obligation from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of istinbat to derive the obligation of acting upon khabar al-wahid from Quran 9:122, identifying the textual categories (amm, etc.) and the reasoning steps.

Core Idea
The command to warn (ta'ifa) and to accept the warning (firqa) in 9:122 proves khabar al-wahid obligates action.

This passage presents the primary Quranic proof for the hujjiyyah (authoritativeness) of khabar al-wahid. The verse at-Tawbah 9:122 is analyzed in detail, with attention to pronoun references and the meaning of 'ta'ifa' to show that a report from a single person can be binding. As a Hanafi usul student, you will learn how this verse is categorized as 'amm' and how the derivation progresses through takhsis and bayan to reach the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary text
Locate the Quranic verse (9:122) cited in the passage. Note that it is the core evidence for khabar al-wahid's authority.
The verse is quoted in full in the source.
2
Classify the key term 'ta'ifa'
Determine that 'ta'ifa' is 'amm' (general) because it can refer to one or more individuals. This is a textual analysis step.
Hanafis accept that 'ta'ifa' can be one person, based on linguistic usage and the Prophet's practice.
3
Analyze the pronoun references
Trace the pronouns: who is the subject of 'to become learned', 'to warn', 'they return', etc. The first interpretation (direct pronouns) makes it clear that the small group (ta'ifa) warns the large party, and the large party must accept the warning.
Two interpretations are given; both lead to the same conclusion.
4
Derive the obligation
Conclude that since Allah obligated the large party to accept the warning from a group that can be as small as one, a single person's report is binding. This is the ruling (hukm).
The verse shows that action is required upon receiving the report.
5
Address counter-interpretations
Consider the second interpretation (pronouns reversed) and see that it still supports the same conclusion. This strengthens the proof.
The commentator notes that the second interpretation is weaker but still relevant.

Chapter on the Divisions of the Sunnah. The obligation of acting upon the Book and the Sunnah. And that it obligates action without certain knowledge from the Book, and that is His statement: 'If only a group from every party among them could go out to become learned in the religion and to warn their people when they return to them, that they might be cautious.' (At-Tawbah 9:122) Meaning: why does not a small group from every large party go out from their homes to become learned in the religion, i.e., this small group goes to the scholars and travels to the horizons of the world to acquire knowledge, and to warn their people remaining at home for the sake of managing livelihood and protecting family and wealth from the disbelievers, when this small group returns to this large party, perhaps they too will be cautious. So the pronoun of 'to become learned' and 'to warn' and 'they return' refers to the small group, and the pronoun of 'to them' and 'perhaps they' refers to the large party. Thus Allah obligated warning upon the small group, and it is a term for one, two, and more, and He obligated upon the large party to accept their statement and act upon it; so it is proven that the report of a single narrator obligates action. In the verse there is another interpretation in which these pronouns are reversed. Its conditions: and that it obligates action etc. except if the single-narrator report concerns something that frequently occurs and is widely needed, and many men are present at it, like the hadith of aloud saying 'Bismillah', then it does not obligate action. (Al-Qamar) It obligates action because it gives prevailing opinion of truthfulness when the conditions for obligation of action are complete. [Fath al-Ghaffar (1272)] without certain knowledge and without tranquility, for the single non-infallible person, even if he is just or a saint, may be subject to forgetfulness such that he does not distinguish between what he heard and what he did not hear, and thinks what he did not hear is heard, and reports it, or error; so how can his report give certainty or tranquility? Yes, the single report with a decisive indication gives certainty, as if someone reports the death of the sultan's son with his crying among his companions, and slapping of cheeks of his family, and great wailing, but certainty is obtained from that indication, not from the single report as such, and the discussion is about it. (Al-Qamar) 'And He obligated' etc. This is based on the fact that 'la'alla' originally is for hope, which is impossible for Allah, so it is used metaphorically for request, because request is necessary for hope, thus it indicates obligation. (Al-Qamar) 'Reversing these pronouns' such that the pronoun of 'to become learned', 'to warn', and 'to them' refers to the large party, and the pronoun of 'they return' and 'perhaps they' refers to the small group, and 'people' is the small group, meaning: why does not go out for jihad from every large party a small group to become learned (i.e., the large remaining party in religion) and to warn (i.e., the remaining party) their people (i.e., the small group who went out) when they return (i.e., that small group) to them (i.e., the remaining party), perhaps they (i.e., the small group who went out) will be cautious. And it is possible that what is meant by the Book is His statement: 'And when Allah took a covenant from those who were given the Scripture: You shall make it known to the people and not conceal it.' (Aal Imran 3:187) He obligated upon everyone given knowledge of the Book to explain it and preach to people, and there is no benefit from it except people's acceptance of that preaching, thus the single report is a proof for action. And the Sunnah: that he accepted ... and the report of Salman about the gift until he took and ate it. Also he sent Ali and Muadh to Yemen for judging, and Dihya al-Kalbi to Caesar of Rome with a letter calling him to Islam. So if single reports were not obligatory for action, he would not have done that. The report of Barira about charity until he said in answer to her: 'It is charity for you.' All this ruling is on the basis of predominance, otherwise all the pronouns are not reversed; for the pronoun of 'they return' in both interpretations refers to the small group. (Al-Qamar) 'from our subject' i.e., that single report obligates action. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is possible that what is meant' etc. The commentator expresses the second interpretation by saying 'it is possible' indicating its weakness. And the reason is that our discussion is about the report of subjects, not the Lawgiver, and the speech of the Lawgiver is definitively proof upon everyone. ... Because when a plural is opposed to a plural, it requires distribution of individuals to individuals. And the report of Salman etc.: i.e., he accepted the report of Salman when he brought a plate of fresh dates, 'this is a gift', so he ate it and ordered his companions to eat. So it is said. In 'Jami' at-Tirmidhi' from Muawiya ibn Hayda al-Qushayri: When a thing was brought to the Messenger of Allah, he asked, 'Is it charity or a gift?' If they said charity, he did not eat; if they said gift, he ate. In this chapter from Salman and Abu Huraira. (Al-Qamar) 'to Yemen' and also the report of Umm Salma about gifts. (Al-Muhashi) 'And Dihya to him etc.': i.e., he sent Dihya ... and Dihya with kasra of the dal, and al-Kalbi attributed to Banu Kalb, a tribe of Arabs, and Qaysar is a generic name for the king of Rome, and the name of the one to whom the Prophet sent the letter of invitation was Heraclius. (Al-Qamar) Narrated by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak from Buraydah. [Ishraq al-Absar 17] ** As for sending Ali, it was narrated by Abu Dawud in his Sunan no. 3582, chapter on how to judge, from Ali: The Messenger of Allah sent me to Yemen as a judge etc. As for sending Muadh, it preceded. *** Narrated by al-Bukhari in his Sahih no. 2782, chapter on the Prophet's invitation to Islam and prophethood, and Muslim no. 1773, chapter on the Prophet's letter to Heraclius inviting to Islam, from Ibn Abbas.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive istinbat (derivation) proving that khabar al-wahid (a report from a single narrator) obligates action in Hanafi usul. The author begins by citing the Quranic verse 9:122, giving a detailed analysis of its pronouns to show that Allah obligated the small group (ta'ifa) to warn, and the large party (firqa) to accept and act upon that warning. Since a 'ta'ifa' can refer to one or more, this establishes that a single narrator's report must be acted upon. The commentary then addresses two interpretations of the verse (with reversed pronouns), but concludes that both support the obligation. The author also notes that khabar al-wahid provides 'ghalabat al-zann' (prevailing opinion), not certainty, except when accompanied by a decisive indication (qarina qati'a). The passage then cites hadith examples: the Prophet accepting Salman's report about a gift, sending single envoys like Ali, Muadh, and Dihya to convey important rulings and invitations – acts that would be pointless if their reports were not binding. Thus, the Qur'an and Sunnah jointly prove the hujjiyya (authoritativeness) of khabar al-wahid for action.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur (mass transmission); it obligates action (yujibu al-'amal) but does not provide certainty.
طائفة (ta'ifa): A group that can be one, two, or more; used in the verse to refer to the small group that goes out to learn and warn.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderant opinion; the level of certainty produced by khabar al-wahid when its conditions are met. It is less than certainty (yaqin) and tranquility (tuma'nina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis of Quran 9:122, what is the category of the term 'ta'ifa' and why does it support khabar al-wahid?
A) 'Ta'ifa' is 'khass' (specific) meaning exactly one person, so the verse proves khabar al-wahid directly.
B) 'Ta'ifa' is 'amm' (general) including one or more, so the obligation to accept the warning applies even if the group is a single individual.
C) 'Ta'ifa' is 'mujmal' (ambiguous) and requires further clarification, so the verse does not provide proof.
D) 'Ta'ifa' is 'zahir' (apparent) meaning a large group, so the verse only proves tawatur.

Key Takeaway
The general term 'ta'ifa' in Quran 9:122, combined with the command to accept the warning, establishes that a report from a single narrator (khabar al-wahid) obligates action in Hanafi usul.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
7 min
Sunnah Evidence for Acting upon Khabar al-Wahid: The Prophet's Practice
Sunnah evidence for khabar al-wahid's authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to use the Prophet's actions (accepting gifts based on single reports, sending single envoys) as evidence for the hujjiyyah of khabar al-wahid, and explain the Hanafi distinction between khabar al-wahid providing ghalabat al-zann versus certainty.

Core Idea
The Prophet's acceptance of Salman's gift and sending single judges prove that khabar al-wahid is binding for action.

This passage complements the Quranic proof by providing several examples from the Sunnah where the Prophet acted upon reports from single individuals. These practical demonstrations show that if khabar al-wahid were not obligatory, the Prophet would not have based his actions on them. Additionally, the passage clarifies the epistemological status of khabar al-wahid: it provides 'ghalabat al-zann' (prevailing opinion), not certainty, unless supported by external indications. Understanding this distinction is critical for applying the Hanafi hierarchy of legal proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prophetic examples
Locate the stories cited: 1) Salman's report about a gift, 2) Sending Ali and Muadh to Yemen as judges, 3) Sending Dihya to Heraclius. Note that each involves acting upon a single narrator's report.
These examples are from the Sunnah al-fi'liyyah (practical Sunnah).
2
Derive the obligation from these examples
Argue that if the Prophet did not consider single reports binding, he would not have acted upon them or sent single individuals to perform important tasks like judging or conveying a message from him.
The reasoning is a reverse implication: 'If not X, then Y would be pointless.'
3
Understand the epistemological status
Read the passage that explains khabar al-wahid gives 'ghalabat al-zann', not 'yaqin' or 'tuma'nina'. Know that certainty only comes with a decisive external indication (qarina qati'a).
The Hanafi position is that khabar al-wahid is zanni in both transmission and indication, yet sufficient for obligation.
4
Recognize exceptions
Note the condition mentioned: if khabar al-wahid concerns a matter that frequently occurs and is widely needed, like the recitation of basmala aloud, it does not obligate action because such matters require tawatur.
This is a Hanafi specificity; Shafi'is do not make this exception.

باب أقسام السنة وجوب العمل بالكتاب والسنة وأنه يوجب العمل دون العلم اليقين بالكتاب، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَوْلا نَفَرَ مِنْ كُلِّ فِرْقَةٍ مِنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ لِيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنْذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ إِذَا رَجَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ﴾ (التوبة: ١٢٢) أي فهلا خرج من كل جماعة كثيرة طائفة قليلة من بيوتهم ليتفقهوا في الدين، أي تذهب هذه الجماعة القليلة عند العلماء، ويسيروا في آفاق العالم لأخذ العلم ولينذروا قومهم الباقية في البيوت لأجل ترتيب المعاش ومحافظة الأهل والأموال عن الكفار إذا رجعت هذه الطائفة أي الجماعة القليلة إلى هذه الفرقة أي الجماعة الكثيرة لعلهم يحذرون أيضًا، فضمير "ليتفقهوا" و"لينذروا" و"رجعوا" راجع إلى الطائفة وضمير "إليهم" و"لعلهم" راجع إلى الفرقة فالله تعالى أوجب الإنذار على الطائفة، وهي اسم للواحد والاثنين فصاعدًا، وأوجب على الفرقة قبول قولهم والعمل به؛ فثبت أن خبر الواحد موجب للعمل، وفي الآية توجيه آخر فيه تعكس هذه الضمائر شرائطه، وهي وأنه يوجب إلخ إلا إذا كان خبر الواحد فيما يتكرر وقوعه ويعم به البلوى، ويحضره الرجال الكثيرون كحديث الجهر بالتسمية، فهو لا يوجب العمل. (القمر) يوجب العمل لإفادته غلبة الظن بالصدق عند استجماع كافية لوجوب العمل. [فتح الغفار (۱۲۷۲] دون العلم اليقين ودون الطمأنينة، فإن الواحد الغير المعصوم وإن كان عادلاً أو وليًا يحتمل أن يكون يعرضه النسيان بأن لا يتميز بين المسموع وغير المسموع، ويظن غير المسموع مسموعا، ويخبر به أو الخطاء، فكيف يكون خبره مفيدًا لليقين أو الطمأنينة؟ نعم، إن خبر الواحد مع انضمام القرينة القطعية يفيد اليقين كما إذا أخبر أحد بموت ابن السلطان عند بكائه مع جلسائه، وضرب خدود أهل بيته، والنوحة العظيمة، لكن اليقين حصل بتلك القرينة لا بخبر الواحد من حيث إنه خبر الواحد، والكلام فيه. (القمر) للواحد والاثنين إلخ على ما قال ابن عباس الها. (القمر) وأوجب إلخ هذا بناء على أن "لعل" في الأصل للترجي، وهو ممتنع على الله تعالى، فأريد بها الطلب مجازا؛ لكون الطلب لازما للترجي، فيفيد الوجوب. (القمر) تعكس هذه الضمائر بأن يكون ضمير ليتفقهوا، ولينذروا، وإليهم راجعا إلى الفرقة، وضمير "رجعوا، ولعلهم راجع إلى الطائفة، والقوم هو الطائفة، والمعنى فهلا خرج للجهاد من كل فرقة أي جماعة كثيرة منهم طائفة قليلة ليتفقهوا أي الجماعة الكثيرة الباقية في الدين ولينذروا أي الفرقة الباقية قومهم أي الطائفة الخارجين إذا رجعوا أي تلك الطائفة إليهم أي الفرقة الباقية، لعلهم أي لعلّ الطائفة الخارجة يحذرون، في " التفسير الأحمدي"، والغرض أنه لا يخرج جميع الناس إلى النفير حتى يبطل التفقه، وهو الجهاد الأكبر.(القمر) كذا كلها، وحينئذٍ تكون ممّا نحن فيه على ما بيّنتُ ذلك في "التفسير الأحمدي"، ويمكن أن يكون المراد بالكتاب هو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ مِيثَاقَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ لَتَبَيِّنَنَّهُ لِلنَّاسِ وَلا تَكْتُمُونَهُ﴾ (آل عمران: ۱۸۷) فقد أوجب على كل من أوتي علم الكتاب بيانه، ووعظه للناس، ولا فائدة منه إلا قبول الناس تلك الموعظة، فيكون خبر الواحد حجة للعمل. والسنة، وهي أنه عليها قبل ولنا هدية"، وخبر سلمان في الهدية حتى أخذها وأكلها، وأيضا بعث عليا الله ومعاذا الله إلى اليمن بالقضاء، ودحية الكلبي له إلى قيصر روم برسالة كتاب يدعوه إلى الإسلام، *** فلو لم يكن أخبار الآحاد موجبة للعمل لما فعل ذلك، خبر بريرة لها في الصدقة حتى قال في جوابها: "لكِ صدقة كلها هذا الحكم على سبيل التغليب، وإلا فجميع الضمائر ليست معكوسة؛ فإن ضمير "رجعوا" على كلا التوجيهين راجع إلى الطائفة. (القمر) مما نحن فيه أي من أن خبر الواحد موجب للعمل. (القمر) ويمكن أن يكون المراد إلخ ويعبر الشارح عن التوجيه الثاني بقوله : ويمكن إشارة إلى ضعفه، ووجه هذا أن كلامنا في خبر العباد دون الشارع، وكلام الشارع بحجة البتة على كل من أدنى إلخ لأن الجمع إذا قوبل بالجمع يقتضي انقسام الآحاد على الآحاد وخبر سلمان إلخ : أي قبل خبر سلمان حين أتى بطبق رطب "هذه هدية" فأكلها ، وأمر أصحابه بالأكل، كذا قيل، وفي جامع الترمذي" عن معاوية بن حيدة القشيري قال: كان رسول الله الله إذا أتي بشيء سأل: أصدقة أم هديّة؟ فإن قالوا صدقة لم يأكل، وإن قالوا: هدية، يأكل. وفي الباب عن سلمان وأبي هريرة لها. (القمر) إلى اليمن وكذا خبر أم سلمى في الهدايا أيضًا. (المحشي) ودحية له إلخ: أي بعث دحية الله إلخ ودحية بكسر الدال والكلبي منسوب إلى بني كلب قبيلة من العرب، والقيصر اسم جنس لملك الروم، وكان اسم الذي أرسل إليه النبي الله كتاب الدعوة هرقل. (القمر) رواه الحاكم في المستدرك عن بريدة . [ إشراق الأبصار ١٧] ** أما بعثة على الله أخرجه أبو داود في سننه رقم ۳۵۸۲ باب كيف القضاء عن علي له قال: بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى اليمن قاضيًا إلخ، وأما بعثة معاذ الله فقد سبقت. *** أخرجه البخاري في "صحيحه" رقم ۲۷۸۲ باب دعاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى الإسلام والنبوة، ومسلم رقم: ۱۷۷۳، باب كتاب النبي إلى هرقل بدعوة إلى الإسلام، عن ابن عباس
Chapter on the Divisions of the Sunnah. The obligation of acting upon the Book and the Sunnah. And that it obligates action without certain knowledge from the Book, and that is His statement: 'If only a group from every party among them could go out to become learned in the religion and to warn their people when they return to them, that they might be cautious.' (At-Tawbah 9:122) Meaning: why does not a small group from every large party go out from their homes to become learned in the religion, i.e., this small group goes to the scholars and travels to the horizons of the world to acquire knowledge, and to warn their people remaining at home for the sake of managing livelihood and protecting family and wealth from the disbelievers, when this small group returns to this large party, perhaps they too will be cautious. So the pronoun of 'to become learned' and 'to warn' and 'they return' refers to the small group, and the pronoun of 'to them' and 'perhaps they' refers to the large party. Thus Allah obligated warning upon the small group, and it is a term for one, two, and more, and He obligated upon the large party to accept their statement and act upon it; so it is proven that the report of a single narrator obligates action. In the verse there is another interpretation in which these pronouns are reversed. Its conditions: and that it obligates action etc. except if the single-narrator report concerns something that frequently occurs and is widely needed, and many men are present at it, like the hadith of aloud saying 'Bismillah', then it does not obligate action. (Al-Qamar) It obligates action because it gives prevailing opinion of truthfulness when the conditions for obligation of action are complete. [Fath al-Ghaffar (1272)] without certain knowledge and without tranquility, for the single non-infallible person, even if he is just or a saint, may be subject to forgetfulness such that he does not distinguish between what he heard and what he did not hear, and thinks what he did not hear is heard, and reports it, or error; so how can his report give certainty or tranquility? Yes, the single report with a decisive indication gives certainty, as if someone reports the death of the sultan's son with his crying among his companions, and slapping of cheeks of his family, and great wailing, but certainty is obtained from that indication, not from the single report as such, and the discussion is about it. (Al-Qamar) 'for one, two, etc.' according to what Ibn Abbas said: ... (Al-Qamar) 'And He obligated' etc. This is based on the fact that 'la'alla' originally is for hope, which is impossible for Allah, so it is used metaphorically for request, because request is necessary for hope, thus it indicates obligation. (Al-Qamar) 'Reversing these pronouns' such that the pronoun of 'to become learned', 'to warn', and 'to them' refers to the large party, and the pronoun of 'they return' and 'perhaps they' refers to the small group, and 'people' is the small group, meaning: why does not go out for jihad from every large party a small group to become learned (i.e., the large remaining party in religion) and to warn (i.e., the remaining party) their people (i.e., the small group who went out) when they return (i.e., that small group) to them (i.e., the remaining party), perhaps they (i.e., the small group who went out) will be cautious. In 'At-Tafsir al-Ahmadi', and the purpose is that not all people go out to battle until learning is suspended, and it is the greater jihad. (Al-Qamar) Thus all of it, and then it is from our subject as I clarified in 'At-Tafsir al-Ahmadi'. And it is possible that what is meant by the Book is His statement: 'And when Allah took a covenant from those who were given the Scripture: You shall make it known to the people and not conceal it.' (Aal Imran 3:187) He obligated upon everyone given knowledge of the Book to explain it and preach to people, and there is no benefit from it except people's acceptance of that preaching, thus the single report is a proof for action. And the Sunnah: that he accepted ... and the report of Salman about the gift until he took and ate it. Also he sent Ali and Muadh to Yemen for judging, and Dihya al-Kalbi to Caesar of Rome with a letter calling him to Islam. So if single reports were not obligatory for action, he would not have done that. The report of Barira about charity until he said in answer to her: 'It is charity for you.' All this ruling is on the basis of predominance, otherwise all the pronouns are not reversed; for the pronoun of 'they return' in both interpretations refers to the small group. (Al-Qamar) 'from our subject' i.e., that single report obligates action. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is possible that what is meant' etc. The commentator expresses the second interpretation by saying 'it is possible' indicating its weakness. And the reason is that our discussion is about the report of subjects, not the Lawgiver, and the speech of the Lawgiver is definitively proof upon everyone. ... Because when a plural is opposed to a plural, it requires distribution of individuals to individuals. And the report of Salman etc.: i.e., he accepted the report of Salman when he brought a plate of fresh dates, 'this is a gift', so he ate it and ordered his companions to eat. So it is said. In 'Jami' at-Tirmidhi' from Muawiya ibn Hayda al-Qushayri: When a thing was brought to the Messenger of Allah, he asked, 'Is it charity or a gift?' If they said charity, he did not eat; if they said gift, he ate. In this chapter from Salman and Abu Huraira. (Al-Qamar) 'to Yemen' and also the report of Umm Salma about gifts. (Al-Muhashi) 'And Dihya to him etc.': i.e., he sent Dihya ... and Dihya with kasra of the dal, and al-Kalbi attributed to Banu Kalb, a tribe of Arabs, and Qaysar is a generic name for the king of Rome, and the name of the one to whom the Prophet sent the letter of invitation was Heraclius. (Al-Qamar) Narrated by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak from Buraydah. [Ishraq al-Absar 17] ** As for sending Ali, it was narrated by Abu Dawud in his Sunan no. 3582, chapter on how to judge, from Ali: The Messenger of Allah sent me to Yemen as a judge etc. As for sending Muadh, it preceded. *** Narrated by al-Bukhari in his Sahih no. 2782, chapter on the Prophet's invitation to Islam and prophethood, and Muslim no. 1773, chapter on the Prophet's letter to Heraclius inviting to Islam, from Ibn Abbas.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive istinbat (derivation) proving that khabar al-wahid (a report from a single narrator) obligates action in Hanafi usul. The author begins by citing the Quranic verse 9:122, giving a detailed analysis of its pronouns to show that Allah obligated the small group (ta'ifa) to warn, and the large party (firqa) to accept and act upon that warning. Since a 'ta'ifa' can refer to one or more, this establishes that a single narrator's report must be acted upon. The commentary then addresses two interpretations of the verse (with reversed pronouns), but concludes that both support the obligation. The author also notes that khabar al-wahid provides 'ghalabat al-zann' (prevailing opinion), not certainty, except when accompanied by a decisive indication (qarina qati'a). The passage then cites hadith examples: the Prophet accepting Salman's report about a gift, sending single envoys like Ali, Muadh, and Dihya to convey important rulings and invitations – acts that would be pointless if their reports were not binding. Thus, the Qur'an and Sunnah jointly prove the hujjiyya (authoritativeness) of khabar al-wahid for action.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of mass transmission; it obligates action but does not provide certainty.
سنة فعلية (sunnah fi'liyyah): Practical Sunnah; the actions of the Prophet that serve as a source of law.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderant opinion; the epistemic level of khabar al-wahid, sufficient for action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Prophet's sending of Ali and Muadh to Yemen as judges prove the obligation of acting upon khabar al-wahid?
A) Because the judges were sent to decide cases based on their own opinions, not reports.
B) Because the Prophet trusted them to convey his judgments, but that is not related to reports.
C) Because if single reports were not binding, the Prophet would not have sent single individuals to perform tasks that require conveying rulings and taking decisions based on reports.
D) Because the Prophet sent them to teach, not to judge.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's consistent practice of acting upon single reports (e.g., Salman's gift, sending single envoys) provides a strong Sunnah-based argument that khabar al-wahid is obligatory to act upon in Hanafi usul.
