باب أقسام السنة

حديث حمل بن مالك في الجنين، وأوجب الغُرّة فيه بيان أحوال الراوي أنه مخالف للقياس؛ لأن الجنين إن كان حيًّا وجبت الدية كاملةً، وإن كان ميتا فلا شيء فيه، وأما حديث الوضوء على من قهقه في الصلاة فهو وإن كان مخالفًا للقياس لكن رواه عدة من الصحابة الكبراء كجابر وأنس وغيرهما.

أخرجه أبو داود في "سننه" رقم ٤٥٧٢، باب دية الجنين، عن ابن عباس عن عمر أنه سأل عن قضية النبي في ذلك، فقام حمل بن مالك بن النابغة، فقال: كنت بين امرأتين فضربت إحداهما الأخرى بمسطح، فقتلتها وجنينها، فقضى رسول الله في جنينها بغرة وأن تقتل. وروى البخاري رقم: ٦٥۱۱ ، باب جنين المرأة، ومسلم رقم ٩٦٨١ ، باب دية الجنين، عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله قضى في جنين امرأة من بني لحيان بغرة عبد أو أمة. ** أما رواية أنس فأخرجها أبو القاسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمي في "تاريخ جرجان" قال: قال رسول الله : من قهقه قهقةً شديدةً فليعد الوضوء والصلاة وأما حديث جابر فأخرجه الدار قطني قال: قال لنا رسول الله : من قهقه منكم في صلاته فليتوضأ، ثم يعيد الصلاة. وأما رواية غيرهما فمنه عبد الله بن عمر قال: قال رسول الله : من ضحك في صلاته قهقهةً فليعد الوضوء والصلاة. رواه ابن عدي، وفيه بقية أخرج له مسلم متابعًا، واختلف فيه، والتحقيق أنه ثقة مدلّس فلو روى عن ثقة بلفظ "حدثنا" كما في هذا الحديث فهو حجة.

ولذا كان مقدمًا على القياس.
وإن كان مجهولاً أي في رواية الحديث والعدالة لا في النسب بأن لم يعرف إلا بحديث أو حديثين كوابصة بن معبد، فحاله لا يخلو عن خمسة أقسام، فإن روى عنه السلف، أو اختلفوا فيه، أو سكتوا عن الطعن صار كالمعروف في كل من الأقسام الثلاثة؛ لأن رواية السلف شاهدة بصحته والسكوت عن الطعن بمنزلة قبولهم فلذا يقبل، وأما المختلف فيه فأوردوا في مثاله.

أي الرواية والاختلاف والسكوت
مقدمًا على القياس إلخ : قال صدر الإسلام أبو اليسر وإليه مال أكثر العلماء: لأن التغيير من الراوي بعد ثبوت عدالته وضبطه موهوم والظاهر أنه يروي كما سمع، ولو غيّره لغيره على وجه لا يتغير المعنى، هذا هو الظاهر من أحوال الصحابة والرواة والعدول؛ لأن الأخبار وردت بلسانهم فعلمهم باللسان يمنع عن غفلتهم عن المعنى وعدم فهمهم إياه وعدالتهم تدفع تهمة الزيادة والنقصان عليه. (السنبلي)
وإن كان مجهولاً : اعلم أن كلام المصنف له في مطلق الراوي صحابيًا كان أو غيره كما يظهر من السوق، فالعجب منه أنه كيف يتفوه بجهالة العدالة في الصحابة والعلم فإن الصحابة وهم كلهم عدول الأمة ليسوا بمحل الطعن نعم يحكم بتوهم بعضهم في بعض الروايات وهذا ليس منافيًا لعدالتهم، اللهم إلا أن يقال: إن الجزم بالعدالة يختص بمن اشتهر بالصحبة والباقون كسائر الناس عدول وغير عدول، كذا قيل. (القمر)
لا في النسب : فإن الجهالة في النسب غير مانعة عن القبول عند عامة الأصوليين خلافًا للبعض. (القمر)
بأن لم يعرف إلخ: هذا بيان الجهالة في رواية الحديث. (القمر)
لم يعرف إلا إلخ بيان للجهالة أي كان مجهولاً في رواية الحديث حتى لا يعرف إلا بكذا واحترز به عن مجهول النسب، فإن هذا اللفظ قد يطلق عليه، وتلك الجهالة غير مانعة عن القبول عند عامة الأصوليين وأهل الحديث وإن كانت مانعة عند البعض. (السنبلي)
كوابصة بن معبد هذا لا يخلو عن شيء فإن وابصة بن معبد من المعروفين، روى عن النبي وعن ابن مسعود وأم قيس بنت محصن وغيرهم أحاديث كذا قيل: وفي "التقريب": وابصة بكسر الباء الموحدة ثم مهملة ابن معبد صحابي، فلا تُصِغ إلى من أنكر كونه صحابيا، فافهم (القمر)
أو اختلفوا فيه: أي قبل حديثه بعضهم و لم يقبل بعضهم. (القمر)
أو سكتوا عن الطعن أي بعد بلوغ روايته إليهم.(القمر)
صار كالمعروف أي بالعدالة، فإن وافق حديثه القياس عمل به وإن خالفه لم يترك إلا بالضرورة. (القمر)
شاهدة إلخ لأن السلف لا يتهمون بالتقصير. (القمر)
بمنزلة قبولهم: إذ لو لم يكن كذلك لتطرّقت نسبة التقصير إليهم، وهم لا يتهمون بذلك. (القمر)
Chapter: Divisions of the Sunnah. The hadith of Hamal ibn Malik about the fetus, and he obligated a ghurrah in it; it explains the conditions of the narrator that it is contrary to analogy; because the fetus if it was alive the full blood-money is wajib, and if it was dead there is nothing in it. As for the hadith of wudu upon one who laughs out loud in prayer, it is contrary to analogy but several of the senior Companions narrated it like Jabir, Anas, and others. Abu Dawud recorded it in his Sunan... Therefore it was given precedence over analogy. And if he is unknown, meaning in narration of hadith and reliability not in lineage, so that he is not known except by one or two hadiths like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad, then his case is not free from five categories: if the Salaf narrated from him, or they differed about him, or they remained silent about criticism, he becomes like known in each of the three categories; because the narration of the Salaf is a witness to his soundness and silence about criticism is in the position of their acceptance, therefore it is accepted. As for the one differed about, they presented examples.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary (likely on Nur al-Anwar) establishes two key principles: first, a hadith from reliable narrators—even if contrary to qiyas—is taken as evidence and given precedence over qiyas. Two hadiths are cited as examples: the hadith of Hamal ibn Malik obligating a ghurrah for a fetus, and the hadith invalidating wudu for loud laughter in prayer. Both contradict qiyas but are accepted due to their reliable transmission. The commentator explains that the possibility of the narrator altering the meaning is remote once his reliability is established; the Salaf's practice confirms this. Second, the passage discusses the unknown narrator (majhul). It defines 'unknown' as not being known except through one or two hadiths, in terms of narration and reliability, not lineage. Three of the five categories are explained: if the Salaf narrated from him, or differed about him, or remained silent on criticism, then he becomes like a known narrator, and his hadith is accepted, because the Salaf's engagement implies verification and their silence implies tacit approval. The commentary also notes that unknown lineage does not prevent acceptance according to most Hanafi and hadith scholars. The example of Wabisah ibn Ma'bad is given, noting that he is actually well-known, so the example is not perfect; the point is conceptual.

Key Terms
مجهول (majhūl): Unknown narrator: one known only by one or two hadiths and whose reliability is not well-established.
السلف (al-salaf): The early pious generations, especially the Companions and early scholars.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following does NOT make an unknown narrator acceptable?
A) Salaf narrated from him.
B) Salaf differed about him.
C) Salaf remained silent about criticism.
D) He is known by three hadiths.

Key Takeaway
An unknown narrator becomes reliable if the Salaf engaged with him—through narration, difference, or silence—and his hadith is then accepted even if contrary to qiyas.

Conditions for Accepting the Narration of an Unknown Narrator
Categories and acceptance rules for unknown narrator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conditions under which an unknown narrator's hadith becomes acceptable according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
An unknown narrator is accepted if the salaf narrated from him, if scholars disagreed about him, or if they remained silent on his criticism.

This lesson unpacks a key rule in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: when can a narrator who is unknown in terms of memory and uprightness still have his narration accepted? The text divides the situation into five categories, three of which elevate the narrator to the status of a known, reliable transmitter. We will explore the reasoning behind this rule and examine a famous case from the Companions that illustrates its application.

Guided Path
1
Define the unknown narrator
Identify what makes a narrator 'majhool' in Hanafi usul: he is known only through one or two hadiths and his integrity is not established. Note that this ignorance is about his hadith narration, not his lineage.
The example given is Wabisa ibn Ma'bad, though commentators note he is actually a well-known Companion.
2
List the five categories
The text states there are five categories (aqsam) for such a narrator, but only three lead to acceptance. Identify the three: (1) salaf narrated from him, (2) scholars disagreed about him, (3) scholars remained silent about criticism.
The other two categories are implied to be rejection.
3
Understand the rationale for acceptance
The three conditions are accepted because: (a) the salaf would not narrate from an unreliable person, (b) disagreement shows the narrator is not unanimously rejected, (c) silence implies tacit approval.
This reasoning relies on the trustworthiness of the early generations.
4
Analyze the example from practice
Read the story of Ibn Mas'ud and Ma'qil ibn Sinan. Note how Ibn Mas'ud initially rejected Ma'qil's hadith due to his Bedouin background (an unknown narrator), but later accepted it when it was corroborated by his own ijtihad matching the Prophet's ruling.
This story is used by the commentators to show that an unknown narrator's narration can be accepted under certain conditions.
5
Apply the rule to the story
Determine which of the three conditions applies to Ma'qil. Is it that the salaf narrated from him, that there was disagreement, or that there was silence? In the story, Ibn Mas'ud's eventual acceptance can be seen as an example of the first condition (the salaf, i.e., Ibn Mas'ud himself, narrated from him after verification).
The story also illustrates the importance of corroboration and the principle that a narrator's unknown status can be overcome.

وإن كان مجهولاً أي في رواية الحديث والعدالة لا في النسب بأن لم يعرف إلا بحديث أو حديثين كوابصة بن معبد، فحاله لا يخلو عن خمسة أقسام، فإن روى عنه السلف، أو اختلفوا فيه، أو سكتوا عن الطعن صار كالمعروف في كل من الأقسام الثلاثة؛ لأن رواية السلف شاهدة بصحته والسكوت عن الطعن بمنزلة قبولهم فلذا يقبل، وأما المختلف فيه فأوردوا في مثاله

ما روي أن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه سئل عمن تزوّج امرأة ولم يسمّ لها مهراً حتى مات عنها، فاجتهد شهرًا وقال بعد ذلك: ما سمعت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم شيئًا، ولكن أجتهد برأيي، فإن أصبت فمن الله وإن أخطأت فمني ومن الشيطان أرى لها مهر مثل نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط، فقام سنان وقال: أشهد أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى في بردع بنت واشق مثل قضائك، معقل بن أي أظن لها فسر ابن مسعود ده سرورًا لم يُر مثله قط لموافقة قضائه قضاءَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وردّه على وقال: ما نُصغي بقول أعرابي بوّال على عقبيه وحسبها الميراث ولا مهر لها؛ ** عن ثلاث وستين ما روي أن ابن مسعود إلخ والوكس بفتح الواو وسكون الكاف النقصانُ والشطط بفتحتين الظلم والمجاوزة الحد، ومعقل بفتح الميم وكسر القاف شهد فتح مكة معه، سكن الكوفة، وقتل يوم الحرة بالمدينة سنة كذا في "كشف البزدوي". وبردع بكسر الباء الموحدة وسكون الراء المهملة كمنبر، كذا ضبط أصحاب الحديث، وقال العلامة التفتازاني بفتح الباء الموحدة، وفي "القاموس": برذع كجدول، ولا تكسر، وكانت بنت واشق بكسر الشين المعجمة من أشجع وكان زوجها هلال بن مرّة الأشجعي، وقد تزوج بها بلا فرض مهر ومات عنها بلا دخول . (القمر) بوّال إلخ مبالغة في البائل وفيه إشارة إلى أنه من الذين غلب فيهم الجهل الجهل من أهل البوادي وسكان الرمال؛ إذ من عادتهم الاحتباء في الجلوس من غير إزار، والبول في المكان الذي جلسوا فيه إذا احتاجوا إليه، وعدم المبالاة بإصابة أعقابهم. (السنبلي) بوّال على عقبيه كان من عادة الأعراب الجلوس محتبيا والبول في مكان جلسوا فيه إذا احتاجوا إلى البول وعدم المبالاة بأن يصيب البول أعقابهم، وذلك من الجهل وقلة احتياطهم ولا مهر لها لعدم الدخول في "جامع الترمذي"، وقال بعض أهل العلم من أصحاب النبي منهم علي بن أبي طالب وزيد بن ثابت وابن عباس وابن عمر إذا تزوّج الرجل امرأة ولم يدخل بها ولم يفرض لها صداقًا حتى مات قالوا لها الميراث ولا صداق لها، وعليها العدة، وهو قول الشافعي رحمه الله وقال العلي القارئ له في شرح مختصر "المنار": ما روي عن علي أنه قال: "لا يقبل معقل بن سنان فإنه أعرابي بوّال على عقبيه لم يصح عن علي . Chapter: Divisions of the Sunnah. Explanation of the conditions of the narrator. Therefore it is given precedence over analogy. And if he is unknown, i.e., in narrating hadith and uprightness, not in lineage, such that he is only known through one or two hadiths like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad, then his situation is not free from five categories. If the salaf narrated from him, or they disagreed about him, or they remained silent about criticism, he becomes like the known in each of the three categories because the narration of the salaf testifies to his soundness, and silence about criticism is like their acceptance, so it is accepted. As for the one about whom there is disagreement, they mentioned as an example... (commentary follows including explanation of the categories, then the story of Ibn Mas'ud about a man who married without specifying a dower and died, Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad, and the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan about Barada' bint Washiq, Ibn Mas'ud's initial rejection of the Bedouin's statement, and then the ruling that she gets inheritance but no dower because there was no consummation. The passage ends with references to Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Abu Dawud, and the position of Ali and others.)
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work discussing the acceptance of hadith from an unknown narrator (majhool). The author first states that a narrator who is only known through one or two hadiths (like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad) falls into five categories regarding the acceptance of his narration. Three of these categories lead to him being treated as a known narrator: (1) if the salaf (the early generations) narrated from him, (2) if there was disagreement among scholars about him, with some accepting and some rejecting his narrations, or (3) if scholars remained silent about his criticism. The reasoning given is that the salaf are trustworthy and their narration indicates his reliability; silence implies tacit approval. The commentary by al-Sanbali and al-Qamar clarifies that unknown narrators among the Companions (sahaba) are generally considered trustworthy, but ignorance of lineage does not prevent acceptance. The passage then narrates a famous story where Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married without specifying a dower and died before consummation. After a month of deliberation, Ibn Mas'ud ruled that the woman is entitled to the mahr of her peers. The narrator Ma'qil ibn Sinan then testified that the Prophet had given a similar judgment in the case of Barada' bint Washiq. Despite initially dismissing Ma'qil as an uncivilized Bedouin, Ibn Mas'ud accepted the hadith and was overjoyed that his ruling matched the Prophet's. The passage concludes with the legal rule that in such a case, the woman receives inheritance but no dower, citing the opinions of Ali, Zayd ibn Thabit, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and al-Shafi'i, and noting that the hadith is recorded in the major hadith collections.

Key Terms
مجهول (majhool): A narrator known only through one or two hadiths, not well-known in terms of memory and uprightness
وكس (waks): Deficiency or reduction (in the context of dower)
شطط (shatat): Excess or injustice, going beyond the proper limit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the three conditions that make an unknown narrator's narration acceptable?
A) The salaf narrated from him
B) Scholars disagreed about him
C) Scholars praised him explicitly
D) Scholars remained silent about criticism

Key Takeaway
An unknown narrator becomes known if the salaf narrated from him, if there was ikhtilaf about him, or if there was sukt 'an al-ta'n.

The Nature of Intellect and Its Role in Hadith Narration
Defining the condition of intellect as a light and discussing its epistemological implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'aql, explain the analogy of light, and describe the epistemological function of intellect in hadith narration.

Core Idea
The intellect is a light that illuminates the path from sensory perception to rational understanding, making it a fundamental condition for reliable narration.

In this passage, the commentator explains the first condition of a narrator: intellect ('aql). He defines it as a light that enables the transition from what the senses perceive to abstract reasoning. This definition not only clarifies the epistemological role of the intellect but also hints at the relationship between the heart and intellect. Additionally, the passage addresses a potential objection: why attribute a ruling to a hadith when it could be derived by qiyas? The answer reveals the practical benefit of establishing authority via transmission.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context
The passage begins after listing the four conditions of a narrator. Identify that intellect is the first condition under discussion.
2
Parse the definition of 'aql
Break down the phrase: 'nur fi badan al-adami yudi'u bihi tariq yubtada'u bihi min haythu yantahi ilayhi dark al-hawass.' Understand the analogy of light, the path, and the starting point at the end of sensory perception.
The example of a tall building illustrates how the intellect moves from sensory observation to abstract conclusion.
3
Notice the hint about the heart
The commentator says 'fihi tanbih 'ala anna al-qalba mudrik, wa al-'aqlatu lahu.' This indicates that perception is ultimately attributed to the heart, with intellect as its instrument. How does this relate to the definition?
This aligns with Quran 50:37, which refers to the heart as the seat of understanding.
4
Understand the benefit of attributing the ruling to hadith
The passage then addresses a potential objection: if the hadith is not contrary to qiyas, why not rely on qiyas? The answer is that attributing the ruling to the hadith preempts objections that could be raised against qiyas. Appreciate how this strengthens the authority of hadith.
This shows that even when a ruling can be derived rationally, the direct transmission from the Prophet ﷺ carries greater authority and silences doubt.

ولما فرغ عن بيان تقسيم الراوي شرع في شرائطه، فقال: وإنما جعل الخبر حجة بشرائط في الراوي وهي أربعة: العقل والضبط والعدالة والإسلام. فالعقل: وهو نور في بدن الآدمي يضيء به طريق يبتدأ به من حيث ينتهي إليه درك الحواس، أي نور يضيء بسبب ذلك النور طريق يبتدأ بذلك الطريق من مكان ينتهي إلى ذلك المكان درك الحواس، مثلاً لو نظر أحد إلى بناء رفيع انتهى درك البصر إلى البناء، ثم يبتدئ منه طريق إلى أنه لا بد له من صانع ذي علم وحكمة. فمبتدأ العقول هو منتهى الحواس، وهذا فيما كان الانتقال من المحسوس إلى المعقول، وأما إذا كان معقولاً صرفاً، فإنما يبتدئ به طريق العلم من حيث يوجد، فيتبدى المطلوب للقلب، فيدركه القلب بتأمله. وفيه تنبيه على أن القلب مدرك، والعقل آلة له. ولا يجب لتمكن الشبهة لعدم اشتهاره في السلف. وفائدة إضافة الحكم حينئذ إلى الحديث دون القياس: دفع دخل مقدر، تقريره: أنه إذا لم يكن الحديث مخالفاً للقياس فكان الحكم ثابتاً بالقياس فما فائدة إضافة الحكم حينئذ إلى الحديث دون القياس؟ الحكم: أي جواز العمل وعدم وجوبه. حينئذٍ: أي حين إذا لم يكن الحديث مخالفاً للقياس. الخبر: أي خبر الواحد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. شرائط: أي بصفات متحققة في الراوي. وهو نور إلخ: قوة شبيهة بالنور في أنه يحصل بها الإدراك. في بدن الآدمي: أي في الرأس أو في القلب على اختلاف القولين. طريق: والمراد بالطريق مقدمات الاكتساب والنظر في القياس والأوصاف والأجزاء في التعريفات. وهذا: أي كون مبتدأ العقول منتهى الحواس. مدرك فيضاف الإدراك إلى القلب في الشرع كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَى لِمَنْ كَانَ لَهُ قَلْبٌ﴾ [ق:37] هو لطيفة ربانية، وهو المدرك العالم العارف كذا في شرح الأوراد. والعقل آلة له: فالعقل قوة تكون آلة للفهم، وبها الامتياز بين الأمور النافعة والضارة بحسب الظن والاعتقاد. على طريق أهل الإسلام، فللقلب عين باطنة يدرك بها الأشياء بعد إشراقه بالعقل كما أن في الملك الظاهر تدرك العين بعد الإشراق بالشمس أو السراج. وعند الحكماء: المدرك هو النفس الناطقة بواسطة العقل والحواس الظاهرة أو الباطنة. والشرط الكامل منه، أي الشرط في باب رواية الحديث الكامل من العقل وهو عقل البالغ دون القاصر منه، وهو عقل الصبي والمعتوه والمجنون؛ لأن الشرع لما لم يجعلهم أهلاً للتصرف في أمور أنفسهم ففي أمر الدين أولى، وهذا إذا كان السماع والرواية قبل البلوغ. يدربها الأشياء أي الغائبة عن الحواس من غير أن يكون العقل موجباً لذلك. تدرك العين: أي من غير أن يوجب الشمس أو السراج رؤية تلك الأشياء. هو النفس الناطقة إلخ: وهو جوهر مجرّد ليس جسماً ولا جسمانيا، وتعلقه بالبدن تعلّق التدبير والتصرف، لا تعلق الجزء بالكل والحال بالمحل وهذا تعريف النفس عند جمهور الفلاسفة، وهو مختار كثير من علماء الإسلام كالإمام الرازي والإمام حجة الإسلام، وأكثر الصوفية الكرام. بواسطة العقل هذا عجيب فإن النفس الناطقة هو العقل المدرك عند الحكماء بواسطة السمع والبصر والشم والذوق واللمس، وهي الحواس الظاهرة بواسطة الحس المشترك والوهم والخيال والحافظة والمتصرفة، وهي الحواس الباطنة، وللتفصيل مقام آخر. الكامل من العقل: ولما كان كمال العقل مشككا لا يضبط فحدّه الشارع بعقل البالغ؛ ولذا قال المصنف: وهو إلخ، ووجه اشتراط عقل البلوغ أن الصبي غير مكلف، فلا يعتمد على احترازه عن الكذب فوقعت الشبهة في روايته. وهو عقل الصبي: لأن الصبي الكامل التمييز وإن كان ضابطاً لا يجتنب الكذب لعلمه بأن لا إثم عليه، فلا يكون خبره حجة، ولأن الشرع لم يجعله وليا في أمر دنياه ففي أمر الدين أولى. [فتح الغفار 281] جَعْلُ عقل الصبي قاصراً أمر حكمي بناءً على الغالب، فإنه ضعيف البنية التي قوتها دليل على قوة القوى، وإلا فكم من صبي يكون أفطن من بالغ. والمعتوه: العته آفة توجب خللاً في العقل، فيصير صاحبه مختلط الكلام يشبه بعض كلامه بكلام العقلاء، وبعضه بكلام المجانين، كذا قال الشارح فيما سيأتي. لما لم يجعلهم أهلاً إلخ: فيه أن العبد ليس بأهل للتصرف في أمور نفسه مع أنه يقبل روايته اللهم إلا أن يقال: إن ذلك لحق المولى لا لنقصان في العقل. وهذا: أي عدم اعتبار عقل الصبي. السماع والرواية: أي سماع الحديث وروايته. قبل البلوغ إلخ: من شرائط الرواية التعقل والتميز للتحمل أي لتحمل الحديث، والشرط للأداء الكمال للعقل وقد اختلفوا في تعيين أقلّ السنين التي يحصل به التميّز فقيل: خمسة، وهو المختار عند ابن الصلاح، وقيل: غير ذلك.
When he finished clarifying the classification of the narrator, he began on his conditions, saying: The khabar is made an authority only by conditions in the narrator, which are four: intellect, memory, integrity, and Islam. Intellect: it is a light in the human body by which a path is illuminated, a path that starts from where the perception of the senses ends. For example, if one looks at a tall building, the perception of sight ends at the building, then from it a path begins to the conclusion that it must have a maker possessing knowledge and wisdom. So the starting point of intellects is the end point of the senses. This applies when the transition is from the sensible to the intelligible. But if it is purely intelligible, then the path of knowledge begins from where it exists, and the sought thing appears to the heart, and the heart perceives it by contemplating it. In this is a hint that the heart is a perceiver and the intellect is its instrument. And it is not obligatory due to the possibility of doubt because it is not well-known among the predecessors. The benefit of attributing the ruling in that case to the hadith rather than to qiyas is to repel a potential objection, which is: if the hadith is not contrary to qiyas and the ruling is established by qiyas, what is the benefit of attributing the ruling to the hadith instead of qiyas? The ruling: i.e., the permissibility of acting upon it and not its obligation. At that time: i.e., when the hadith is not contrary to qiyas. The khabar: i.e., the khabar wahid from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Conditions: i.e., attributes existing in the narrator. And it is a light etc.: a power resembling light in that perception is attained through it. In the human body: i.e., in the head or in the heart according to the two opinions. Path: and by 'path' is meant the premises of acquisition and consideration in qiyas and the descriptions and parts in definitions. And this: i.e., that the starting point of intellects is the end point of the senses. A perceiver, so perception is attributed to the heart in the Shariah as Allah Most High said: 'Indeed in that is a reminder for whoever has a heart' (Q. 50:37). It is a subtle spiritual substance, and it is the perceiving, knowing, cognizant entity, as in Sharh al-Awrad. And the intellect is an instrument for it: the intellect is a power that serves as an instrument for understanding, and by it the distinction is made between beneficial and harmful matters based on conjecture and belief. According to the way of the people of Islam, the heart has an inner eye by which it perceives things after being illuminated by the intellect, just as in the external realm the eye perceives after illumination by the sun or a lamp. And according to the philosophers, the perceiver is the rational soul by means of the intellect and the external or internal senses. And the complete condition from it, i.e., the condition in the chapter of narrating hadith is the complete intellect, which is the intellect of an adult, not the deficient one, which is the intellect of a child, the mentally deficient, and the insane; because since the Shariah did not make them fit to manage their own affairs, then in matters of religion it is more appropriate. This is if the hearing and narration occur before puberty. She perceives things i.e., things absent from the senses without the intellect being a cause for that. The eye perceives: i.e., without the sun or lamp causing the vision of those things. It is the rational soul etc.: it is an abstract substance, neither a body nor embodied, and its relation to the body is that of management and disposition, not that of a part to a whole or a state to a locus. This is the definition of the soul according to most philosophers, and it is chosen by many Islamic scholars such as Imam al-Razi, Imam Hujjat al-Islam, and most of the noble Sufis. By means of the intellect: this is strange, for the rational soul is the perceiving intellect according to the philosophers by means of hearing, sight, smell, taste, and touch—the external senses—by means of the common sense, imagination, estimation, memory, and the dispositive faculty—the internal senses. A detailed discussion belongs elsewhere. The complete condition from intellect: Since the perfection of intellect is gradational and cannot be determined, the Lawgiver defined it by the intellect of an adult; hence the author said: it is etc. The reason for requiring the intellect of adulthood is that a child is not obligated (mukallaf), so one cannot rely on his avoidance of lying, thus doubt arises in his narration. And it is the intellect of a child: because the child with complete discernment, even if he is accurate in memory, does not avoid lying because he knows that there is no sin on him, so his khabar is not authoritative. And because the Shariah did not make him a guardian in his worldly affairs, so in matters of religion it is more appropriate. [Fath al-Ghaffar 281] The classification of a child's intellect as deficient is a ruling based on the predominance, because his constitution is weak, and its strength is evidence of the strength of faculties; otherwise, many children are more perceptive than adults. And the mentally deficient (ma'tuh): 'atih is a defect that causes a defect in the intellect, so the person becomes confused in speech, part of his speech resembling that of sane people and part resembling that of the insane, as the commentator said later. 'Since the Shariah did not make them fit etc.': there is in it that the slave is not fit to manage his own affairs, yet his narration is accepted—unless it is said that is due to the right of the master, not due to a deficiency in intellect. And this: i.e., not considering the intellect of a child. Hearing and narration: i.e., hearing hadith and narrating it. Before puberty etc.: among the conditions of narration are intellect and discernment for tahammul (receiving), and the condition for performance (ada') is perfection of intellect. And they differed on determining the minimum age at which discernment occurs: it was said five years, which is the chosen opinion of Ibn al-Salah, and it was said otherwise, =
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the conditions required for a narrator to be considered authoritative (hujja). It begins by stating the four conditions: intellect, memory, integrity, and Islam. The focus here is on intellect ('aql). The author defines 'aql as a light in the human body by which one can reason from sensory perceptions to abstract conclusions, as in the example of inferring a maker from a tall building. This shows that intellect enables knowledge beyond mere senses. The text then discusses that perception is ultimately attributed to the heart, with the intellect as its instrument, citing Quran 50:37. It also addresses a potential objection: if a hadith is not contrary to qiyas, why not rely on qiyas alone? The answer is that attributing the ruling to the hadith prevents opponents from objecting with the same questions they could raise against qiyas. Crucially, the passage explains that the required intellect must be 'complete,' meaning that of a baligh (adult) who is sane and free from mental deficiency. The reasoning is that the Shariah does not consider children, the insane, or the mentally deficient as fit to manage their own affairs, so how could they be trusted with religious transmission? Even a discerning child might lie without feeling sin because he is not obligated. The text also mentions that the age of discernment is disputed, with Ibn al-Salah choosing five years. This lesson underscores the Hanafi insistence on the narrator's legal competence (ahliyyah) as a prerequisite for accepting reports.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): نور في بدن الآدمي يضيء به طريق يبتدأ به من حيث ينتهي إليه درك الحواس، أي قوة شبيهة بالنور يحصل بها الإدراك.
البالغ (al-baligh): من بلغ سن التكليف، وهو المكلف بالشرع، وعقله كامل معتبر في الرواية.
المعتوه (al-ma'tuh): آفة توجب خللاً في العقل، فيصير صاحبه مختلط الكلام يشبه بعضه كلام العقلاء وبعضه كلام المجانين.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary function of intellect ('aql) in relation to hadith narration?
A) To ensure the narrator can memorize long chains of transmission.
B) To enable the narrator to move from sensory perception to abstract reasoning, ensuring correct understanding.
C) To allow the narrator to derive legal rulings from the hadith independently.
D) To make the narrator morally upright and trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'aql as a light from senses to intellect underpins the requirement for a narrator to be capable of understanding and conveying the prophetic message accurately.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
The Requirement of Adulthood (Bulugh) for Hadith Narration
Explaining the condition of complete intellect and the exclusion of children and the insane from narration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the narrator to be a baligh (adult), and state the ruling regarding narrations from a child, an insane person, and a ma'tuh (mentally deficient).

Core Idea
Only the complete intellect of a legally responsible adult guarantees reliability; children and the insane are excluded because the Shariah does not trust them in worldly matters, let alone religious ones.

This passage delves into the second aspect of the intellect condition: it must be complete, which the Lawgiver defines as the intellect of an adult (baligh). The text explains why children, the insane, and the mentally deficient (ma'tuh) are not acceptable narrators, even if they show discernment. The reasoning is that since the Shariah does not grant them legal capacity in their own affairs, they cannot be trusted with the sacred duty of transmitting hadith. The passage also touches on a scholarly dispute about the minimum age at which a child's narration can be accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement of complete intellect
The text says 'al-shart al-kamil minhu, wa huwa 'aql al-baligh.' Note that the condition is not just intellect but complete intellect, i.e., that of an adult.
The perfection of intellect is gradational, so the Lawgiver specifically identified the adult stage as the threshold.
2
Understand the rationale
The text gives two reasons: (a) the child is not mukallaf, so he might not avoid lying; (b) the Shariah did not make him a guardian in worldly affairs, so a fortiori not in religion.
This is a qiyas awwalawi: if not trusted in worldly matters, certainly not in religious.
3
Apply to categories
Examine the exclusions: child (sabi), insane (majnun), and ma'tuh (mentally deficient). For each, the passage explains why their narration is rejected.
For the ma'tuh, his speech is a mix of sensible and nonsensical, making him unreliable.
4
Note the exception of the slave
The text raises an objection: a slave is not fit to manage his own affairs yet his narration is accepted. The response is that the slave's incapacity is due to the master's right, not a deficiency in intellect.
This distinguishes between legal incapacity (due to servitude) and intellectual incapacity (which affects narration).
5
Consider the dispute on age of discernment
The passage mentions that scholars differed on the minimum age for a child's narration to be considered. The chosen view according to Ibn al-Salah is five years. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical implications.
Even if a child of five shows discernment, the Hanafi position still requires adulthood for narration, but this dispute affects the time of tahammul (receiving).

ولما فرغ عن بيان تقسيم الراوي شرع في شرائطه، فقال: وإنما جعل الخبر حجة بشرائط في الراوي وهي أربعة: العقل والضبط والعدالة والإسلام. فالعقل: وهو نور في بدن الآدمي يضيء به طريق يبتدأ به من حيث ينتهي إليه درك الحواس، أي نور يضيء بسبب ذلك النور طريق يبتدأ بذلك الطريق من مكان ينتهي إلى ذلك المكان درك الحواس، مثلاً لو نظر أحد إلى بناء رفيع انتهى درك البصر إلى البناء، ثم يبتدئ منه طريق إلى أنه لا بد له من أن الصبي غير مكلف، فلا يعتمد على احترازه عن الكذب فوقعت الشبهة في روايته. وهو عقل الصبي: لأن الصبي الكامل التمييز وإن كان ضابطاً لا يجتنب الكذب لعلمه بأن لا إثم عليه، فلا يكون خبره حجة، ولأن الشرع لم يجعله وليا في أمر دنياه ففي أمر الدين أولى. [فتح الغفار 281] جَعْلُ عقل الصبي قاصراً أمر حكمي بناءً على الغالب، فإنه ضعيف البنية التي قوتها دليل على قوة القوى، وإلا فكم من صبي يكون أفطن من بالغ. والمعتوه: العته آفة توجب خللاً في العقل، فيصير صاحبه مختلط الكلام يشبه بعض كلامه بكلام العقلاء، وبعضه بكلام المجانين، كذا قال الشارح فيما سيأتي. لما لم يجعلهم أهلاً إلخ: فيه أن العبد ليس بأهل للتصرف في أمور نفسه مع أنه يقبل روايته اللهم إلا أن يقال: إن ذلك لحق المولى لا لنقصان في العقل. وهذا: أي عدم اعتبار عقل الصبي. السماع والرواية: أي سماع الحديث وروايته. قبل البلوغ إلخ: من شرائط الرواية التعقل والتميز للتحمل أي لتحمل الحديث، والشرط للأداء الكمال للعقل وقد اختلفوا في تعيين أقلّ السنين التي يحصل به التميّز فقيل: خمسة، وهو المختار عند ابن الصلاح، وقيل: غير ذلك.
When he finished clarifying the classification of the narrator, he began on his conditions, saying: The khabar is made an authority only by conditions in the narrator, which are four: intellect, memory, integrity, and Islam. Intellect: it is a light in the human body by which a path is illuminated, a path that starts from where the perception of the senses ends. For example, if one looks at a tall building, the perception of sight ends at the building, then from it a path begins to the conclusion that it must have a maker possessing knowledge and wisdom. So the starting point of intellects is the end point of the senses. This applies when the transition is from the sensible to the intelligible. But if it is purely intelligible, then the path of knowledge begins from where it exists, and the sought thing appears to the heart, and the heart perceives it by contemplating it. In this is a hint that the heart is a perceiver and the intellect is its instrument. And it is not obligatory due to the possibility of doubt because it is not well-known among the predecessors. The benefit of attributing the ruling in that case to the hadith rather than to qiyas is to repel a potential objection, which is: if the hadith is not contrary to qiyas and the ruling is established by qiyas, what is the benefit of attributing the ruling to the hadith instead of qiyas? The ruling: i.e., the permissibility of acting upon it and not its obligation. At that time: i.e., when the hadith is not contrary to qiyas. The khabar: i.e., the khabar wahid from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Conditions: i.e., attributes existing in the narrator. And it is a light etc.: a power resembling light in that perception is attained through it. In the human body: i.e., in the head or in the heart according to the two opinions. Path: and by 'path' is meant the premises of acquisition and consideration in qiyas and the descriptions and parts in definitions. And this: i.e., that the starting point of intellects is the end point of the senses. A perceiver, so perception is attributed to the heart in the Shariah as Allah Most High said: 'Indeed in that is a reminder for whoever has a heart' (Q. 50:37). It is a subtle spiritual substance, and it is the perceiving, knowing, cognizant entity, as in Sharh al-Awrad. And the intellect is an instrument for it: the intellect is a power that serves as an instrument for understanding, and by it the distinction is made between beneficial and harmful matters based on conjecture and belief. According to the way of the people of Islam, the heart has an inner eye by which it perceives things after being illuminated by the intellect, just as in the external realm the eye perceives after illumination by the sun or a lamp. And according to the philosophers, the perceiver is the rational soul by means of the intellect and the external or internal senses. And the complete condition from it, i.e., the condition in the chapter of narrating hadith is the complete intellect, which is the intellect of an adult, not the deficient one, which is the intellect of a child, the mentally deficient, and the insane; because since the Shariah did not make them fit to manage their own affairs, then in matters of religion it is more appropriate. This is if the hearing and narration occur before puberty. She perceives things i.e., things absent from the senses without the intellect being a cause for that. The eye perceives: i.e., without the sun or lamp causing the vision of those things. It is the rational soul etc.: it is an abstract substance, neither a body nor embodied, and its relation to the body is that of management and disposition, not that of a part to a whole or a state to a locus. This is the definition of the soul according to most philosophers, and it is chosen by many Islamic scholars such as Imam al-Razi, Imam Hujjat al-Islam, and most of the noble Sufis. By means of the intellect: this is strange, for the rational soul is the perceiving intellect according to the philosophers by means of hearing, sight, smell, taste, and touch—the external senses—by means of the common sense, imagination, estimation, memory, and the dispositive faculty—the internal senses. A detailed discussion belongs elsewhere. The complete condition from intellect: Since the perfection of intellect is gradational and cannot be determined, the Lawgiver defined it by the intellect of an adult; hence the author said: it is etc. The reason for requiring the intellect of adulthood is that a child is not obligated (mukallaf), so one cannot rely on his avoidance of lying, thus doubt arises in his narration. And it is the intellect of a child: because the child with complete discernment, even if he is accurate in memory, does not avoid lying because he knows that there is no sin on him, so his khabar is not authoritative. And because the Shariah did not make him a guardian in his worldly affairs, so in matters of religion it is more appropriate. [Fath al-Ghaffar 281] The classification of a child's intellect as deficient is a ruling based on the predominance, because his constitution is weak, and its strength is evidence of the strength of faculties; otherwise, many children are more perceptive than adults. And the mentally deficient (ma'tuh): 'atih is a defect that causes a defect in the intellect, so the person becomes confused in speech, part of his speech resembling that of sane people and part resembling that of the insane, as the commentator said later. 'Since the Shariah did not make them fit etc.': there is in it that the slave is not fit to manage his own affairs, yet his narration is accepted—unless it is said that is due to the right of the master, not due to a deficiency in intellect. And this: i.e., not considering the intellect of a child. Hearing and narration: i.e., hearing hadith and narrating it. Before puberty etc.: among the conditions of narration are intellect and discernment for tahammul (receiving), and the condition for performance (ada') is perfection of intellect. And they differed on determining the minimum age at which discernment occurs: it was said five years, which is the chosen opinion of Ibn al-Salah, and it was said otherwise, =
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the conditions required for a narrator to be considered authoritative (hujja). It begins by stating the four conditions: intellect, memory, integrity, and Islam. The focus here is on intellect ('aql). The author defines 'aql as a light in the human body by which one can reason from sensory perceptions to abstract conclusions, as in the example of inferring a maker from a tall building. This shows that intellect enables knowledge beyond mere senses. The text then discusses that perception is ultimately attributed to the heart, with the intellect as its instrument, citing Quran 50:37. It also addresses a potential objection: if a hadith is not contrary to qiyas, why not rely on qiyas alone? The answer is that attributing the ruling to the hadith prevents opponents from objecting with the same questions they could raise against qiyas. Crucially, the passage explains that the required intellect must be 'complete,' meaning that of a baligh (adult) who is sane and free from mental deficiency. The reasoning is that the Shariah does not consider children, the insane, or the mentally deficient as fit to manage their own affairs, so how could they be trusted with religious transmission? Even a discerning child might lie without feeling sin because he is not obligated. The text also mentions that the age of discernment is disputed, with Ibn al-Salah choosing five years. This lesson underscores the Hanafi insistence on the narrator's legal competence (ahliyyah) as a prerequisite for accepting reports.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): نور في بدن الآدمي يضيء به طريق يبتدأ به من حيث ينتهي إليه درك الحواس، أي قوة شبيهة بالنور يحصل بها الإدراك.
البالغ (al-baligh): من بلغ سن التكليف، وهو المكلف بالشرع، وعقله كامل معتبر في الرواية.
المعتوه (al-ma'tuh): آفة توجب خللاً في العقل، فيصير صاحبه مختلط الكلام يشبه بعضه كلام العقلاء وبعضه كلام المجانين.

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the narration of a child who has not reached puberty, even if he is intelligent and has a good memory?
A) Because a child cannot physically travel to hear hadith.
B) Because the child is not obligated (mukallaf) and may lie without feeling sin, so doubt exists.
C) Because the child's memory is naturally weak.
D) Because the child cannot understand the meaning of the hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts hadith narration to adults of sound mind, ensuring that narrators are legally accountable and thus more trustworthy.

Al-Sunnah as Source

The Four Components of Dabt (Accuracy) in Hadith Narration
Explaining the components of ضبط for hadith narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four components of dabt as defined by the Hanafi school and apply them to evaluate a narrator's accuracy.

Core Idea
Dabt requires complete hearing, understanding meaning, memorization with effort, and persistent review until transmission.

In this lesson, we dissect the Hanafi definition of dabt (accuracy) for hadith narrators. The text breaks down dabt into four essential components, revealing that mere word memorization is insufficient. Understanding these components is crucial for evaluating the reliability of a narrator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching definition of dabt
Find the sentence that defines dabt and note its elements: سماع الكلام, فهمه, حفظه, الثبات عليه.
The definition is explicitly given at the start of the passage.
2
Extract the first component: Complete hearing
Look for the description of how the speech must be heard: from beginning to end, with full words and structure.
The text provides an example of a latecomer; such incomplete hearing is not valid.
3
Extract the second component: Understanding the intended meaning
Identify the requirement that the narrator must understand the meaning (لغويًا أو شرعيًا), not just the words.
This is a distinct Hanafi position; the majority do not require this.
4
Extract the third component: Memorization with effort
Find the part about حفظ and بذل المجهود, meaning memorization to the extent of human capacity.
The pronoun references point back to the heard speech.
5
Extract the fourth component: Persistence and action
Look for الثبات عليه and محافظة الحدود, which means acting upon the hadith and reviewing it until transmission.
This includes guarding and repeating to avoid forgetting.

الحفظ
بمعنى الجهد وهو الطاقة أي ثم حفظ ذلك المسموع بقدر الطاقة البشرية له. ثم الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده وهي العمل بموجبه ببدنه ومراقبته بمذاكرته أي مع أي أحكامه مذاكرته حال كونه مستقراً على إساءة الظن بنفسه بأن لا يعتمد على نفسه بالقوة الحافظة، بل يقول : إني إذا تركته ،نسيته، وهذا كله إلى حين أدائه أي إلى حين أن يؤديه ويبلغه إلى شخص آخر كذالك واحدًا كان أو جماعةً، فحينئذٍ تفرغ ذمته عند الله تعالى، أي كما بلغ إليه وتشتغل به ذمة إنسان آخر يؤدّيه إلى أحد، وهكذا إلى يوم التناد أو إلى أن تُؤلّف كتب الأحاديث، وهذا بخلاف القرآن؛ لأنه لم يشترط لنقله فهمه بمعناه؛ لأنه ما ثبت في الأصل إلا بأئمة الهدى وخير الورى، وهم نقلوه بعد الضبط التام، ونظمه في نفسه يتعلّق معجز به الأحكام فلم يعتبر معناه، ولأنه محفوظ عن التغيير، ومصون عن التبديل، قال الله تعالى:
إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَافِظُونَ ﴾ ، فيصح نقل نظمه ممن ليست له معرفة بمعناه.
(الحجر : ٩)
وهي: أي محافظة الحدود وهي الأحكام (القمر) ومراقبته إلخ يقال: راقبه أي حرسه، ويقال: راقب إليه في أمره خافه؛ لأن الخائف يرقب العقاب ويتوقعه. (السنبلي) بمذاكرته بأن يكرّر ما حفظه باللسان لئلا يذهب من الذهن. (القمر) إلى شخص آخر كذلك أي السامع حق السماع، والفَاهِمُ المعناه المراد، والحافظ ببذل الطاقة والمحافظة عليه. (القمر) فحينئذ إلخ : أي فحين إذا أدّى إلى الشخص الآخر الكذائي (القمر) به ذمة أي بكل واحد من الحفظ والثبات والمراقبة. (المحشي) يؤدّيه أي إلى أن المحشي) يوم التناد إلخ: بتشديد الدال بمعنى يوم القيمة، ومنه يوم التنادي يقال: تنادى القوم تناديا اجتمعوا وحضروا النادي، وتجالسوا في النادي، ونادى بعضهم بعضًا. (السنبلي) وهذا أي اشتراط فهم المعنى المراد في ضبط السنن. (القمر) وهم نقلوه إلخ : فلا يتوهم وقوع الخلل بسبب نقل مَن لا ضبط له. (القمر) يتعلق به الأحكام ألا ترى أنه يحرم تلاوته على الجنب والحائض (القمر) فلم يعتبر معناه ولذا كان نقل القرآن بالمعنى حراما، ولا يمتنع الترجمة بالفارسية وغيرها، وإنما الممتنع النقل بالمعنى على أنه القرآن المجيد والكتاب الحكيم، فإنه يورث تضليلا، فإن المروي له يقع في ذهنه أنه الكلام الإلهي فحينئذٍ يقرأ في الصلاة ،فضل كذا في "الصبح الصادق". (القمر)
Section: Divisions of the Sunnah. Conditions of the Narrator: Narration after puberty; the statement of a child is accepted therein because there is no defect in his acquisition due to his being discerning, nor in his narration due to his being sane. And 'dabt' (accuracy) is listening to speech as it deserves to be heard, i.e., listening like the listening of something that deserves to be heard, meaning from its beginning to its end with complete words and syntactic structure. He said that only because often the listener comes to a preaching session after part of its beginning has passed and he missed it and the teacher did not inform him—i.e., the latecomer—because of crowding, so the teacher repeats the past speech after his attendance. Such listening is not a proof in the chapter of hadith; rather it is for blessing, just as children are brought to the preaching session for blessing. Then understanding its meaning intended, whether linguistic or legal; not restricting to memorizing words only, because it is not absolute listening but listening to sound—i.e., complete listening. Then memorizing it by exerting effort for it; the pronoun 'his' in 'memorizing it' and 'for him' refer to what is heard, and 'majhud' (effort) is infinitive. And the correct view is that it is not determined by age, but rather estimation by understanding the address and responding, and completeness of intellect also differs by persons, so a specific amount cannot be determined; so its cause is put in its place legally, like in travel and hardship, and its measure is puberty, as stated by 'Bahr al-'Ulum'. (Sunbuli) Since there is no defect in his acquisition, it is not required at the time of acquisition except intellect of discernment, because there is consensus on accepting the narrations of Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them, even though he heard them before puberty, and the narrations of Abd al-Zubayr, since his birth was after the Hijra, so his hearing and acquisition were in childhood. (Qamar) 'Being discerning': there is an indication that discernment is sufficient for acquisition according to the correct view, and it has no fixed limit, contrary to those who say the first period in which a child becomes eligible for acquisition is four years, as is said. (Qamar) [unclear: God bin with] Meaning: from its beginning etc., because understanding meaning is not possible without hearing the complete speech. (Qamar) And he said that only: i.e., he only stipulated in hearing right hearing because etc. (Qamar) Then understanding etc.: so whoever has no knowledge of the meaning of hadith and narrates only the words is not precise, and his narration is not acceptable. This is what the Hanafis adhere to, contrary to the majority. For the custom in recording the sunnah is knowledge of their meanings, because their meanings are intended, not their words. (Qamar) 'Linguistic or legal': this generality is derived from the author's not restricting the meaning. (Qamar) 'Because': i.e., memorizing words only. (Muhashi) The pronoun in 'memorizing it' and 'for him' etc.: apparently it is said that the author's phrase 'for him' is an attribute of his phrase 'the effort', and the pronoun 'him' refers to the precise narrator. (Qamar) 'Al-hifdh' (memorization): meaning effort, i.e., energy. Then memorizing that heard to the extent of human capacity. Then persistence upon it by preserving its limits, which is acting according to it with his body and guarding it by its repetition, i.e., with its rules, its repeating while being settled on thinking ill of himself by not relying on his memorizing faculty, but saying: 'If I leave it, I will forget it.' And all this until the time of his performance, i.e., until he performs it and conveys it to another person likewise, whether one or a group. At that time his responsibility is discharged before God Almighty—i.e., as it was conveyed to him—and the responsibility of another person becomes occupied with it, conveying it to another, and so on until the Day of Assembly or until the books of hadith are compiled. And this is contrary to the Qur'an, because understanding its meaning was not stipulated for its transmission; because it was established originally only by the Imams of guidance and the best of creation, and they transmitted it after complete accuracy, and its composition itself concerns miracles and rulings, so its meaning was not considered, and because it is protected from change and safeguarded from alteration. Allah says: 'Indeed, We have sent down the Reminder, and indeed We are its guardians' (15:9). So it is valid to transmit its wording from one who has no knowledge of its meaning. (9) (Qamar) 'Which are': i.e., preserving the limits, which are the rulings. (Qamar) And guarding it etc.: it is said: 'raqabahu' meaning he guarded him, and 'raqaba ilayhi fi amrihi' meaning he feared him, because the fearful person watches for punishment and expects it. (Sunbuli) 'By its repetition': by repeating what he memorized with the tongue so that it does not leave the mind. (Qamar) 'To another person likewise': i.e., the listener with right hearing and the understander of the intended meaning, and the memorizer by expending energy and preserving it. (Qamar) 'At that time' etc.: i.e., when he has conveyed to the other person of that description. (Qamar) 'By it, responsibility': i.e., by each of memorization, persistence, and guarding. (Muhashi) 'He conveys it' i.e., to. (Muhashi) 'The Day of Assembly' etc.: with shadda on the dal, meaning the Day of Resurrection; from it 'yawm al-tanadi'—it is said 'tanada al-qawm tanadiyan' meaning they gathered and attended the assembly, and they sat together in the assembly, and they called each other. (Sunbuli) 'And this': i.e., the stipulation of understanding the intended meaning in recording the sunnah. (Qamar) 'And they transmitted it' etc.: so one should not imagine that defect occurs due to transmission by one without accuracy. (Qamar) 'Connected to rulings': do you not see that it is forbidden for a junub or menstruating woman to recite it? (Qamar) So its meaning was not considered; therefore transmitting the Qur'an by meaning is forbidden. But translation into Persian and other languages is not prevented; what is prevented is transmission by meaning as being the glorious Qur'an and the wise book, because it leads to misguidance, for the recipient comes to think it is the divine speech and then recites it in prayer, etc. As in 'al-Subh al-Sadiq'. (Qamar)
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the condition of 'dabt' (accuracy) for a hadith narrator, as part of the broader discussion of narrator conditions in Hanafi usul. The text first clarifies that a child's narration is accepted after puberty, provided he was discerning at the time of hearing and sane at the time of narrating. The core of the passage defines 'dabt' as having several components: full hearing from beginning to end with complete words and structure; understanding the intended meaning (whether linguistic or legal), not merely memorizing sounds; memorization with effort; and persistence by acting upon the hadith and reviewing it constantly until it is transmitted to another. The author provides an example of a listener who arrives late to a session and hears only a repetition—such incomplete hearing is not considered valid for hadith transmission. The text then highlights a key difference between the Hanafi madhhab and others: Hanafis require the narrator to understand the meaning of the hadith, not just memorize the words. The reason is that the goal of hadith is its meaning, and mere word-for-word recitation without comprehension risks error. The passage also distinguishes hadith from the Qur'an: understanding the meaning is not required for transmitting the Qur'an because the Qur'an was transmitted by impeccable authorities, its wording itself is miraculous and contains rulings, and Allah has guaranteed its preservation. Therefore, a person who does not understand the Arabic may still transmit the Qur'anic text in its original wording, but transmitting by meaning (i.e., paraphrasing) and claiming it is the Qur'an is forbidden. This extensive treatment covers the theoretical basis for the condition of dabt and its practical implications in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): هي صفة في الراوي تقتضي سماع الكلام كاملاً، وفهم معناه، وحفظه، والثبات عليه حتى الأداء
التحمل (al-tahammul): تلقي الحديث من الشيخ بقصد الرواية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a component of dabt according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hearing the speech completely from beginning to end.
B) Understanding the intended meaning (linguistic or legal).
C) Writing the hadith in a notebook.
D) Memorizing with effort and persistent review.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of dabt comprises four components: full hearing, understanding meaning, memorization with effort, and persistent review until transmission.

The Hanafi Position on Understanding Meaning in Hadith Transmission
Explaining the Hanafi requirement of understanding meaning in dabt and the distinction from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires understanding of meaning for hadith transmission and contrast this with the Quran, and evaluate the methodological grounds of the dispute with the majority.

Core Idea
Understanding meaning is essential for hadith accuracy because meaning is the goal; for Quran, wording alone suffices due to divine protection.

This lesson focuses on the key ikhtilaf between Hanafis and the majority regarding the requirement of understanding the meaning (fahm al-ma'na) for dabt. The text provides a rational argument based on custom ('urf) and also explains why the Quran is treated differently, due to its miraculous nature and divine preservation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on understanding meaning
Find the sentence that states that a narrator who only memorizes words without knowledge of meaning is not ضابط.
The text says: 'فمن ليس له علم معنى الحديث وروى الألفاظ فقط فهو ليس بضابط وروايته ليست بمقبولة'.
2
Identify the opposing view (الأكثرون)
Note that the majority of scholars do not require understanding; they accept word-for-word memorization as sufficient.
The text explicitly says 'خلافًا للأكثرين'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
The evidence is based على العادة (custom): 'العادة في ضبط السنن علم معانيها لكون معانيها مقصودة منها دون ألفاظها'.
This is an aqli (rational) argument: the purpose of preserving hadith is to convey the meaning, so understanding is necessary.
4
Examine the exception for the Quran
The text explains why understanding is not required for Quran transmission: the Quran's transmission was done by impeccable authorities, its wording is miraculous and contains rulings, and Allah has guaranteed its preservation.
The verse (15:9) is cited: 'إنا نحن نزلنا الذكر وإنا له لحافظون'.
5
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
The consequence is that a narrator who only memorizes words without understanding is rejected by Hanafis but accepted by the majority; and for Quran, even a person who does not understand can transmit the text verbatim.
This highlights the different epistemological weight given to hadith vs. Quran in Hanafi usul.

بمعنى الجهد وهو الطاقة أي ثم حفظ ذلك المسموع بقدر الطاقة البشرية له. ثم الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده وهي العمل بموجبه ببدنه ومراقبته بمذاكرته أي مع أي أحكامه مذاكرته حال كونه مستقراً على إساءة الظن بنفسه بأن لا يعتمد على نفسه بالقوة الحافظة، بل يقول : إني إذا تركته ،نسيته، وهذا كله إلى حين أدائه أي إلى حين أن يؤديه ويبلغه إلى شخص آخر كذالك واحدًا كان أو جماعةً، فحينئذٍ تفرغ ذمته عند الله تعالى، أي كما بلغ إليه وتشتغل به ذمة إنسان آخر يؤدّيه إلى أحد، وهكذا إلى يوم التناد أو إلى أن تُؤلّف كتب الأحاديث، وهذا بخلاف القرآن؛ لأنه لم يشترط لنقله فهمه بمعناه؛ لأنه ما ثبت في الأصل إلا بأئمة الهدى وخير الورى، وهم نقلوه بعد الضبط التام، ونظمه في نفسه يتعلّق معجز به الأحكام فلم يعتبر معناه، ولأنه محفوظ عن التغيير، ومصون عن التبديل، قال الله تعالى:

(القمر)
Section: Divisions of the Sunnah. Conditions of the Narrator: Narration after puberty; the statement of a child is accepted therein because there is no defect in his acquisition due to his being discerning, nor in his narration due to his being sane. And 'dabt' (accuracy) is listening to speech as it deserves to be heard, i.e., listening like the listening of something that deserves to be heard, meaning from its beginning to its end with complete words and syntactic structure. He said that only because often the listener comes to a preaching session after part of its beginning has passed and he missed it and the teacher did not inform him—i.e., the latecomer—because of crowding, so the teacher repeats the past speech after his attendance. Such listening is not a proof in the chapter of hadith; rather it is for blessing, just as children are brought to the preaching session for blessing. Then understanding its meaning intended, whether linguistic or legal; not restricting to memorizing words only, because it is not absolute listening but listening to sound—i.e., complete listening. Then memorizing it by exerting effort for it; the pronoun 'his' in 'memorizing it' and 'for him' refer to what is heard, and 'majhud' (effort) is infinitive. And the correct view is that it is not determined by age, but rather estimation by understanding the address and responding, and completeness of intellect also differs by persons, so a specific amount cannot be determined; so its cause is put in its place legally, like in travel and hardship, and its measure is puberty, as stated by 'Bahr al-'Ulum'. (Sunbuli) Since there is no defect in his acquisition, it is not required at the time of acquisition except intellect of discernment, because there is consensus on accepting the narrations of Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them, even though he heard them before puberty, and the narrations of Abd al-Zubayr, since his birth was after the Hijra, so his hearing and acquisition were in childhood. (Qamar) 'Being discerning': there is an indication that discernment is sufficient for acquisition according to the correct view, and it has no fixed limit, contrary to those who say the first period in which a child becomes eligible for acquisition is four years, as is said. (Qamar) [unclear: God bin with] Meaning: from its beginning etc., because understanding meaning is not possible without hearing the complete speech. (Qamar) And he said that only: i.e., he only stipulated in hearing right hearing because etc. (Qamar) Then understanding etc.: so whoever has no knowledge of the meaning of hadith and narrates only the words is not precise, and his narration is not acceptable. This is what the Hanafis adhere to, contrary to the majority. For the custom in recording the sunnah is knowledge of their meanings, because their meanings are intended, not their words. (Qamar) 'Linguistic or legal': this generality is derived from the author's not restricting the meaning. (Qamar) 'Because': i.e., memorizing words only. (Muhashi) The pronoun in 'memorizing it' and 'for him' etc.: apparently it is said that the author's phrase 'for him' is an attribute of his phrase 'the effort', and the pronoun 'him' refers to the precise narrator. (Qamar) 'Al-hifdh' (memorization): meaning effort, i.e., energy. Then memorizing that heard to the extent of human capacity. Then persistence upon it by preserving its limits, which is acting according to it with his body and guarding it by its repetition, i.e., with its rules, its repeating while being settled on thinking ill of himself by not relying on his memorizing faculty, but saying: 'If I leave it, I will forget it.' And all this until the time of his performance, i.e., until he performs it and conveys it to another person likewise, whether one or a group. At that time his responsibility is discharged before God Almighty—i.e., as it was conveyed to him—and the responsibility of another person becomes occupied with it, conveying it to another, and so on until the Day of Assembly or until the books of hadith are compiled. And this is contrary to the Qur'an, because understanding its meaning was not stipulated for its transmission; because it was established originally only by the Imams of guidance and the best of creation, and they transmitted it after complete accuracy, and its composition itself concerns miracles and rulings, so its meaning was not considered, and because it is protected from change and safeguarded from alteration. Allah says: 'Indeed, We have sent down the Reminder, and indeed We are its guardians' (15:9). So it is valid to transmit its wording from one who has no knowledge of its meaning. (9) (Qamar) 'Which are': i.e., preserving the limits, which are the rulings. (Qamar) And guarding it etc.: it is said: 'raqabahu' meaning he guarded him, and 'raqaba ilayhi fi amrihi' meaning he feared him, because the fearful person watches for punishment and expects it. (Sunbuli) 'By its repetition': by repeating what he memorized with the tongue so that it does not leave the mind. (Qamar) 'To another person likewise': i.e., the listener with right hearing and the understander of the intended meaning, and the memorizer by expending energy and preserving it. (Qamar) 'At that time' etc.: i.e., when he has conveyed to the other person of that description. (Qamar) 'By it, responsibility': i.e., by each of memorization, persistence, and guarding. (Muhashi) 'He conveys it' i.e., to. (Muhashi) 'The Day of Assembly' etc.: with shadda on the dal, meaning the Day of Resurrection; from it 'yawm al-tanadi'—it is said 'tanada al-qawm tanadiyan' meaning they gathered and attended the assembly, and they sat together in the assembly, and they called each other. (Sunbuli) 'And this': i.e., the stipulation of understanding the intended meaning in recording the sunnah. (Qamar) 'And they transmitted it' etc.: so one should not imagine that defect occurs due to transmission by one without accuracy. (Qamar) 'Connected to rulings': do you not see that it is forbidden for a junub or menstruating woman to recite it? (Qamar) So its meaning was not considered; therefore transmitting the Qur'an by meaning is forbidden. But translation into Persian and other languages is not prevented; what is prevented is transmission by meaning as being the glorious Qur'an and the wise book, because it leads to misguidance, for the recipient comes to think it is the divine speech and then recites it in prayer, etc. As in 'al-Subh al-Sadiq'. (Qamar)
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the condition of 'dabt' (accuracy) for a hadith narrator, as part of the broader discussion of narrator conditions in Hanafi usul. The text first clarifies that a child's narration is accepted after puberty, provided he was discerning at the time of hearing and sane at the time of narrating. The core of the passage defines 'dabt' as having several components: full hearing from beginning to end with complete words and structure; understanding the intended meaning (whether linguistic or legal), not merely memorizing sounds; memorization with effort; and persistence by acting upon the hadith and reviewing it constantly until it is transmitted to another. The author provides an example of a listener who arrives late to a session and hears only a repetition—such incomplete hearing is not considered valid for hadith transmission. The text then highlights a key difference between the Hanafi madhhab and others: Hanafis require the narrator to understand the meaning of the hadith, not just memorize the words. The reason is that the goal of hadith is its meaning, and mere word-for-word recitation without comprehension risks error. The passage also distinguishes hadith from the Qur'an: understanding the meaning is not required for transmitting the Qur'an because the Qur'an was transmitted by impeccable authorities, its wording itself is miraculous and contains rulings, and Allah has guaranteed its preservation. Therefore, a person who does not understand the Arabic may still transmit the Qur'anic text in its original wording, but transmitting by meaning (i.e., paraphrasing) and claiming it is the Qur'an is forbidden. This extensive treatment covers the theoretical basis for the condition of dabt and its practical implications in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): هي صفة في الراوي تقتضي سماع الكلام كاملاً، وفهم معناه، وحفظه، والثبات عليه حتى الأداء
التحمل (al-tahammul): تلقي الحديث من الشيخ بقصد الرواية
العادة (al-'adah): العرف أو العادة المستمرة التي تعتبر دليلاً في استنباط الأحكام

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely requires understanding of meaning as part of dabt, based on custom, while the Quran is exempted due to divine protection and miraculous nature of its wording.

Condition of Memory (Hifdh) for Hadith Narration
Defines and explains the condition of memory for narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi requirement of memory (hifdh) for hadith narrators from the transmission of the Quran, applying the dalil of divine preservation.

Core Idea
Hadith transmission requires memory with understanding; Quran transmission does not, because Allah guarantees its preservation.

In this lesson, we examine the condition of memory (hifdh) for a hadith narrator as defined in Hanafi usul. The text explains that hifdh involves effort, steadfastness, and review until transmission. Significantly, it contrasts hadith with the Quran, where understanding is not required due to divine protection. This distinction affects how we evaluate narrators and the transmission of sacred texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the element being expanded
The passage expands on the condition of memory (hifdh) for a hadith narrator. Note that it is part of the conditions for accepting a narration.
2
Deconstruct the definition of hifdh
Break down the components: effort (energy), steadfastness, safeguarding limits (acting upon hadith), monitoring by reviewing, and continuance until delivery. Understand that memory is not mere retention but includes conscious maintenance.
The passage emphasizes that the narrator should think ill of his own memory, not rely solely on it.
3
Identify the contrast with Quran
The passage explicitly contrasts hadith with the Quran: for Quran, understanding of meaning is not a condition for transmission. Identify the reason given: divine preservation (Quran 15:9).
4
Analyze the dalil
Examine the Quranic verse: 'Indeed, We have sent down the Reminder, and indeed, We will be its guardian.' Note its certainty (qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala) and how it provides a specific exemption for the Quran.
This verse is cited as proof that the Quran does not require human memory conditions like hadith.
5
Note practical consequences
Since Quran transmission does not require understanding, a narrator who merely memorizes the wording can transmit it. For hadith, understanding is required; otherwise, the narrator is deficient.
This difference stems from the nature of the texts: the Quran is divinely protected, while hadith relies on human preservation.

والمحافظة عليه. (القمر) فحينئذ إلخ : أي فحين إذا أدّى إلى الشخص الآخر الكذائي (القمر)
به ذمة أي بكل واحد من الحفظ والثبات والمراقبة. (المحشي) يؤدّيه أي إلى أن المحشي)
يوم
التناد إلخ: بتشديد الدال بمعنى يوم القيمة، ومنه يوم التنادي يقال: تنادى القوم تناديا اجتمعوا وحضروا النادي، وتجالسوا في النادي، ونادى بعضهم بعضًا. (السنبلي) وهذا أي اشتراط فهم المعنى المراد في ضبط السنن. (القمر)
وهم نقلوه إلخ : فلا يتوهم وقوع الخلل بسبب نقل مَن لا ضبط له. (القمر)
يتعلق به الأحكام ألا ترى أنه يحرم تلاوته على الجنب والحائض (القمر)
فلم يعتبر معناه ولذا كان نقل القرآن بالمعنى حراما، ولا يمتنع الترجمة بالفارسية وغيرها، وإنما الممتنع النقل بالمعنى على أنه القرآن المجيد والكتاب الحكيم، فإنه يورث تضليلا، فإن المروي له يقع في ذهنه أنه الكلام الإلهي فحينئذٍ يقرأ في الصلاة ،فضل كذا في "الصبح الصادق". (القمر)
Chapter on Divisions of Sunnah. Conditions of the Narrator: Memory (hifdh). By meaning effort, i.e., capacity: then he preserves what he heard to the extent of human capacity. Then steadfastness upon it by safeguarding its limits, which are acting according to it with his body, and monitoring it by reviewing it, i.e., with any of its rulings reviewing it while being settled on thinking ill of himself, not relying on his own memory, but saying: if I leave it, I forget it. And all this until the time of his delivery, i.e., until he delivers it and conveys it to another person likewise, whether one or a group. Then his responsibility is discharged before Allah, the Exalted, just as he conveyed it. And another person's responsibility becomes occupied with it, and he delivers it to someone else, and so on until the Day of Summoning or until hadith books are compiled. This is different from the Quran, because understanding its meaning was not stipulated for its transmission, because it was established originally only by the Imams of guidance and the best of mankind, and they transmitted it after complete preservation. Its very composition is connected to miracles by which rulings are derived, so its meaning was not considered; and because it is preserved from alteration and protected from change. Allah the Exalted said, 'Indeed, We have sent down the Reminder, and indeed, We will be its guardian' (al-Hijr: 9). So it is valid to transmit its wording from someone who does not have knowledge of its meaning. [Commentary:] 'And it' i.e., safeguarding the limits which are the rulings (al-Qamar). 'And monitoring it' etc. It is said: raqabahu meaning he guarded it, and it is said: raqaba ilayhi fi amrihi khafahu because the fearful person watches for punishment and expects it (al-Sunbuli). 'By reviewing it' means by repeating what he memorized with his tongue so it does not leave his mind (al-Qamar). 'To another person likewise' i.e., the listener who hears properly and understands the intended meaning, and the preserver who exerts effort and preserves it (al-Qamar). 'Then at that time' etc. i.e., at the time he delivers to that other person (al-Qamar). 'His responsibility' i.e., by each of memory, steadfastness, and monitoring (al-Muhashi). 'He delivers it' i.e., until (al-Muhashi). 'Day of Summoning' etc. with shaddah on the dal, meaning the Day of Resurrection; from it is 'yawm al-tanadi'; it is said: tanada al-qawm tanadiyan, they gathered and attended the gathering, and they sat in the gathering, and they called one another (al-Sunbuli). 'And this' i.e., the stipulation of understanding the intended meaning in recording the Sunnah (al-Qamar). 'And they transmitted it' etc. So do not imagine corruption occurring due to transmission from one without preservation (al-Qamar). 'Rulings are attached to it' do you not see that it is forbidden for the junub and menstruating woman to recite it (al-Qamar). 'So its meaning was not considered' and hence transmission of the Quran by meaning is forbidden, but translation into Persian and other languages is not forbidden; the forbidden is transmission by meaning as if it were the glorious Quran and the wise book, for it causes misguidance, because the recipient thinks it is divine speech and then recites it in prayer, etc. as in al-Subh al-Sadiq (al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the condition of memory (hifdh) for a hadith narrator. It explains that memory requires effort and steadfastness, and the narrator must review what he has memorized and maintain it until he transmits it to another. A key point is that the narrator must understand the meaning of what he transmits—this is required for hadith but not for the Quran. The Quran is protected by divine guarantee (verse 15:9), so even someone without understanding of its meaning can transmit its wording. However, transmitting the Quran by meaning is forbidden. The passage includes commentary from various scholars like al-Qamar and al-Sunbuli clarifying terms such as 'monitoring' and 'reviewing'.

Key Terms
الحفظ (al-hifdh): Memory with effort and steadfastness, including understanding and maintaining until delivery.
المراقبة (al-muraqabah): Monitoring by reviewing one's memory and fearing loss of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Quran is longer and harder to understand.
B) Because the Quran is divinely protected from alteration, so even a non-expert can transmit its wording.
C) Because hadith scholars are more strict.
D) Because the Quran was revealed in a single dialect.

Key Takeaway
Hadith transmission requires memory with understanding; Quran transmission does not, due to divine protection.

Deficient 'Adalah: Definition and Scope in Hanafi Usul
Defines deficient 'adalah and applies it to testimony vs. narration with evidence from major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define deficient 'adalah (al-‘adālah al-qāṣirah), explain why it suffices for testimony but not for hadith narration, and identify the Hanafi proof from the hadith of destructive sins.

Core Idea
Deficient 'adalah is sufficient for worldly testimony but too weak for preserving the Sunnah.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between complete and deficient 'adalah. While any Muslim of sound intellect is presumed trustworthy for most legal purposes, narrating hadith demands a higher standard because the soul's desire may lead to falsehood. This lesson unpacks the concept of deficient 'adalah, its justification, and its practical implications, drawing on the hadith of the seven destructive sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of deficient 'adalah
From the text, extract the two components: apparent Islam (zāhir al-islām) and sound intellect (i‘tidāl al-‘aql). This is the basis of deficient 'adalah.
The text calls it 'al-‘adālah al-qāṣirah'.
2
Understand the rationale for rejecting it in hadith
The apparent reliability is opposed by another apparent, namely the soul's desire (hawā al-nafs). This creates doubt, so narration is rejected.
The text says: 'hādhā al-zāhir yu‘āriḍuhu zāhir ākhar, wa huwa hawā al-nafs'.
3
Apply the distinction to testimony vs. narration
Deficient 'adalah suffices for testimony (shahāda) to avoid stagnation of worldly affairs. For hadith narration (riwāya), complete 'adalah is needed to preserve the religion.
The reason provided: 'law i‘tubirat al-‘adālah al-kāmilah la-afḍā ilā ta‘ṭīl al-maṣāliḥ al-dunyawīyah'.
4
Locate the evidence for major sins that remove 'adalah
The hadith of Abu Hurayra lists seven destructive sins (al-mūbiqāt). These are examples of acts that compromise 'adalah.
The hadith is aḥad, but its thubūt is qaṭ‘ī (Bukhari/Muslim); its dalāla is ẓannī.
5
Recognize the ikhtilāf regarding sufficiency
The Hanafi position is that deficient 'adalah is not enough for hadith; the opposing school (implicitly Shafi‘i) may hold otherwise. The practical difference (thamarah) is that a narrator with weak 'adalah might have testimony accepted but hadith rejected.
The text implies this dispute; the Hanafi response is stricter for hadith.

Source Text
